# Gap analysis ‚Äî catalogs vs PromptZero Specs

Synthesises the four researcher catalogs (`firmware.md`, `apps.md`,
`attacks.md`, `hardware.md`) against the current Spec inventory and the
existing v0.8 roadmap (`docs/refactor/v0.8-team-audit.md`). Goal: surface
**what the prior audit missed**, not re-list what it already covered.

## Inputs (snapshot 2026-04-25)

| Source | Lines | Inventory |
|---|---|---|
| `docs/catalog/firmware.md` | 748 | 11 firmwares |
| `docs/catalog/apps.md` | 470 | 233 apps surveyed; ~190 with hw primitives |
| `docs/catalog/attacks.md` | 614 | 34 attack entries (2024-2026) |
| `docs/catalog/hardware.md` | 338 | 38 hardware entries |
| `docs/refactor/v0.8-team-audit.md` | 257 | existing roadmap (the floor) |
| `internal/tools/` registry | ‚Äî | **230 Spec `Name:` registrations / 221 unique** (verified by `grep -rohE 'Name:\s+"[a-z0-9_]+"' --exclude="*_test.go" \| sort -u`) |

## Headline finding

The v0.8 audit covers the **strategic surface** (Phase 1 architecture,
Phase 2 capability themes) very well. The four researcher catalogs
broaden the picture in exactly two ways:

1. **Tactical Spec gaps** the audit didn't enumerate ‚Äî defensive
   classifiers, forensic-side decoders, and a handful of widely-shipped
   Flipper apps (NFC relay, MagSpoof, Sentry Safe, POCSAG, AVR ICSP /
   SWD).
2. **Two net-new hardware backends** beyond audit ¬ß2c ‚Äî
   **Proxmark3 (Iceman)** and **CatSniffer V3 / Sniffle dongle**.

That is the entire delta. **Diminishing returns set in fast.** Below ~30
items the new findings tail off into stuff already implied by the audit
or out-of-scope by policy. The "Top-30" list at ¬ß3 is therefore the
honest ceiling, not a quota.

One **factual correction to a researcher claim**: `firmware.md` ¬ß4.2
lists `subghz_chat` as missing. It is **already a Spec**
(`internal/tools/subghz.go:123`). Treat that as a stale finding; the
remaining four firmware-catalog gaps stand.

The **Cuyler36** entry from the original task #7 spec was confirmed
**not a Flipper firmware** by the firmware researcher (their ¬ß2.11). It
**does not appear in `docs/refactor/v0.8-team-audit.md`** ‚Äî the typo
lives only in the task system / earlier draft notes, so no patch to the
audit is required. Recommendation: drop it from any future spec drafts;
no PromptZero detection branch should be added.

---

## 1. Coverage matrix

Every primitive identified in the four catalogs as a row. Columns:

- **Native** ‚Äî Spec exists today in `internal/tools/`
- **Container-bridge** ‚Äî wraps a containerised tool (mfoc/mfcuk/hashcat
  pattern) ‚Äî counts as covered if the bridge is wired
- **Federation** ‚Äî reachable via `mcpfed` prefix (e.g. `pm3.*`,
  `secsec.*`)
- **Gap** ‚Äî not covered by any of the above today

‚úÖ = present ¬∑ ‚öÝÔ∏è = partial / variant ¬∑ ‚ùå = missing.
"¬ß2a"/"¬ß2b"/"¬ß2c" cells reference the corresponding row in the v0.8
audit (`docs/refactor/v0.8-team-audit.md`).

| Mifare hardnested host-bridge | attacks + audit Q2 | ‚öÝÔ∏è `mifare_hardnested_host` (bridge) | ‚úÖ | ‚úÖ | ‚Äî |

| ISO15693-3 writer | firmware ¬ß4.2 #4 | ‚ùå | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | **NEW** small gap |
| EMV parse (visa/mc) | firmware ¬ß4.2 #3 | ‚úÖ `nfc_emv_decode` (+ `nfc_emv_encode`) ‚Äî BER-TLV walker + ~80-tag dictionary; `nfc_emv_track2_decode` v0.414 cracks tag 57 (PAN/expiry/service code, Luhn-gated); `nfc_emv_dol_decode` v0.415 walks PDOL/CDOL/DDOL/TDOL (tag,length) lists; `nfc_emv_afl_decode` v0.416 expands tag 94 (SFI/record ranges ‚Üí READ RECORD list); `nfc_emv_cvm_decode` v0.426 cracks tag 8E (X/Y amounts + CVM method/condition rules) | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | shipped ‚Äî BER-TLV + Track-2 + DOL + AFL + CVM-List field decode. | UHF EPC Gen2 (M6E-Nano) | apps `uhf_rfid` | ‚öÝÔ∏è | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | Adjacent-HW gap for *reading*; **offline EPC *decode* shipped v0.468.0 (`epc_decode`, SGTIN-96)** |
| Mag-stripe wireless emulation (MagSpoof) | apps top-20 #9 | ‚öÝÔ∏è partial | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | offline half ‚úÖ `magstripe_decode` (v0.453 ‚Äî ISO 7813 Track 1/2 ASCII swipe parser); the wireless-coil TX emulation remains a hardware loader step |

---

## 2. De-duplication ‚Äî gaps already covered by v0.8 audit

These are **already in `docs/refactor/v0.8-team-audit.md`** and are *not*
re-listed in the prioritised gap section below. References use the
audit's own ¬ß2a/¬ß2b/¬ß2c/¬ß2d/Q-numbers for cross-link. The catalogs
*confirm* every one of them ‚Äî none of the audit's Phase 2 picks looks
weakened on second pass.

| Spec / item | Audit anchor | Catalog confirmation |
|---|---|---|
| `mifare_fm11rf08_backdoor` | ¬ß2a row 1 | attacks #2 (Quarkslab Aug 2024 ‚Äî confirmed strongest) |
| `nfc_unsaflok_forge` | ¬ß2a row 2 | attacks #3 + apps top-20 #5 |
| `subghz_rollback_detect` | ¬ß2a row 3 + Q5 | attacks #5 + firmware ¬ß2.12 (adversarial CFW) |

## 3. Prioritised gap list ‚Äî top 30 missing capabilities

Scoring: `prevalence √ó adversarial-leverage / effort`. Effort tags:
**S** ‚â§ 1 week ¬∑ **M** 1-3 weeks ¬∑ **L** 3+ weeks ¬∑ **XL** ‚â• 2 months.
Items already in the audit (¬ß2 above) are excluded ‚Äî this list is the
**delta** the audit missed.

### Honourable mentions (rank 31-40)

Below the line ‚Äî small gaps, niche surfaces, or duplicates of items
above pending evidence:

- `nfc_amiibo_clone` (RM `amiibo_toolkit`)
- `nfc_dicts_manager` (already covered by `corpora` Spec ‚Äî keep as is)
- `dcf77_clock_spoof` (LF time-signal synth) ‚Äî ‚öÝÔ∏è telegram-synth shipped v0.375 (`dcf77_synth`: offline 60-bit minute-telegram generator, BCD + even parity, round-trip-verified against `dcf77_decode`). The long-wave TX stage (actual spoof transmission) remains a separate loader step.
- `ipv6_eui64_recover` (IPv6 ‚Üí MAC deanonymisation) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.424 ‚Äî recover the hardware MAC embedded in an IPv6 Modified-EUI-64 interface identifier (detect the FF:FE marker, strip it, flip the U/L bit). The offline complement to `ndp_decode` / `dhcpv6_decode` (which surface IPv6 addresses); chains the recovered MAC into `mac_classify` so a MAC-derived SLAAC address is deanonymised and a randomized one is flagged. Observation-framed (privacy/RFC-7217 IIDs carry no marker), no hardware (`internal/macaddr`).
- `hash_identify` AD-roasting coverage ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.434 extended the existing hash-format identifier with the Active Directory roasting loot: Kerberos TGS-REP (`$krb5tgs$`, Kerberoast ‚Üí hashcat 13100/19600/19700), AS-REP (`$krb5asrep$` ‚Üí 18200), AS-REQ pre-auth (`$krb5pa$` ‚Üí 7500), DCC2/mscash2 (`$DCC2$` ‚Üí 2100), and NetNTLMv1/v2 (the `user::domain:‚Ä¶` Responder format ‚Üí 5500/5600). Definitive `$`-prefixes (no confidently-wrong); the colon-prefix strip now skips `$`-structured and `::` NetNTLM hashes so they reach the identifier intact. Ties to `kerberos_decode`. v0.435 added WPA hashcat-22000 lines (`WPA*01*` PMKID / `WPA*02*` EAPOL ‚Äî closing the coherence gap with `wifi_pmkid_hc22000`, which emits them) and Cisco-IOS type 8 (`$8$` ‚Üí 9200) / type 9 (`$9$` ‚Üí 9300) (`internal/tools/security.go`).
- Werkzeug **scrypt** (`scrypt:N:r:p$‚Ä¶`) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.459 extended `internal/webpass` (and so `pbkdf2_password` verify/compute + the `hash_crack` `werkzeug` mode) to cover Werkzeug's **modern default** password hash (Werkzeug ‚â•2.3 / current Flask), closing the scrypt deferral noted when pbkdf2_password shipped (v0.457). The `werkzeug` cracker now auto-detects pbkdf2 vs scrypt; compute via `scheme=werkzeug-scrypt` (N/r/p). `Wrap-vs-native: wrap` ‚Äî `golang.org/x/crypto/scrypt` (already a dep; native port infeasible), with a 1 GiB memory-cost cap against hostile N/r and our own `scrypt:N:r:p$salt$hex` framing. Verified byte-for-byte against the reference Werkzeug library + Go's x/crypto/scrypt. No new tool. (`internal/webpass`)
- `phpass_password` (WordPress $P$ / phpBB $H$) + `hash_crack` phpass ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.458 ‚Äî the phpass portable-hash format used by **WordPress** (the most-deployed CMS) and phpBB3 ‚Äî among the most common user-DB offline-crack targets (hashcat 400). Compute or verify (constant-time), and `hash_crack_dictionary` gained a `phpass` dictionary mode so a dumped wp_users table can be cracked directly. Iterated MD5 finished with phpass's own base64; reuses the crypt `itoa64` alphabet. A hostile embedded cost (> 2^24 rounds) is rejected rather than allowed to hang. Verified byte-for-byte against the reference **passlib** library (an independent oracle) ‚Äî `Compute` reproduces the passlib hash exactly; fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî `crypto/md5`, stdlib only (`internal/phpass`).
- `pbkdf2_password` (Django / Werkzeug PBKDF2 password hashes) + `hash_crack` django/werkzeug ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.457 ‚Äî the user-credential format in a **Python web-app database dump** (Django `pbkdf2_sha256$‚Ä¶`, Werkzeug/Flask `pbkdf2:sha256:‚Ä¶`) ‚Äî a top offline-crack target the toolkit couldn't previously handle. Compute or verify (framework auto-detected, constant-time, sha256/sha1/sha512), and `hash_crack_dictionary` gained `django`/`werkzeug` dictionary modes (high-iteration ‚Üí workers capped) so a dumped user table can be cracked directly. Reuses the generic `internal/wpa.PBKDF2`. Verified against reference **Django and Werkzeug** library output (an independent oracle) + raw `hashlib.pbkdf2_hmac`; fuzz-clean. Offline, no hardware (`internal/webpass`).
- `flask_session` (Flask/itsdangerous session cookie decode / verify / forge) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.456 ‚Äî the **web-pentest analogue of the JWT trio** for Flask, the most common Python web framework. A Flask session is signed-not-encrypted, so **decode** reads the payload with no key; **verify** tests a candidate `SECRET_KEY` or a list (the **flask-unsign weak-key attack** ‚Äî a top web finding, parallel to the JWT weak-secret test); **forge** mints a validly-signed cookie (e.g. `{"admin":true}`) for an authorized test. Handles itsdangerous's HMAC-SHA1 signing, the `HMAC-SHA1(SECRET_KEY, "cookie-session")` key derivation, the 2011 timestamp epoch, and transparent zlib payload inflation. **Verified byte-for-byte against the reference itsdangerous library** (an independent oracle via a venv) ‚Äî decode/verify against itsdangerous-produced cookies (compressed + uncompressed) and `Sign` reproduces an itsdangerous cookie exactly; fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî HMAC-SHA1 + base64url + zlib, stdlib only (`internal/flasksession`).
- `aprs_packet_decode` Mic-E decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.490.0 ‚Äî decoded **Mic-E** (Microphone Encoder, APRS101 ¬ß10), the single most-used APRS position format (the great majority of trackers + mobile radios: Kenwood TM-D700/D710, Yaesu FTM, the original Mic-Encoder), previously listed deferred as "~150 LoC of bit-twiddling". Mic-E packs latitude + the A/B/C message bits + N/S + longitude-offset + W/E into the **6-char AX.25 destination address**, and longitude + speed + course + symbol into the **information field** (data-type IDs `` ` `` current / `'` old GPS + the 0x1c/0x1d beta IDs). Decodes `latitude_deg` / `longitude_deg`, `speed_knots`, `course_deg`, the 15 standard/custom/emergency `message_type`s, symbol, latitude `ambiguity`, and surfaces trailing status text raw. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the two APRS101 ¬ß10 worked examples** (destination `S32U6T` ‚Üí 33¬∞25.64'N / M3 Returning; info field `` `(_fn"Oj/ `` ‚Üí 112¬∞7.74'W / 20 kt / 251¬∞), both re-extracted from the spec via the pypdf venv-oracle ‚Äî and the canonical modular speed/course formula (`speed=sp*10+dc/10`, `course=(dc%10)*100+se`, with the ‚àí800/‚àí400 wraps) reproduces the example exactly (820‚Üí20, 651‚Üí251). The destination-decode tables (`0-9`/`A-J`/`K`/`L`/`P-Y`/`Z` ‚Üí digit/blank/std-vs-custom bit; bytes 4-6 high-group ‚Üí North/+100/West) are transcribed verbatim from the ¬ß10 encoding table. A test-caught transcription slip (a stray space in the info-field vector) was fixed before shipping ‚Äî verification working as intended. Mic-E telemetry channels are surfaced as part of the raw status text rather than parsed. Fuzz-clean (~12.1M execs, 0 crashes) incl. the Mic-E seeds. No new tool ‚Äî extends `aprs_packet_decode` (`internal/aprs`); registry unchanged.
- `aprs_packet_decode` complete weather report ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.489.0 ‚Äî the noted v0.488 follow-up, completing APRS101 ¬ß12: a **position report (with or without timestamp) whose symbol code is `_`** carries weather data in place of a free-text comment. Per the spec, the 7-byte **`ddd/sss` Wind Direction/Speed Data Extension replaces the positionless `cccc/ssss` fields** (the gotcha ‚Äî wind here uses the position course/speed encoding, not `c.../s...`), after which gust / temperature / optional fields follow identically ‚Äî so the shared "gust-onward" tail was factored out of the v0.488 parser and reused. Re-extracted the authoritative APRS101 ¬ß12 complete-weather pages (pypdf venv-oracle) for the two canonical examples ‚Äî `!4903.50N/07201.75W_220/004g005t077r000p000P000h50b09900wRSW` and the timestamped `@092345z‚Ä¶W_220/004g005t-07‚Ä¶` ‚Äî and anchored the tests on both. **Gated on the `ddd/sss` pattern** so a plain `_`-symbol position carrying a free-text comment is NOT mis-parsed as weather (verified by a dedicated gate test; the weather data also never leaks into `comment`). Fuzz-clean (~12.3M execs, 0 crashes) incl. the new complete-weather seeds. No new tool ‚Äî extends `aprs_packet_decode` (`internal/aprs`); registry unchanged. The compressed-lat/lon complete weather report remains deferred with the rest of the base-91 compressed-position format.
- `aprs_packet_decode` positionless weather report ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.488.0 ‚Äî re-surveyed off the credential vein into the project's **ham-RF domain**: decoded the APRS positionless weather report (`_` data-type identifier, APRS101 ¬ß12), previously dispatched-but-deferred ("deferred until real captures surface"). Pulled the authoritative APRS101.pdf ¬ß12 via the venv-oracle technique (pypdf) ‚Äî including the canonical worked example `_10090556c220s004g005t077r000p000P000h50b09900wRSW` ‚Äî so the decode is spec-anchored, not memory. Decodes the 8-char MDHM timestamp + the fully-specified fields: wind direction (c), sustained wind speed (s), gust (g), temperature (t, incl. the ‚àí01..‚àí99 below-zero form), rainfall last hour / 24 h / since midnight (r/p/P, hundredths-inch ‚Üí inches), humidity (h, 00 = 100%), barometric pressure (b, tenths-hPa ‚Üí hPa) and luminosity (L ‚â§ 999 / l ‚â• 1000 W/m¬≤). The **`s` wind-speed-vs-snowfall ambiguity is resolved by the spec's fixed mandatory-head order** (wind dir ‚Üí speed ‚Üí gust ‚Üí temp), so the leading `s` is unambiguously wind speed; an absent sensor (`...`/spaces) decodes to a **null field, not a zero**; and the under-specified tail (snowfall, `#` raw counter, software/WX-unit trailer) is surfaced raw rather than guessed (no confidently-wrong output). Added the package's first **fuzz harness ‚Äî which immediately caught a liveness bug** I'd introduced (a recognised field code with a too-short value, e.g. `L3`, spun the optional-field loop forever); fixed with a no-progress‚Üíraw guard, the failing input locked in as a corpus regression seed, then fuzz-clean (~12.7M execs, 0 crashes). Verified against the spec's canonical example + non-zero/negative-temp/100%-humidity/unknown-sensor/luminosity cases. No new tool ‚Äî extends `aprs_packet_decode` (`internal/aprs`); registry unchanged. The complete weather report (weather appended to a position report whose symbol code is `_`) is the noted follow-up.
- `snowflake_decode` (Snowflake-ID decoder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.520.0 ‚Äî the **integer / social-media-OSINT counterpart** to the string identifier decoders (`uuid_decode` / `objectid_decode` / `ulid_decode`). A Snowflake is the 64-bit ID used by Discord, Twitter/X, Instagram and others; it packs a 41-bit millisecond timestamp (from a platform-specific epoch) in its high bits, then machine/worker + sequence bits. Decoding one is a **standard OSINT technique**: a Discord user / message / channel / guild ID, or a tweet / X-post ID, reveals exactly **when the object was created** (account age, message timing, enumeration). Because a bare Snowflake does not identify its platform ‚Äî and the same integer yields a different timestamp under each epoch ‚Äî the decoder reports a **labelled candidate per platform** (Discord, epoch 2015-01-01; Twitter/X, epoch 2010-11-04) and **asserts none** (no confidently-wrong single answer); a `platform` filter narrows to one. Each candidate gives the UTC timestamp + unix-ms + the low-bit fields (Discord: worker/process/increment; Twitter/X: machine-id/sequence). Native ‚Äî a shift + add + masks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored to Discord's own documented example**: `175928847299117063` ‚Üí 2016-04-30T11:18:25.796Z (worker 1, process 0, increment 7); Twitter/X arithmetic cross-checked. Instagram and other Snowflake variants use a different bit layout and are deliberately not decoded (a wrong field split would be confidently-wrong). Non-numeric / out-of-uint64 input rejected; fuzz-clean. **This completes the identifier info-leak family**: UUID (v1/v6/v7) + MongoDB ObjectId + ULID + Snowflake ‚Äî all the major timestamp-bearing ID formats. `internal/snowflake`. Registry 538‚Üí539.
- `ulid_decode` (ULID decoder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.519.0 ‚Äî **completes the identifier-timestamp triad** with `uuid_decode` (v0.517) and `objectid_decode` (v0.518). A ULID (Universally Unique Lexicographically Sortable Identifier) is a 26-character Crockford-base32 string encoding 128 bits ‚Äî a 48-bit millisecond Unix timestamp + 80 bits of randomness ‚Äî widely used by modern backends as a sortable, UUID-sized identifier (the spec's answer to UUIDv4, a peer of UUIDv7). Like a UUIDv1/v7 or a MongoDB ObjectId it is **not opaque**: it leaks the creation time of whatever it identifies (tokens, URLs, API params, logs, DB keys), and its lexicographic sortability aids record enumeration. Returns the timestamp (UTC + unix ms) and the 80-bit randomness (hex). Input must be exactly 26 Crockford-base32 chars (case-insensitive; no I/L/O/U) with the first char 0-7 (a larger first char overflows 128 bits ‚Äî the spec's max is `7ZZ‚Ä¶`); anything else is rejected. Native ‚Äî Crockford base-32 decode (via `math/big` for the 128-bit value) + a uint48 read, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored to python-ulid AND a hand-verified Crockford decode**: `01ARZ3NDEKTSV4RRFFQ69G5FAV` ‚Üí 1469922850259 ms / 2016-07-30T23:54:10.259Z / randomness `d6764c61efb99302bd5b` (I manually Crockford-decoded the first ten chars to confirm 1469922850259, settling a mis-recalled spec value; a test-vector boundary mis-split was caught by the test before shipping). All-zero ULID ‚Üí epoch; fuzz-clean. `internal/ulid`. Registry 537‚Üí538.
- `objectid_decode` (MongoDB ObjectId decoder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.518.0 ‚Äî the **MongoDB analogue of `uuid_decode`** and the completion of the opaque-hex ObjectId rendering in `mongodb_decode` / `bson_decode`. A 12-byte ObjectId is the default `_id` of every MongoDB document and is not opaque ‚Äî its first 4 bytes are the Unix-second creation time ‚Äî and ObjectIds leak into URLs, REST API parameters, logs, and exported documents, so a captured ObjectId reveals **when its record was created** (and the trailing 3-byte counter supports record-enumeration / timing inference). Returns the timestamp (UTC + unix seconds), the 5-byte per-process random value (hex), and the 3-byte counter (int). The legacy pre-3.4 machine-id/process-id split of the middle bytes is deprecated and deliberately **not asserted** (it would be a confidently-wrong reading on a modern ObjectId ‚Äî surfaced raw instead). Accepts a bare 24-hex string or an `ObjectId("‚Ä¶")` / quoted wrapper; a non-24-hex string is rejected. Native ‚Äî BSON-spec field extraction (a 4-byte big-endian uint32 read), stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored to pymongo `ObjectId.generation_time`**: `507f1f77bcf86cd799439011` ‚Üí 2012-10-17T21:13:27Z, `65a1b2c3d4e5f60718293a4b` ‚Üí 2024-01-12T21:44:35Z, the all-zero ObjectId ‚Üí 1970-01-01T00:00:00Z (a test-vector mis-slice in the random/counter expectation was caught by the test before shipping ‚Äî verification working as intended). Fuzz-clean. `internal/objectid`. Registry 536‚Üí537.
- `uuid_decode` (UUID/GUID structure + info-leak decoder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.517.0 ‚Äî a **recon primitive**, not just a parser: UUIDs appear in tokens, API responses, email Message-IDs, filenames, DB keys and session IDs, and some versions are not opaque. **v1/v6** (time-based) embed the **generating host's MAC address** + the **creation timestamp** ‚Äî the classic `UUIDv1 leaks the MAC + time` info-disclosure finding ‚Äî so a captured v1 UUID deanonymizes the minting host; **v7** embeds a millisecond creation timestamp (record time-ordering / enumeration); **v3/v5** (name-hash) and **v4** (random) carry no recoverable data and say so (never guessed). Reports version + variant (RFC 4122/9562 / NCS / Microsoft GUID / future), the v1/v6 timestamp (UTC) + node-as-MAC + a `node_is_mac` assessment **gated on the IEEE multicast bit** (a randomized node is never reported as a hardware MAC), the clock sequence, and recognises the nil/max UUIDs. Accepts dashed / bare-hex / `urn:uuid:` / `{braced}` forms. Native ‚Äî RFC 9562 bit-layout extraction + a gregorian‚Üíunix epoch shift, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (Go has no UUID type; distinct from `bluetooth_gatt_uuid_lookup`, which is BT GATT service UUIDs). **Anchored to Python's reference `uuid` module**: the v1 example ‚Üí version 1, node 00:11:24:44:be:1e, 2006-06-10T10:48:31.013993Z, clock-seq 15642; the v7 example ‚Üí 2022-02-22T19:22:22Z (unix-ms 1645557742000); v3/v4/v5 versions; nil UUID. v6 (which the reference module does not timestamp-decode) is cross-checked by field-reordering the v1 instant and asserting the same UTC. A non-UUID string is rejected; fuzz-clean. `internal/uuidinfo`. Registry 535‚Üí536.
- `geohash_decode` (geohash ‚Üî lat/lon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.516.0 ‚Äî added the **geohash converter as a decode companion to the project's data decoders**: the geohash (compact base-32 geocode, e.g. `ezs42`) is stored by **Redis GEO** (GEOADD/GEOPOS), Elasticsearch / MongoDB geo indexes, and countless location APIs ‚Äî so a geohash surfaced by `redis_decode` / `mongodb_decode` / `bson_decode` in a captured cache value, document, or API response now decodes to a real latitude+longitude (a genuine forensic/triage tie, not generic utility; sibling of v0.515's `maidenhead_locator`). Bidirectional: **decode** a geohash (case-insensitive, 1‚Äì12 chars) ‚Üí cell **center** + ¬± error (half-cell) + bounding box (precision explicit, never overstated); **encode** a fix ‚Üí geohash at 1‚Äì12 chars (default 9 ‚âà 4.8 m). Native ‚Äî base-32 range-bisection over the lat (‚àí90..90) / lon (‚àí180..180) ranges, 5 bits per char (alphabet `0123456789bcdefghjkmnpqrstuvwxyz`, no a/i/l/o); stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the `pygeohash` reference library**: `ezs42` ‚Üí (42.60498, ‚àí5.60303) ¬± 0.0220¬∞, `u4pruydqqvj` ‚Üí (57.649111, 10.407440), `9q8yy` ‚Üí San Francisco, single-char `0` ‚Üí (‚àí67.5, ‚àí157.5) ¬± 22.5¬∞; encode reproduces each, and decode‚Üíencode round-trips. Out-of-alphabet chars and out-of-range coords are rejected; fuzz-clean. `internal/geohash`. Registry 534‚Üí535.
- `maidenhead_locator` (Maidenhead grid-locator ‚Üî lat/lon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.515.0 ‚Äî added the **ham-radio geo converter** that complements the project's APRS / AIS / GPS-NMEA decoders: the Maidenhead grid locator (a.k.a. QTH / grid square, e.g. `FN31pr`) is the location format used throughout amateur radio ‚Äî in APRS, ham logging, contesting, and on the displays of many handheld/mobile rigs. Bidirectional: **decode** a locator (case-insensitive, 1‚Äì4 pairs) to its grid-square **center** lat/lon + **SW corner** + cell size (so the precision is explicit, never overstated), or **encode** a fix to a locator at 1‚Äì4 pairs (default 3 ‚Üí the common 6-character locator). Native ‚Äî the Maidenhead system is public fixed-base arithmetic (alternating base-18 field A-R, base-10 square, base-24 subsquare a-x, base-10 extended over the 360¬∞√ó180¬∞ world grid); stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the `maidenhead` reference library** (venv-oracle): e.g. (41.714, ‚àí72.728) ‚Üí `FN31pr` (and `FN31`, `FN31pr21` at 2/4 pairs), (48.146, 11.608) ‚Üí `JN58td`, (0,0) ‚Üí `JJ00aa`; and `JN58td` ‚Üí SW corner 48.125¬∞N/11.5833¬∞E, center 48.1458¬∞N/11.625¬∞E. Malformed locators (odd length, out-of-range field/square/subsquare char) and out-of-range coordinates are rejected; decode is case-insensitive and round-trips with encode. Fuzz-clean (~3.4M execs). `internal/maidenhead`. Registry 533‚Üí534.
- `subghz_jammer_detect` (offline sub-GHz jammer analyser) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.514.0 ‚Äî shipped the ¬ß3 **rank-16** gap, and the last pure-offline, no-hardware item left on the Top-30 (the rest need a HackRF / Pineapple / Sniffle / PM3 / chip-dump backend). It is the host-side complement to the on-device Sub-GHz Jammer Detect FAP (`loader_subghz_jammer_detect`, which only flags on the Flipper itself): the operator feeds an already-captured RSSI sample sequence (dBm, capture order) and the analyser computes the objective statistics ‚Äî min / max / mean / median / std-dev / **noise floor** (a low percentile, robust to bursts) / **occupancy fraction** / **longest continuous dwell** ‚Äî then applies the same receive-only "RSSI floor + dwell" heuristic as the FAP. Three flags, each an **observation with its benign explanation** stated (never a jammer verdict ‚Äî a confidently-wrong alert is worse than none, the same framing as the shipped `subghz_rollback_detect` and `tpms_anomaly_detect`): **elevated_noise_floor** (the channel idles at a raised level), **sustained_occupancy** (continuous rather than bursty energy), **long_dwell** (the longest unbroken above-busy run spans most of the capture). The decision thresholds (busy dBm, elevated-floor dBm, floor percentile, occupancy fraction, dwell fraction) all have documented defaults, are overridable, and are echoed back in the result so the reading is reproducible. Native ‚Äî a pure statistical sequence transform, stdlib `math`/`sort` only, no hardware and no new go.mod dep. **No confidently-wrong risk**: the statistics are deterministic and hand-vector-verified (a known ramp's mean/median/std-dev/10th-percentile-floor/occupancy/dwell asserted exactly; a continuous ‚àí45 dBm carrier fires all three flags; a bursty low-duty-cycle capture fires none); the flags are thresholded observations, not a verdict. Fuzz-clean. `internal/subghz.AnalyzeJamming`. Registry 532‚Üí533.
- `gps_nmea_decode` GSV per-satellite + GST + ZDA ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.513.0 ‚Äî expanded the v0.512 NMEA decoder with the sentences most useful for GPS signal-integrity / spoofing-and-jamming analysis: **GSV per-satellite detail** (PRN / elevation / azimuth / SNR for each satellite in view ‚Äî anomalous SNR or geometry is a spoofing/jamming signal; SNR is null when a satellite is tracked-but-unused), **GST** (pseudorange error statistics ‚Äî RMS, the error-ellipse major/minor/orientation, and lat/lon/altitude standard deviations ‚Äî fix integrity), and **ZDA** (UTC time + date). `gps_nmea_decode` now covers GGA/RMC/GLL/VTG/GSA/GSV/GST/ZDA. **Anchored to pynmea2** ‚Äî the canonical example sentences reproduce its per-satellite PRN/elev/azim/SNR, GST error fields, and ZDA date exactly. Fuzz-clean (~6.9M execs). No new tool ‚Äî extends `gps_nmea_decode` (`internal/nmea`); registry unchanged.
- `gps_nmea_decode` (GPS/GNSS NMEA 0183 sentence decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.512.0 ‚Äî closed a real gap in the GPS workflow: the project had device-side GPS tools (`marauder_nmea`, `gps_tracker_*`, `gps_poi`) but **no offline NMEA decoder** ‚Äî `marauder_nmea` only *streams* raw sentences the operator then has to read by hand. `gps_nmea_decode` is the offline complement (the GPS counterpart to `ais_nmea_decode`, which only handles AIS `!AIVDM`): paste a captured NMEA log ‚Äî a wardriving track, a geotag stream, a drone-telemetry dump, or a single `$GPGGA‚Ä¶` line ‚Äî and get the parsed fix. Decodes the position/velocity/fix sentences with the per-sentence XOR checksum validated: **GGA** (time, lat/lon, fix quality, satellites, HDOP, altitude), **RMC** (time, status, lat/lon, speed-knots, course, date, magnetic variation), **GLL** (lat/lon, time, status), **VTG** (true+magnetic course, speed knots+km/h), **GSA** (no-fix/2D/3D fix type, PDOP/HDOP/VDOP), **GSV** (satellites in view). Coordinates convert `ddmm.mmmm`/hemisphere ‚Üí signed decimal degrees; the talker ID (GP/GN/GL/GA/GB/BD/GQ/GI) is identified; a multi-sentence stream decodes to an array. `checksum_ok` is reported (bad/absent checksum still parses but is flagged); an empty field (no fix yet) decodes to null, never a zero; an unrecognised sentence type is surfaced with its raw fields rather than guessed. Native ‚Äî public comma-delimited ASCII + XOR checksum, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (a Go NMEA library would be a runtime dep for a few hundred lines of field handling). **Anchored to the pynmea2 reference library** ‚Äî the canonical example sentences reproduce its decoded latitude/longitude/time/speed/course/fix fields exactly (e.g. `$GPGGA,123519,4807.038,N,01131.000,E,‚Ä¶` ‚Üí 48.1173¬∞N, 11.5167¬∞E). Fuzz-clean (~7.4M execs, 0 crashes). `internal/nmea`. Registry 531‚Üí532.
- `aprs_packet_decode` compressed complete weather report (APRS101 ¬ß12) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.511.0 ‚Äî the noted v0.509 follow-up, completing APRS weather coverage: a **¬ß9 compressed position whose symbol code is `_`** (weather station) carries a weather block after the 13-byte compressed position. Unlike the uncompressed ¬ß12 complete weather report, there is **no leading `ddd/sss` wind extension** ‚Äî the wind is carried by the compressed cs course/speed (already decoded), so the block begins directly at the gust/temperature fields and is parsed by the same shared gust-onward tail parser used by the positionless and uncompressed-complete forms. Decodes gust / temperature / rain (1 h / 24 h / since-midnight) / humidity / pressure / luminosity. **Gated on at least one weather field actually parsing**, so a `_`-symbol compressed position carrying a plain free-text comment is reported as a comment, never as empty weather (no confidently-wrong output). **Anchored to the aprslib reference decoder** ‚Äî three vectors (no-cs weather, cs-present weather, and the comment-gate case) reproduce aprslib's decoded gust/temp/humidity/pressure exactly (APRS-native units). Fuzz-clean (~6.3M execs) incl. the new weather seeds. This closes the last APRS gap noted in v0.509; no new tool ‚Äî extends `aprs_packet_decode` (`internal/aprs`); registry unchanged. Shipped alongside a stability-hardening continuation of v0.510: FuzzDecode harnesses added to 33 more decoder packages (the remaining un-fuzzed binary + text parsers ‚Äî arpdecode/bfd/imap/ntlm/redis/sip/syslog/‚Ä¶ ), all swept clean over millions of execs and now permanent `go test` regression coverage.
- `aprs_packet_decode` compressed position (APRS101 ¬ß9) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.509.0 ‚Äî re-surveyed off the (now-exhausted) credential / key-file veins back into the project's **ham-RF domain** and closed the last open APRS position-format gap: the **base-91 compressed position** (APRS101 ¬ß9), previously dispatched-but-deferred ("a separate format with base-91 lat/lon encoding"). A compressed position packs symbol-table + 4-byte latitude + 4-byte longitude + symbol-code + a 2-byte cs + a 1-byte type into 13 bytes; modern trackers and APRS-IS feeds use it heavily. Decodes `latitude_deg` (90 ‚àí base91/380926) + `longitude_deg` (‚àí180 + base91/190463) + symbol, plus the cs+type extension to exactly one of **course_deg + speed_knots**, **altitude_ft**, or **radio_range_mi** (kept in APRS-native units; a space cs byte = no extension), dispatched by the type byte (`type&0x18==0x10` ‚Üí altitude; `c1` 0..89 ‚Üí course/speed; `c1==90` ‚Üí range) exactly as the reference decoders do. Compressed vs ¬ß8 uncompressed is detected unambiguously (compressed leads with a `/`/`\`/A-Z/a-j symbol-table char; uncompressed with a digit). This completes APRS position coverage: **uncompressed (¬ß8) + Mic-E (¬ß10) + compressed (¬ß9)**. **Anchored to the `aprslib` Python reference library** (venv-oracle): five vectors ‚Äî course/speed, no-cs, altitude, radio-range, and a `=`-with-comment case ‚Äî reproduce aprslib's decoded lat/lon/course/speed/altitude/range exactly (converted to APRS-native units: knots = aprslib km/h √∑ 1.852, feet = m √∑ 0.3048, miles = km √∑ 1.609344). Fuzz-clean (~9M execs, 0 crashes) incl. the new compressed seeds; an uncompressed-still-works regression guards the dispatch. No new tool ‚Äî extends `aprs_packet_decode` (`internal/aprs`); registry unchanged. The compressed-position **complete weather report** (a ¬ß9 position whose symbol code is `_`, trailing a weather block) remains the noted follow-up.
- `pem_privkey_decode` (PEM private-key triage) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.508.0 ‚Äî completed the **key-file loot-triage trio** (after `ssh_privkey_decode` v0.506 and `putty_privkey_decode` v0.507) with the **openssl-key counterpart**: a stolen `.pem` / `.key` (TLS server key, client-cert key, API key) is top loot, and this answers the same triage questions across the openssl PEM family ‚Äî PKCS#1 (`BEGIN RSA PRIVATE KEY`), SEC1 (`BEGIN EC PRIVATE KEY`), PKCS#8 (`BEGIN PRIVATE KEY`), and both encrypted forms (traditional `Proc-Type`/`DEK-Info`, and PKCS#8 `BEGIN ENCRYPTED PRIVATE KEY`). **encrypted?** ‚Üí if yes, crack with openssl / pem2john + John before use; **algorithm + size** ‚Äî RSA (+ modulus bits, with an **RSA-1024 weak-key warning**), ECDSA (+ curve), Ed25519, DSA (the type/size of an *encrypted* key live in the ciphertext and are reported unavailable, never guessed); **public_sha256** (unencrypted) ‚Äî the SHA-256 of the SubjectPublicKeyInfo DER, to correlate the key with a known cert / TLS endpoint; **cipher + KDF** (encrypted) ‚Äî traditional cipher + IV len (legacy MD5 KDF), or PKCS#8 PBES2 cipher + IV + the KDF: **PBKDF2** (salt len + iterations + PRF) or **scrypt** (N / r / p) ‚Äî the crack cost. Native ‚Äî own code + Go stdlib: `crypto/x509` parses the standard unencrypted key DER (hand-rolling RSA/EC DER would reinvent stdlib poorly and risk a confidently-wrong decode), and the part stdlib won't do passphrase-free ‚Äî reading the cipher/KDF params out of an encrypted key ‚Äî is a hand-rolled `encoding/asn1` walk of the `EncryptedPrivateKeyInfo` (PBES2 ‚Üí PBKDF2/scrypt + encryption scheme). No PEM/PKCS library added to go.mod. **Anchored to openssl**: a generated EC P-256 (`535d736b‚Ä¶`), Ed25519 (`ae34dd3b‚Ä¶`) and RSA-1024 (`55116c99‚Ä¶`) key reproduce `openssl pkey -pubout -outform DER | sha256sum` exactly; the encrypted vectors' cipher / KDF / salt-len / iterations (PBKDF2 20000, hmacWithSHA256) / N,r,p (scrypt 16384/8/1) / IV-len reproduce `openssl asn1parse` exactly. Every recognised OID is vector-checked; an unrecognised algorithm/cipher/KDF/PRF OID is surfaced as its dotted string with `(unrecognized)`, never guessed. A non-PEM blob / un-parseable DER is rejected; an OpenSSH-format key is redirected to `ssh_privkey_decode`. Fuzz-clean (~7.3M execs, 0 crashes/hangs). `internal/pemkey`. Registry 530‚Üí531.
- `putty_privkey_decode` (PuTTY .ppk private-key triage) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.507.0 ‚Äî continued the **key-file loot triage** vein opened by `ssh_privkey_decode`, adding its **Windows counterpart**: a saved PuTTY / WinSCP / FileZilla / pscp `.ppk` key is the same top-tier loot as a stolen `id_ed25519`, and it answers the same triage questions. **encrypted?** (`encryption` none / aes256-cbc + flag ‚Üí if yes, putty2john + John the Ripper; if no, directly usable); for a v3 encrypted key the **Argon2 KDF** flavour (Argon2id/i/d) + memory / passes / parallelism / salt length (crack cost); the **key type + SHA256 fingerprint** (a .ppk's `Public-Lines` block is byte-for-byte the **same SSH-wire public blob** as an OpenSSH `.pub`, so the fingerprint correlates the key with an `authorized_keys` entry); and the **comment** ‚Äî which, unlike an OpenSSH key, is a **cleartext header readable even when the key is encrypted**. The format is the documented line-based `PuTTY-User-Key-File-N` text container (PuTTY AppendixC). Native ‚Äî line parsing + base64 + `crypto/sha256`, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (a PPK library would be a runtime dep for a few dozen lines of text parsing). **Verification: the key-type + fingerprint are cross-validated against `ssh-keygen -l`** ‚Äî a .ppk built from a generated ed25519 (alice@victim ‚Üí `SHA256:RYwu7r7v81keCa5t4NM5dGBCBmoH1M80rW8RJt3HlKY`) and rsa-2048 (svc@host ‚Üí `SHA256:AWeSx77RBL5vG83pduVmy6GNYeQr2qZTvlOGE+S6UfU`) key reproduces ssh-keygen's exact fingerprint, type and comment; the header fields (version 2/3, Encryption, Comment, Key-Derivation, Argon2-*, Private-MAC) follow the AppendixC spec verbatim (plain-text reads ‚Äî no transform that could be confidently wrong). The Private-Lines section (PuTTY's own private layout) and the Private-MAC are surfaced/raw, not decoded or verified ‚Äî MAC verification needs the passphrase-derived key, and a wrong valid/invalid verdict would be worse than none. Block-count consumption and line counts are bounds-checked; CRLF tolerated; fuzz-clean (~9.6M execs, 0 crashes/hangs). No `puttygen` was available to produce an end-to-end oracle, so the security-critical decode (fingerprint/type, the only transform) is cross-validated against `ssh-keygen` instead ‚Äî a stronger anchor than a single tool's self-output. `internal/puttykey`. Registry 529‚Üí530.
- `ssh_privkey_decode` (OpenSSH private-key triage) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.506.0 ‚Äî pivoted off the (now-exhausted) recognized-credential-format vein into **key-file loot triage**, a fresh area. A stolen private key (`id_ed25519` / `id_rsa`) is top pentest loot, and the openssh-key-v1 format exposes ‚Äî from the **public** portion, readable even when the key is encrypted ‚Äî everything that drives the next step: **encrypted?** (cipher + flag ‚Üí if yes, ssh2john + hashcat `-m 22921`; if no, directly usable), the **bcrypt KDF** rounds + salt length (crack cost), the **key type** + **SHA256 fingerprint** (exactly as `ssh-keygen -l` prints, to correlate the key with an `authorized_keys` entry / known target), and ‚Äî for an unencrypted key ‚Äî the **comment** (often `user@host`; for an encrypted key it lives in the encrypted section and is reported unavailable, never guessed). Native ‚Äî base64 + an SSH-wire length-prefixed walk + SHA-256 (x/crypto/ssh refuses to even parse an encrypted key without the passphrase, defeating triage). **Anchored to `ssh-keygen -l`**: generated ed25519 + rsa keys (encrypted and not) reproduce its exact SHA256 fingerprint / type / encrypted state / comment byte-for-byte. Length fields bounds-checked; fuzz-clean. No new go.mod dep (`internal/sshkey`). Registry 528‚Üí529.
- `dcc2` (Domain Cached Credentials v2 / mscash2 compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.505.0 ‚Äî the remaining recognized-but-uncomputable AD credential format, completing the credential-compute set: DCC2 is how Windows (Vista / Server 2008+) caches domain logons locally, dumped from a compromised workstation's SECURITY hive (impacket secretsdump), hashcat mode 2100. Unlike an NT hash it **cannot be passed-the-hash** ‚Äî it's offline-crack-only ‚Äî so the compute/verify side is the gap (`hash_identify` flags `$DCC2$`, `hash_crack` attacks it, but neither produced/checked one). Algorithm: DCC1 = MD4(MD4(password)‚Äñlower(username)) (UTF-16LE); DCC2 = PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA1(DCC1, lower(username), iterations, 16); stored `$DCC2$<iters>#<username>#<hex>` (default 10240). Compute (username = the salt, optional iterations) or verify a candidate (username+iterations taken from the hash, constant-time; malformed rejected). **Strongest verification class ‚Äî gated byte-for-byte against the canonical hashcat mode-2100 example** `$DCC2$10240#tom#e4e938d12fe5974dc42a90120bd9c90f` (password `hashcat`, the independent anchor) + pycryptodome-confirmed vectors; round-trip + case-insensitive-salt + malformed tests; fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî composes the in-tree **MD4** (`internal/nthash`) + **PBKDF2** (`internal/wpa`), no new go.mod dep (`internal/dcc2`). Registry 527‚Üí528.
- `krb_roast_hashcat` AES support ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.504.0 ‚Äî the noted v0.503 follow-up: extended the roast-line builder to **AES (etype 17/18)** tickets, now the modern AD default. The AES cipher splits **edata ‚Äñ checksum(12)** ‚Äî the checksum is the LAST 12 bytes, opposite to RC4's leading 16 ‚Äî so getting this wrong would be confidently-wrong; the format is anchored to **impacket's GetUserSPNs / GetNPUsers AES output verbatim**: AES Kerberoast ‚Üí `$krb5tgs$<17|18>$user$realm$*spn*$checksum$edata` (hashcat **-m 19600** AES128 / **-m 19700** AES256, the SPN `*`-wrapped alone with `:`‚Üí`~`); AES AS-REP roast ‚Üí `$krb5asrep$<17|18>$user$realm$checksum$edata` (no standard hashcat mode ‚Äî flagged for John). The RC4 path also gained the `:`‚Üí`~` SPN convention. Verified against hand-built AES TGS-REP (etype 18, SPN `MSSQLSvc/db.corp.local:1433`) + AES AS-REP (etype 17) DERs reproducing impacket's exact lines byte-for-byte; fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî completes `krb_roast_hashcat` (`internal/krbroast`); registry unchanged.
- `krb_roast_hashcat` (Kerberoast / AS-REP-roast crack-line builder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.503.0 ‚Äî the Kerberos sibling of v0.502's `netntlm_hashcat`, closing the capture‚Üícrackable-hash step for the **#1/#2 AD credential attacks**. From a captured KDC response: an **AS-REP** (user with pre-auth disabled ‚Äî its [6] enc-part is encrypted with the user's password key) ‚Üí `$krb5asrep$23$user@REALM:checksum$edata` (hashcat **-m 18200**); a **TGS-REP** (its service ticket's enc-part is encrypted with the service account's key) ‚Üí `$krb5tgs$23$*user$REALM$spn*$checksum$edata` (hashcat **-m 13100**, SPN taken from the service ticket's sname). Required extending `kerberos_decode` to surface the AS-REP/TGS-REP [6] enc-part etype+cipher and the service ticket's enc-part cipher (reusing the v0.501 EncryptedData walker, now capturing the cipher bytes). The RC4 (etype 23) cipher is split checksum(16)‚Äñedata as hashcat expects; an **AES (etype 17/18)** enc-part places its checksum differently (modes 19600/19700) and is reported as not-yet-supported rather than mis-split (no confidently-wrong output). **Anchored to hand-built, spec-conformant AS-REP + TGS-REP DERs** (raw-TLV-assembled to avoid pyasn1 friction, with known enc-parts; the EncryptedData parse is the same one verified against the impacket Ticket) producing the canonical hashcat 18200 / 13100 lines byte-for-byte. Fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî reuses the in-tree `internal/kerberos` decoder, no new go.mod dep (`internal/krbroast`). Registry 526‚Üí527.
- `netntlm_hashcat` (NetNTLM crack-line builder) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.502.0 ‚Äî closes the **capture‚Üícrackable-hash** step of the SMB-relay / Responder / NTLM-over-HTTP loot workflow, complementing `ntlm_decode` (which surfaces the server challenge + NtChallengeResponse but left the operator to hand-assemble). From a captured NTLMSSP **AUTHENTICATE** message + the 8-byte **server challenge** (supplied directly, or extracted from the prior **CHALLENGE** message), it emits the ready-to-crack hashcat line: **NetNTLMv2 (`-m 5600`)** `user::domain:serverChallenge:NTProofStr:blob` (NtChallengeResponse = NTProofStr(16)‚Äñblob), or **NetNTLMv1 (`-m 5500`)** `user::domain:LMresp:NTresp:serverChallenge` when the NtChallengeResponse is exactly 24 bytes (NTLM-downgrade capture). The version is chosen by the response length; a non-AUTHENTICATE input or a non-8-byte challenge errors rather than emitting a malformed line. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the canonical hashcat mode-5600 example** (`admin::N46iSNekpT:08ca45b7d7ea58ee:88dcbe‚Ä¶:5c7830‚Ä¶`): an AUTHENTICATE message built via impacket to embed that example's user/domain/NtChallengeResponse, plus its server challenge, reproduces the example line exactly. Reuses the in-tree `internal/ntlm` parser (no new dep, one-way import); fuzz-clean. Native (`internal/netntlm`). Registry 525‚Üí526.
- `kerberos_decode` bare-Ticket decode + `ccache_decode` ticket chain ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.501.0 ‚Äî completed the AD-loot chain from v0.499/v0.500: `kerberos_decode` previously only **measured** the embedded ticket's byte length; it now decodes a **bare [APPLICATION 1] Ticket** (RFC 4120 ¬ß5.3) ‚Äî the cleartext outer fields **tkt-vno / realm / service principal (sname) / enc-part etype + kvno** ‚Äî and decodes the same for the **embedded ticket of an AS-REP / TGS-REP** (not just its length). An **etype 23 (RC4)** ticket is flagged **Kerberoastable / hashcat-13100-crackable** ‚Äî the key triage signal. `ccache_decode` now **chains each credential's ticket blob into this Ticket decoder** (`inner_ticket`), so a pasted ccache directly surfaces every ticket's target service + encryption (reusing the existing `decodePrincipalName` / `decodeGeneralString` ASN.1 helpers; no import cycle, no new tool). **Anchored to an authoritative impacket-built Ticket DER** (sname HTTP/web.corp.local@CORP.LOCAL, etype 23) ‚Äî and the rebuilt ccache vector embedding it is double-confirmed by `klist -cf` which lists the same `Ticket server: HTTP/web.corp.local@CORP.LOCAL`. Fuzz-clean on both the new Ticket path and the chain. Native ‚Äî reuses the in-tree Kerberos ASN.1 walker, no new go.mod dep (`internal/kerberos` + `internal/ccache`); registry unchanged.
- `ccache_decode` (MIT Kerberos credential cache parser) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.500.0 ‚Äî the natural keytab sibling and the **pass-the-ticket** loot complement to v0.499's keytab (pass-the-key): an on-disk `/tmp/krb5cc_*` / KRB5CCNAME file or a Rubeus / Mimikatz dump holds **live Kerberos tickets**, and a TGT (server `krbtgt/‚Ä¶`) is the golden-ticket / delegation pivot (flagged). Parses the v0x0504 FILE format: the default principal, then per credential the **client** + **server** principals, session **key_type** + key, the validity **times** (auth/start/end/renew-till ‚Üí RFC 3339), the **ticket_flags** decoded to names (forwardable / renewable / initial / pre-authent / ok-as-delegate / ‚Ä¶), and the embedded **ticket** (hex ‚Äî the pass-the-ticket blob). Length fields are bounds-checked, hostile address/authdata counts capped, truncated credentials rejected; legacy 0x0501‚Äì0x0503 reported rather than mis-decoded. **Anchored end-to-end to the authoritative MIT `klist -cf`**: a hand-built ccache is confirmed to list `alice@EXAMPLE.COM`, service `krbtgt/EXAMPLE.COM@EXAMPLE.COM`, the three times, and `Flags: FRIA` ‚Äî the oracle also settled the v4 keyblock's version-specific `etype` field and the exact bit‚Üíname flag mapping ‚Äî and the same bytes parse identically here. The sibling-bug sweep from v0.499 (the keytab MinInt32 panic) confirmed no analogous signed-length path exists; fuzz-clean (~11.5M execs, all-unsigned-length design). Native ‚Äî `encoding/binary` length-prefixed walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/ccache`). Registry 524‚Üí525.
- `keytab_decode` (MIT Kerberos keytab parser) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.499.0 ‚Äî fresh **AD-pentest loot** target and the file-format complement to `kerberos_decode` (which dissects the Kerberos *wire protocol*). A `.keytab` recovered from a compromised host holds the long-term Kerberos keys of the principals it serves ‚Äî used for offline ticket forging (**silver tickets**), **pass-the-key / overpass-the-hash**, and for the **RC4 (etype 23)** entries the account's **NT hash** directly (flagged). Parses the v0x0502 format: per entry the **principal** (components joined `/` + `@realm`), realm + components, **name_type** (KRB5_NT_PRINCIPAL / SRV_HST / ‚Ä¶), **kvno** (8-bit or the 32-bit extended form), **enctype** id + name (aes256 / aes128 / arcfour-RC4 / des3 / ‚Ä¶), timestamp, and the raw **key** (hex); deleted/hole entries (negative size) are counted and skipped; the legacy 0x0501 host-byte-order variant is reported rather than mis-decoded. **Anchored to the authoritative MIT `ktutil`**: a hand-built keytab (HTTP/web.example.com@EXAMPLE.COM, kvno 5, etype 18, 32-byte key) is confirmed by `ktutil rkt ‚Ä¶ / list -e -t` to list exactly those values, and the same bytes parse identically here. **The fuzz harness immediately caught a real panic** ‚Äî a MinInt32 (0x80000000) entry size on the deleted-entry path negated back to negative and drove the offset out of range; fixed with int64 promotion + a bounds guard, locked in as a corpus regression + explicit test, then 30s/15.3M-exec fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî `encoding/binary` length-prefixed walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/keytab`). Registry 523‚Üí524.
- `saml_decode` (SAML 2.0 message decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.498.0 ‚Äî continued the **web-auth decode stack** (jwt_decode + paseto_decode + now SAML), the SSO triage trio. A SAMLRequest / SAMLResponse captured from an SSO flow is standard pentest loot, and **golden-SAML** (forged/unsigned assertions) is a top AD-federation attack. `saml_decode` auto-detects the binding ‚Äî **HTTP-Redirect** (base64(raw-DEFLATE(xml)), the GET-redirect form) vs **HTTP-POST** (base64(xml)) ‚Äî tolerating percent-encoding (URL-pasted) and base64url, and surfaces the decoded **xml** (always, the source of truth) plus the extracted message_type / issuer / destination / id / version / issue_instant / in_response_to / **name_id** (the asserted identity) / status_code / Conditions (NotBefore/NotOnOrAfter) / audiences, and ‚Äî crucially for golden-SAML / unsigned-assertion triage ‚Äî a **signature_count + signature_present** flag (whether an XML-DSig Signature element is present). Fields are extracted by a namespace-agnostic local-name token scan with the raw XML as the source of truth (an absent field is empty, never guessed); a value that is neither DEFLATE-compressed XML nor raw XML is rejected; the inflate is size-bounded (LimitReader) against a hostile blob. XML-DSig signature **verification** (canonicalization + cert trust) and EncryptedAssertion decryption are deferred ‚Äî it reports whether a signature is present (the attack-surface signal), not whether it validates. **Verification: the base64+DEFLATE path is anchored to an independent redirect-binding vector produced by Python zlib** (the same standard DEFLATE real IdPs/SPs emit) that inflates to its exact source XML, plus a POST-binding signed Response whose every field is asserted; percent-encoded + malformed cases covered; fuzz-clean (~3.6M execs, 0 crashes/hangs). Native ‚Äî `encoding/base64` + `compress/flate` + `encoding/xml`, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/saml`). Registry 522‚Üí523.
- `paseto_decode` (PASETO token decode + Ed25519 verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.497.0 ‚Äî decisively diversified off the binary-serialization vein into the **web-token decode stack**: the **PASETO counterpart of `jwt_decode`**. PASETO ("Platform-Agnostic Security Tokens") is the modern signed/encrypted token format positioned as the safer JWT alternative (no algorithm confusion, versioned crypto), increasingly seen in modern APIs. Paste a token from an Authorization header / cookie / API body and get its structure ‚Äî and, for the **public** (signed, not encrypted) variants, the **cleartext claims without any key** (exactly like jwt_decode reads a JWT body). A token is `version.purpose.payload[.footer]` (base64url); for public tokens the payload is `message ‚Äñ signature` (v2/v4 Ed25519 = 64 B, v3 ECDSA P-384 = 96, v1 RSA-PSS = 256), so claims + signature are surfaced; for **local** (encrypted) tokens only the structure is visible (payload as length + hex + note ‚Äî decryption needs the symmetric key); the footer (often a `kid`) is decoded. Optionally **verifies** v2/v4 public signatures with a provided Ed25519 public key ‚Äî the authenticity check, computed natively over the PASETO **Pre-Authentication Encoding (PAE)** via `crypto/ed25519`. **Anchored to the official PASETO v4 test vectors** (`paseto-standard/test-vectors`): 4-S-1 decodes to its exact cleartext claims and verifies true with its published public key; a tampered token and a wrong implicit assertion verify false; 4-S-2's footer decodes; the v4.local 4-E-1 payload is surfaced encrypted, never guessed. Malformed tokens (wrong part count / bad base64url / payload shorter than the signature) are rejected. v1 (RSA) / v3 (ECDSA) verify and local decryption are deferred. Two fuzz harnesses (decode + verify), both clean. Native ‚Äî base64url + `crypto/ed25519`, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/paseto`). Registry 521‚Üí522.
- `bson_decode` Decimal128 decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.496.0 ‚Äî the noted v0.495 follow-up: decoded the BSON **Decimal128** type (deferred at v0.495 as raw hex) from its **IEEE 754-2008 Binary-Integer-Decimal** form to sign + 113-bit coefficient + biased exponent + an **exact plain (non-scientific) decimal value** (preserving Decimal128's unnormalized scale/trailing zeros), with **NaN / ¬±Infinity** surfaced as such; the raw 16 bytes are kept for traceability. Decimal128 carries the financial/scientific values in MongoDB documents, so this turns the last raw-hex BSON type into a usable number. The fiddly 128-bit BID layout (sign / 14-bit exponent at bits 62‚Äì49 / 113-bit coefficient via `math/big`, plus the Inf/NaN/large-coefficient combination forms) was **anchored byte-for-byte against PyMongo `Decimal128` vectors** ‚Äî coefficient + exponent taken straight from the library's `Decimal.as_tuple()` (1.50‚Üí150√ó10‚Åª¬≤, -7.50E+3‚Üí750√ó10¬π, a 30-digit coefficient, 1.234E-10, ¬±0, NaN, ¬±Infinity). The structural components (not a re-derived canonical string) are the decode, so there is no confidently-wrong E-notation-formatting risk; the plain value is the exact coefficient√ó10^exp. Fuzz-clean through the new `math/big` path. No new tool ‚Äî completes `bson_decode` (`internal/bson`); registry unchanged.
- `bson_decode` (BSON document dissector) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.495.0 ‚Äî continued the binary-serialization decode vein: BSON is the format MongoDB stores and that `mongodump` writes to `.bson` files (standard MongoDB loot). It is the **document-format complement to `mongodb_decode`** ‚Äî which dissects the MongoDB *wire protocol* and only shallowly extracts a command name + a few argument fields (its `bsonValueLength` walker just skips values and doesn't even handle several element types). `bson_decode` **fully, recursively decodes a standalone BSON document** into a structured tree, like `cbor_decode` / `msgpack_decode` do for theirs. Decodes every element type: double, int32, int64, bool, null, UTC datetime (‚Üí RFC 3339 + unix ms), timestamp (increment + seconds), string (UTF-8, length-validated), ObjectId (‚Üí hex), binary (length + subtype ‚Üí subtype name + data hex), embedded document + array (recursive, order-preserving), regex (pattern + options), JavaScript code + code-with-scope, the deprecated symbol / DBPointer / undefined, min/max key, and Decimal128 (surfaced as raw 16 bytes ‚Äî the IEEE 754-2008 decimal-string decode deferred to avoid a confidently-wrong value). A truncated/malformed document is rejected with an error (never a partial decode), length fields are bounds-checked, nesting is depth-capped, and trailing bytes are surfaced. **Strongest verification class ‚Äî every element type gated byte-for-byte against the reference PyMongo `bson` library** (venv-oracle): string, int32/64, double, bool/null, array, nested doc+array, ObjectId, datetime, binary (generic + UUID subtype), regex, timestamp, decimal128, min/max key. Fuzz-clean (~9.3M execs, 0 crashes/hangs). Native ‚Äî recursive-descent over a byte cursor, no new go.mod dep (`internal/bson`). Registry 520‚Üí521.
- `msgpack_decode` Timestamp ext decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.494.0 ‚Äî the noted v0.493 follow-up: decoded the **MessagePack Timestamp extension (ext type -1)** to RFC 3339 across all three wire layouts ‚Äî **32-bit** (uint32 seconds), **64-bit** (30-bit nanoseconds + 34-bit seconds), and **96-bit** (uint32 nanoseconds + *signed* int64 seconds, so pre-epoch times decode correctly). Timestamps are pervasive in msgpack payloads (Redis stream entry IDs, API record fields), so this turns the most common ext type from raw hex into a usable time. A non-standard Timestamp length, or a nanoseconds field ‚â• 1e9, is left raw with a note rather than decoded into a confidently-wrong time; other ext types stay raw. Anchored byte-for-byte to reference `msgpack` library vectors for all three layouts (2018-01-01Z 32-bit, +1¬µs 64-bit, 1900-01-01Z pre-epoch 96-bit) + malformed-length/out-of-range-nanos cases; fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `msgpack_decode` (`internal/msgpack`); registry unchanged.
- `msgpack_decode` (MessagePack dissector) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.493.0 ‚Äî deliberately diversified off the credential vein (5 consecutive credential ships) into the **binary-serialization decode space**: the msgpack sibling of `cbor_decode` / `protobuf_decode`. MessagePack (https://msgpack.org) is the compact binary serialization used by Redis internals, msgpack-RPC, many web/API backends, mobile-sync protocols and game-server traffic ‚Äî an operator pastes the hex of a captured blob (packet payload, cache value, stored token) and gets the decoded tree without a throwaway script. Decodes every core type: nil/bool, positive/negative fixint, uint8/16/32/64, int8/16/32/64 (sign-extended), float32/float64, str (fixstr/str8/16/32, UTF-8 with a non-UTF-8‚Üíhex+note fallback), bin (bin8/16/32‚Üíhex), array + map (fix/16/32, recursive, order- and duplicate-preserving), and ext (fixext1..16/ext8/16/32 ‚Üí type + data hex; the Timestamp ext type -1 is flagged but surfaced raw, time decode deferred to avoid a confidently-wrong value). Each node reports its wire `format` so the exact encoding is visible. A truncated/malformed blob is rejected with an error (never a partial/guessed decode), the reserved 0xc1 tag is rejected, hostile huge length fields are bounded (no giant up-front alloc), nesting is depth-capped, and trailing bytes after the top-level value are surfaced as `trailing_bytes_hex`. **Strongest verification class ‚Äî every format family gated byte-for-byte against the reference `msgpack` Python library** (venv-oracle): nil/bool, fixint/neg-fixint, the uint/int widths, float32/64, fixstr/str8, bin8, fixarray, fixmap, fixext4, and a nested `{"x":[1,true,nil],"y":"z"}` vector. Fuzz-clean (~5.6M execs, 0 crashes/hangs ‚Äî the length-bounding holds). Native ‚Äî recursive-descent over a byte cursor, no new go.mod dep (`internal/msgpack`). Registry 519‚Üí520.
- `cisco_type8` (Cisco IOS type-8 secret compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.492.0 ‚Äî the compute/verify side of the **Cisco modern `enable secret`** algorithm (introduced 2013, hashcat mode 9200), the network-device-config analogue of the DB-credential computes: `hash_identify` already flags `$8$‚Ä¶` as Cisco type 8 and `hash_crack` attacks it, but neither could produce or check one (the reversible older type 7 is handled by `cisco_type7_decode`). Type 8 is **PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA256** with an 80-bit salt and 20,000 iterations encoded in the Cisco base64 alphabet: `$8$<14-char salt>$<43-char digest>`, where the salt fed to PBKDF2 is the **ASCII of the salt string itself** (a Cisco quirk) and the 32-byte output is encoded big-endian over the `./0-9A-Za-z` alphabet. The exact construction (salt interpretation + big-endian base64 ordering) was **pinned empirically against the canonical hashcat-9200 vector** `$8$TnGX/fE4KGHOVU$pEhnEvxr‚Ä¶` (password `hashcat`) **plus a second vector cracked to `cisco`** ‚Äî both reproduced byte-for-byte in the tests (no confidently-wrong risk; I refused to ship until the published vector matched). Compute (optional 14-char salt, random if omitted) or verify a candidate (constant-time; a malformed hash ‚Äî wrong prefix / salt or digest length / alphabet ‚Äî is rejected, never silently "verified"). Type 9 (`$9$`, scrypt) is deliberately deferred (scrypt is not in the standard library; a wrong parameterisation would be confidently-wrong ‚Äî hash_identify flags it for cracking). PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA256 reuses the in-tree `internal/wpa.PBKDF2`; fuzz-clean. Native ‚Äî `internal/wpa.PBKDF2` + `crypto/sha256`, stdlib only (`internal/ciscopw` type8.go). Registry 518‚Üí519.
- `postgres_scram` (PostgreSQL SCRAM-SHA-256 verifier compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.491.0 ‚Äî the **modern PostgreSQL credential primitive**: scram-sha-256 is the **default since PostgreSQL 10** (2017) and the successor to the md5 verifier shipped in v0.487, completing the PG credential pair. The value stored in `pg_authid.rolpassword` is `SCRAM-SHA-256$<iter>:<b64 salt>$<b64 StoredKey>:<b64 ServerKey>` (hashcat mode 28600), derived per RFC 5802: SaltedPassword = PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA256(password, salt, iter); ClientKey = HMAC(SP, "Client Key"); StoredKey = SHA256(ClientKey); ServerKey = HMAC(SP, "Server Key"). Compute the verifier (optional base64 salt + iterations, default 4096), or verify a candidate by recomputing StoredKey from the verifier's own salt/iterations and constant-time comparing; a malformed verifier (wrong prefix/field-count/base64/iteration-count) is rejected, never silently "verified" (with an iteration-count cap so a hostile verifier can't wedge PBKDF2). **Strongest verification class ‚Äî anchored byte-for-byte to the RFC 7677 ¬ß3 worked example** (password `pencil`, salt `W22ZaJ0SNY7soEsUEjb6gQ==`, i=4096): the derivation reproduces the RFC's ClientProof (`p=`) and ServerSignature (`v=`) exactly (confirmed via an independent Python computation), and the resulting verifier string is pinned in the test. PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA256 reuses the in-tree `internal/wpa.PBKDF2` (the same primitive `pbkdf2_password` / `wpa_pmk_derive` use) ‚Äî no new dep. Full SASLprep of non-ASCII passwords is deferred (no-op for ASCII, the common case; raw UTF-8 otherwise, flagged). Round-trip + malformed-input tests; fuzz-clean (~5M execs, 0 crashes). Native ‚Äî `internal/wpa.PBKDF2` + `crypto/hmac` + `crypto/sha256` + base64, stdlib only (`internal/pgscram`). Registry 517‚Üí518.
- `postgres_password` (PostgreSQL md5 password compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.487.0 ‚Äî the **DB-credential sibling of `mysql_password`**, covering the PostgreSQL md5-authentication value stored in `pg_authid.rolpassword` / `pg_shadow.passwd` (hashcat mode 12) ‚Äî a standard `pg_dumpall --globals` loot format. PostgreSQL's `pg_md5_encrypt` salts the password with the **role name** before a single MD5: the stored value is `md5` + hex(MD5(password ‚Äñ username)) ‚Äî the literal `md5` + 32 lowercase hex. Because the salt is the username, the same password under two roles yields different values, so verification requires the username as well as the password. Compute the stored value, or verify a candidate against a captured value (`md5`-prefixed or bare 32-hex, either case, constant-time; a malformed value is rejected, never silently "verified"). `hash_identify` deliberately does **not** flag this format ‚Äî `md5`+32hex is ambiguous with a raw MD5, so adding an identify branch would be confidently-wrong; the tool stands alone. SCRAM-SHA-256 (the PG 10+ default, hashcat 28600 ‚Äî salted + iterated PBKDF2/HMAC) is out of scope. Strongest verification class ‚Äî the construction is unambiguous (single salted MD5, no rounds) and is exactly the documented `pg_md5_encrypt`, gated against the stdlib-hashlib oracle; round-trip (incl. empty/unicode passwords + empty role) + bare/uppercase + username-salting + malformed-input tests; fuzz-clean (~5.3M execs, 0 crashes). Native ‚Äî `crypto/md5` + `encoding/hex`, stdlib only (`internal/pgpassword`). Registry 516‚Üí517.
- `mysql_password` (MySQL / MariaDB mysql_native_password compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.486.0 ‚Äî the **MySQL credential primitive** and the next compute/verify gap-fill in the credential cluster: `hash_identify` already flagged this as **MySQL4.1+** (hashcat mode 300) and `hash_crack_dictionary` attacks it (its `mysql` branch), but neither could produce or check one ‚Äî the same gap `nt_hash` / `ldap_password` filled for their formats. The hash is the value stored in `mysql.user` ‚Äî an unsalted double SHA-1, `*` + `UPPER(hex(SHA1(SHA1(password))))`, a 41-character string (literal `*` + 40 uppercase hex; no per-row salt, so equal passwords share a hash). Compute a candidate's hash, or verify a candidate against a captured hash (`*`-prefixed or bare 40-hex, either case, constant-time compared; a malformed hash is rejected, never silently "verified"). The pre-4.1 OLD_PASSWORD (16-hex, hashcat 200 ‚Äî obsolete since 2003) and the `caching_sha2_password` / `sha256_password` plugins (salted, iterated) are out of scope. Strongest verification class ‚Äî the construction is unambiguous (double SHA-1, no rounds/salt), gated against the universally-published `PASSWORD('password') = *2470C0C06DEE42FD1618BB99005ADCA2EC9D1E19` vector + the hashcat-300 example; round-trip + bare/lowercase + malformed-input tests; fuzz-clean (~5.4M execs, 0 crashes). The same algorithm already backed the `mysql` branch of `hash_crack_dictionary`; this factors the compute/verify side into `internal/mysqlpw` so it is callable directly. Native ‚Äî `crypto/sha1` + `encoding/hex`, stdlib only. Registry 515‚Üí516.
- `ldap_password` (LDAP RFC 2307 userPassword compute + verify) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.485.0 ‚Äî the **directory-server credential primitive** and a new compute/verify gap-fill in the md5crypt / sha_crypt / bcrypt cluster: `hash_identify` already recognised `{SSHA}`/`{SHA}`/`{MD5}` (hashcat 111/101/1001) and `hash_crack` attacks them, but neither could produce or check one. Covers the OpenLDAP slapd / 389-DS / Dovecot / Atlassian Crowd `userPassword` schemes ‚Äî `{SHA}`/`{SSHA}` + `{MD5}`/`{SMD5}` (RFC 2307) and the OpenLDAP pw-sha2 / Dovecot SHA-2 extensions `{SHA256}`/`{SSHA256}`/`{SHA384}`/`{SSHA384}`/`{SHA512}`/`{SSHA512}`. Every scheme is `{SCHEME}base64( H(password ‚Äñ salt) ‚Äñ salt )` with no key-stretching, so on verify the **salt length is recovered from the blob** (slapd's 4-byte default and Dovecot's longer salts both verify) and the digest is compared constant-time. Compute (scheme default `{SSHA}`; verbatim or random 4-byte salt; salt rejected for unsalted schemes) or verify a candidate against a captured value (e.g. a slapcat dump). Strongest verification class ‚Äî the construction is unambiguous (single digest + base64, no rounds), gated byte-for-byte against the **OpenLDAP `slappasswd` oracle** (`{SHA}`/`{SSHA}`/`{MD5}`) and the definitional pw-sha2 / Dovecot vectors (SHA-2 variants); fuzz-clean (~5.9M execs, 0 crashes). `{CRYPT}` (RFC 2307 delegates to crypt(3) ‚Äî covered by md5crypt / sha_crypt / bcrypt) and `{CLEARTEXT}` are out of scope. Native ‚Äî `crypto/{md5,sha1,sha256,sha512}` + `encoding/base64`, stdlib only (`internal/ldappw`). Registry 514‚Üí515.
- `dcerpc_decode` sec_trailer NTLMSSP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.484.0 ‚Äî sibling-sweep of the v0.483 SMB2 NTLMSSP work, applying the same signature-scan chain to **DCE/RPC** (the MS-RPC framing layer behind nearly every Windows AD attack chain). When `auth_length > 0` the fragment's last `auth_length + 8` bytes are the sec_trailer header (auth_type / auth_level / pad_length / reserved / auth_context_id) + the auth_value token; the decoder previously surfaced `auth_length` only. Now it parses the sec_trailer ‚Äî naming `auth_type` (NTLMSSP / SPNEGO / Kerberos / NETLOGON / Schannel) + `auth_level` ‚Äî and when the auth_value carries an **NTLMSSP** message (located by the unambiguous 8-byte `NTLMSSP\0` signature, so both raw and **SPNEGO-wrapped** auth_values are handled without parsing the SPNEGO ASN.1) decodes it in place via `internal/ntlm` (the NTLM-over-RPC relay / Pass-the-Hash capture: server challenge, target-info AV pairs, domain / user / workstation ‚Äî the drsuapi/netlogon bind-time NTLM exchange). A Kerberos/Schannel auth_value (no NTLMSSP signature) surfaces auth_type/auth_level but its token body is left for `kerberos_decode` ‚Äî the no-confidently-wrong path. Verified with NTLMSSP CHALLENGE in a BIND_ACK sec_trailer + SPNEGO-wrapped NTLMSSP in an AUTH3 + Kerberos-not-decoded + oversized-auth_length cases; extended the dcerpc fuzz harness with the sec_trailer seeds, fuzz-clean (~6.3M execs, 0 crashes). No new tool ‚Äî extends `dcerpc_decode` (`internal/dcerpc` ‚Üí `internal/ntlm`). (Confirmed no import cycle: `internal/ntlm` does not import `internal/dcerpc`.)
- `smb2_decode` SESSION_SETUP NTLMSSP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.483.0 ‚Äî high-value AD-pentest chain: SMB2 SESSION_SETUP carries the auth token in its SecurityBuffer (NTLM / Kerberos), but the decoder previously didn't even parse SESSION_SETUP. Now it extracts the SESSION_SETUP request/response SecurityBuffer and, when it contains an **NTLMSSP** message ‚Äî located by the unambiguous 8-byte `NTLMSSP\0` signature, so both raw and **SPNEGO-wrapped** blobs are handled without parsing the SPNEGO ASN.1 ‚Äî decodes it in place via `internal/ntlm` (the NTLM-over-SMB relay / Responder / pass-the-hash capture: server challenge, target-info AV pairs, domain / user / workstation). Verified `kerberos.Decode`/`ntlm.Decode` both require the GSS-API wrapper pre-stripped, so the signature-scan approach is the clean no-confidently-wrong path; a Kerberos GSS-API token (no NTLMSSP signature) is left for `kerberos_decode`. Verified with NTLM CHALLENGE (response) + NEGOTIATE (request) + SPNEGO-wrapped + Kerberos-not-decoded vectors; added an smb2 fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through the SecurityBuffer‚Üíntlm path. No new tool ‚Äî extends `smb2_decode` (`internal/smb2` ‚Üí `internal/ntlm`).
- `pppoe_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.482.0 ‚Äî extended the chain-to-existing-decoder seam to **PPPoE** (the broadband-edge encapsulation ‚Äî DSL/fibre CPE, ISP access). A PPPoE Session frame carries a PPP frame; when the PPP Protocol ID is 0x0021 (IPv4) / 0x0057 (IPv6) the subscriber's inner IP packet is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode`, surfacing the session's inner flow's addresses / protocol / ports. PPP control protocols (LCP / IPCP / PAP / CHAP / EAP) are left as hex; an IP-typed payload that fails to parse ‚Üí `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. Verified with inner IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP + LCP-not-decoded + garbage cases; added a pppoe fuzz harness, fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `pppoe_decode` (`internal/pppoe` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`). (MSDP SA-encapsulated multicast is the last niche `ip_packet_decode` sibling.)
- `sflow_decode` sampled-header decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.481.0 ‚Äî extended the chain-to-existing-decoder seam to **sFlow** packet-sampling telemetry (the dominant datacenter monitoring export, UDP 6343). A Raw Packet Header flow record carries the first bytes of the sampled frame; when its header-protocol is Ethernet (1, IP after the 14-byte L2 header), IPv4 (11) or IPv6 (12), the sampled L3 packet is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode`, surfacing the sampled flow's addresses / protocol / ports. The capture is truncated to the sampled-header length so the decode may be partial (ipdecode degrades gracefully); a non-IP EtherType / non-IP header protocol is left as hex; IP-typed garbage ‚Üí `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. **Also fixed a pre-existing doc bug**: the package's header-protocol name table in the doc comment listed "11 802.11 / 12 IPv4 / 13 IPv6" but the implementation (and the sFlow v5 spec) is "11 IPv4 / 12 IPv6 / 13 MPLS" ‚Äî corrected. Verified with Ethernet-inner-IPv4 + direct-IPv4/IPv6 + ARP-not-decoded + garbage cases; added an sflow fuzz harness, fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `sflow_decode` (`internal/sflow` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`).
- `mpls_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.480.0 ‚Äî extended the tunnel-decap pattern to **MPLS** (provider/enterprise label-switched networks, MPLS-over-GRE/UDP): after the bottom-of-stack label, when the payload is IP ‚Äî an IPv4/IPv6 Explicit NULL bottom label, or a first nibble of 4/6 (the heuristic the package already computed) ‚Äî the inner packet is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode`, surfacing the label-switched flow's addresses / protocol / ports. EoMPLS / pseudowire payloads (0-nibble control word, Ethernet) are left as hex; an IP-typed payload that fails to parse ‚Üí `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. Verified with inner IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP + IPv4-Explicit-NULL + EoMPLS-not-decoded + garbage cases; added an mpls fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through the inner‚Üíipdecode path. No new tool ‚Äî extends `mpls_decode` (`internal/mpls` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`).
- `ir_raw_encode` NEC-extended + NEC-repeat ‚Äî completes the NEC family ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.624.0 ‚Äî extended `ir_raw_encode` with **NEC-extended** (16-bit address, command-inversion only) and the **NEC-repeat** code, so the encoder now covers the full NEC family the decoder handles (standard / extended / repeat), alongside Samsung32 / SIRC / RC5-RC5X / Kaseikyo. **No confidently-wrong output**: both are the exact inverse of the `decodeNEC` paths (NEC-extended emits `addrLo¬∑addrHi¬∑cmd¬∑~cmd` with the command-inversion checksum the decoder validates; NEC-repeat emits the `9000/2250/560` repeat code) and round-trip through `ir_raw_decode` (fuzz-verified, ~3.4M execs incl. the new variants). No new tool ‚Äî extends `ir_raw_encode` (`internal/ir`); registry unchanged.
- `ir_raw_encode` Kaseikyo encode ‚Äî full encoder/decoder symmetry ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.622.0 ‚Äî extended `ir_raw_encode` with **Kaseikyo** (Panasonic / Denon / JVC / Sharp / Mitsubishi), so the encoder now covers every protocol the decoder does (NEC / Samsung32 / SIRC / RC5-RC5X / Kaseikyo). Builds the 48-bit frame from vendor (16-bit, `vendor` param, default Panasonic 0x2002) + address (12-bit) + command (8-bit), computing **both** the vendor parity and the frame parity. **No confidently-wrong output**: the encoder is the exact inverse of `decodeKaseikyo` ‚Äî it reproduces the v0.613 Kaseikyo decode vector byte-for-byte (Panasonic 0x2002 / addr 0x123 / cmd 0x45) and round-trips through `ir_raw_decode` (the encode‚Üîdecode pair is fuzz-verified, ~2.3M execs incl. Kaseikyo, every successful encode decoding back to the same vendor/address/command). No new tool ‚Äî extends `ir_raw_encode` (`internal/ir`); registry unchanged.
- `ir_raw_encode` protocol+address+command ‚Üí raw IR ¬µs timings ‚Äî the inverse of ir_raw_decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.621.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the offline IR signal generator: the inverse of `ir_raw_decode` and the offline complement to the device-side `ir_build` (which writes a Flipper .ir file). Generates the raw timing sequence for **NEC** (8-bit address + command, both inverse-byte checksums emitted), **Samsung32** (address¬∑address¬∑command¬∑~command), **Sony SIRC** (12/15/20-bit), and **Philips RC5 / RC5X** (14-bit Manchester; command > 63 emits RC5X) ‚Äî and the emitted timings feed `ir_pronto_encode` to produce a shareable Pronto code. **No confidently-wrong output**: each generator is the exact inverse of the corresponding `ir_raw_decode` reader (promoted from the decoder's own proven test-vector generators), the encode‚Üîdecode pair is **round-trip- and fuzz-verified** (~1.4M random protocol/address/command inputs ‚Äî every successful encode decodes back to the same protocol/address/command), and out-of-range address/command/bits are rejected. Generation only ‚Äî transmits nothing (the actual replay is a separate device step), so it is Low risk. Native ‚Äî per-protocol pulse-distance / pulse-width / Manchester timing emission, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/ir`). Registry 613‚Üí614.
- `ir_pronto_encode` raw IR timings ‚Üí Pronto HEX (CCF) ‚Äî the inverse generator ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.615.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the inverse of `ir_pronto_decode` (v0.614) and the IR companion to the project's other inverse generators (`em4100_encode`, `rfid_pacs_encode`, `subghz_weather_synth`, `dcf77_synth`). Converts a raw IR timing capture (space/comma-separated ¬µs mark/space durations from `ir_receive raw`, a Flipper RAW .ir entry, or a logic-analyser trace) plus a carrier frequency into a raw-oscillated (format 0x0000) Pronto code, so a captured signal can be shared / imported (Logitech Harmony, JP1, RemoteCentral, IrScrutinizer). **No confidently-wrong output**: the conversion is the documented Pronto/CCF arithmetic inverted ‚Äî frequency word = round(1000000 / (carrier_hz √ó 0.241246)) (**38000 Hz ‚Üí 0x006D**, the canonical anchor), each burst = round(¬µs / carrier-period) (9000/4500¬µs ‚Üí 0156/00AB) ‚Äî and it **round-trips with `ir_pronto_decode`** (decoding the emitted code reproduces the input timings within carrier-period rounding, the strongest verification: no external vector needed). An odd timing count (not whole mark/space pairs), a non-numeric timing, a non-positive carrier, or a burst that overflows the Pronto range is rejected. Verified by the carrier/burst anchors, a decode‚àòencode round-trip over an NEC-shaped frame, and malformed-input rejections; fuzz-clean (`FuzzEncodePronto`, ~3.4M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî documented arithmetic inverted, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. Registered as `ir_pronto_encode` (Low risk, offline transform; transmits nothing); registry 607‚Üí608 (`internal/ir`).
- `ir_pronto_decode` Pronto HEX (CCF) IR-code decoder ‚Äî the universal textual IR format ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.614.0 ‚Äî **new tool** decoding **Pronto HEX (CCF)**, the universal textual IR-code format used by remote databases and learning remotes (Philips Pronto, **Logitech Harmony**, JP1, RemoteCentral, IrScrutinizer) ‚Äî the Pronto-format companion to `ir_raw_decode` (which takes raw ¬µs timings), and the Pronto half of the format the IR package doc previously flagged "deliberately not decoded here yet". A Pronto code is a list of 16-bit hex words: a format word, a frequency word, the intro + repeat burst-pair counts, then the burst values (each in carrier cycles). Converts the code to its **carrier frequency** and the **intro / repeat timing sequences in ¬µs**, and ‚Äî for the common raw-oscillated format ‚Äî chains the converted intro timings through the protocol decoder to **name the protocol** (NEC / Kaseikyo / Samsung32 / SIRC / RC5). **No confidently-wrong output**: the format-word meanings, the 0.241246 ¬µs Pronto clock unit and the burst-pair layout are the long-documented Pronto/CCF spec; the frequency word **0x006D ‚Üí 38029 Hz** is the canonical anchor and the burst‚Üí¬µs math (`0156 00AB` ‚Üí ~9000/4500 NEC leader) is verified independently. Only the raw formats (0x0000 oscillated / 0x0100 unmodulated) carry burst pairs and are converted; a predefined-code format word is reported by value with a note, not mis-converted; the chained protocol decode is best-effort (unknown ‚Üí carrier + raw timings surfaced, no guess); a word count inconsistent with the declared burst-pair counts / a non-4-hex word / a zero frequency is rejected. Verified against a real NEC code (006D ‚Üí 38029 Hz, 0156/00AB ‚Üí ~9000/4500, intro chain ‚Üí NEC), the carrier anchor, a predefined-format note case, and malformed-input rejections; fuzz-clean (`FuzzDecodePronto`, ~3.6M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî a word parse + documented arithmetic + a chain into `ir_raw_decode`, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. Registered as `ir_pronto_decode` (Low risk, offline transform); registry 606‚Üí607 (`internal/ir`).
- `ir_raw_decode` Kaseikyo (Panasonic / Denon / JVC / Sharp / Mitsubishi) ‚Äî 48-bit pulse-distance IR family ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.613.0 ‚Äî extended the raw-IR-timing decoder (`internal/ir`, the `ir_raw_decode` tool) with **Kaseikyo**, the 48-bit frame shared by **Panasonic / Denon / JVC / Sharp / Mitsubishi** consumer IR (a huge swath of AV gear) ‚Äî the most-requested pulse-distance family the decoder lacked.
