Kaseikyo uses a 3456¬µs/1728¬µs header (8√ó/4√ó the 432¬µs unit) then 48 LSB-first pulse-distance bits: 16-bit **vendor ID** ‚Üí 4-bit **vendor parity** ‚Üí 12-bit **address** ‚Üí 8-bit **command** ‚Üí 8-bit **frame parity**. Decodes the vendor ID (+ name: Panasonic 0x2002, Denon 0x3254, JVC 0x0103, Sharp 0x5AAA, Mitsubishi 0xCB23), address and command ‚Äî gated by **BOTH** integrity checks: the 4-bit vendor parity (XOR-fold of the vendor nibbles) **and** the 8-bit frame parity (byte2 ^ byte3 ^ byte4). A frame that matches the header + 48-bit structure but fails either gate is reported as `Kaseikyo-like (parity failed)` with its raw bytes ‚Äî never asserted as a real frame; the per-vendor semantics of the address/command vary, so the generic frame fields are surfaced as-is (no over-interpretation). The dispatcher adds a Kaseikyo branch **before** Samsung that matches both the 3456¬µs mark **and** the 1728¬µs space (the 3456¬µs mark falls inside Samsung's wide 4500¬±30% window, but the distinct header space disambiguates ‚Äî verified by a regression test that a Samsung header is not mis-routed). **No confidently-wrong output**: the timing constants, the bit/field layout and both parity formulas are taken from the **Arduino-IRremote** reference (`ir_Kaseikyo.hpp`) ‚Äî cross-corroborated by the SB-Projects Kaseikyo reference and the Flipper IR stack ‚Äî and the dual parity gates self-verify the layout. Verified against an independently-generated Panasonic vector (vendor 0x2002 / addr 0x123 / cmd 0x45 ‚Üí bytes `022030124567`, both parities valid), a parity-fail case, the vendor-parity formula, and a Samsung-non-collision regression; fuzz-clean (existing `FuzzDecodeRaw`, ~4.2M execs incl. Kaseikyo seeds, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî a leader-match + LSB-first pulse-distance reader + two parity folds, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `ir_raw_decode` (`internal/ir`); registry unchanged.
- `ir_raw_decode` Philips RC5 / RC5X (14-bit Manchester) ‚Äî third IR encoding family ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.568.0 ‚Äî extended the raw-IR-timing decoder (`internal/ir`, the `ir_raw_decode` tool) with **Philips RC5 / RC5X**, completing coverage of all three consumer-IR encoding families: pulse-distance (NEC / Samsung), pulse-width (Sony SIRC), and now **bi-phase / Manchester** (RC5), explicitly flagged "not decoded yet" in the package doc. RC5 is one of the most common consumer-IR protocols (Philips + much European/AV gear). Unlike the leader-based protocols, RC5 has **no leader** (it begins directly with the Manchester bit stream) and **no checksum**, so the decoder reconstructs the per-half-bit signal level from the 889¬µs/1778¬µs mark/space durations ‚Äî prepending the un-captured leading half-bit of S1 (captures start at the first mark) ‚Äî into exactly **28 half-bits forming 14 Manchester bit-pairs** (S1, S2, toggle, 5-bit address, 6-bit command), and is gated structurally: every duration must land on the 889/1778 grid, every bit-pair must be a valid Manchester transition, and **S1 must decode to 1** ‚Äî so a polarity-inverted or non-RC5 pulse train fails the grid / bit-pair / S1 gate and is rejected, not mis-decoded. **RC5X** (S2=0 carrying the inverted 7th command bit) is recognised and extends the command range to 0-127. The dispatcher checks RC5 before SIRC (an RC5X frame opens with a merged 1778¬µs mark inside SIRC's wide leader window, but SIRC's 2400¬µs leader is outside RC5's 1778¬±30% window, so the ordering is unambiguous ‚Äî a dispatch-overlap bug caught and fixed by the round-trip test). **No confidently-wrong output** and **no external oracle needed**: verified against two timing waveforms **hand-traced directly from the published RC5 spec** (all-zeros, and address 1 / command 32 to anchor the bit positions ‚Äî independent of the Go encoder), plus an independent encoder round-trip over 10 frames incl. RC5X, plus the structural S1 gate. Fuzz-clean (~5M execs incl. RC5 seeds). Native ‚Äî Manchester reconstruction + a per-bit-pair classifier, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `ir_raw_decode` (`internal/ir`); registry unchanged.
- `bt_adv_decode` Bluetooth advertising / scan-response (GAP AD structure / BR-EDR EIR) ‚Äî BLE-scan recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.607.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **advertising-layer complement** to the project's Bluetooth-stack decode chain (`bt_hci_decode` ‚Üí `bt_l2cap_decode` ‚Üí `bt_att_decode`). A BLE advertising payload is what every **passive BLE scan surfaces first** ‚Äî the Flipper Zero 'BLE scan', an ESP32 Marauder / nRF sniffer, a phone's nRF Connect: before any connection or GATT traffic, the advertising data is the **recon headline**. The exact same length-type-value AD-structure format is the BR/EDR **Extended Inquiry Response (EIR)**, so this decodes EIR too. It carries the device's advertised **name**, its discoverability / **role flags**, the **service UUIDs** it offers, its **TX power** and **appearance**, and ‚Äî most usefully for fingerprinting ‚Äî **manufacturer-specific data**: **Apple iBeacon** (proximity UUID + major/minor + measured power), **Eddystone** beacons (UID / URL / TLM telemetry), and the **company identifier** of the chipset / vendor behind an otherwise anonymous device. Decodes each AD structure: Flags (the discoverability / BR-EDR-not-supported bits), the 16/32/128-bit service-UUID + solicitation lists, Shortened / Complete Local Name, Tx Power Level, Appearance, LE Role, URI, Service Data (with the Eddystone UID/URL/TLM frame decode for UUID 0xFEAA ‚Äî the URL scheme-prefix + in-band domain abbreviations expanded), and Manufacturer Specific Data (company name + the iBeacon sub-format with the proximity UUID rendered MSB-first as transmitted). **No confidently-wrong output**: the AD type numbers, the Flags bits, the service-UUID layouts, the company-identifier assignment and the iBeacon / Eddystone sub-formats follow the Bluetooth Assigned Numbers and the published iBeacon / Eddystone specs; where a value space is open-ended or undocumented (an unknown AD type, an unknown company id, a manufacturer blob other than iBeacon such as Apple's proprietary **Continuity** stream, service data for a UUID other than Eddystone's 0xFEAA), the bytes are surfaced **raw** with a note rather than guessed; a truncated AD structure stops the walk with a note and the advertising-PDU zero-padding terminator is handled. Native ‚Äî a length-prefixed TLV walk + small lookup tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The Flags + Apple iBeacon, the Eddystone URL + TLM frames, the Local-Name + Tx-Power + Appearance, the LE Role + 128-bit service UUID, the unknown-company raw fallback, the truncation and the zero-padding cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean (~1.9M execs). `internal/bleadv`. Registered as `bt_adv_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 600‚Üí601.
- `bt_att_decode` Bluetooth ATT (Attribute Protocol / GATT) ‚Äî BLE GATT-traffic recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.606.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **final (application) layer** of the project's Bluetooth-stack decode chain (`bt_hci_decode` ‚Üí `bt_l2cap_decode` ‚Üí this), pairing with the UUID naming in `bluetooth_gatt_uuid_lookup`. ATT, carried on L2CAP CID 0x0004, is the request/response protocol behind **GATT** ‚Äî how a BLE client reads and writes a server's attributes (characteristics), discovers its services, and receives notifications. Decoding ATT traffic from a btsnoop / HCI-ACL capture is the recon headline for what a BLE app actually does on a device: which attribute **handles** it reads and writes, the **service / characteristic discovery** (Read By Group Type / Read By Type / Find Information) that maps the GATT database, and the **notifications / indications** a device pushes. Field-decodes the common opcodes: Error Response (failing request opcode + handle + error code), Exchange MTU, Find Information, Read By Type / Read By Group Type requests (start/end handle + UUID ‚Äî 16-bit or 128-bit, with the 128-bit wire little-endian reversed to MSB-first), Read / Read Blob, Write Request / Command / Signed Write (handle + value), and Handle Value Notification / Indication (handle + value). **No confidently-wrong output**: the ATT opcodes, the error codes and the per-opcode field layouts follow the Bluetooth Core specification (Vol 3 Part F); the attribute **value** blobs are surfaced as **raw hex** (characteristic-specific), and the length-prefixed attribute-data lists (discovery responses) are surfaced raw with the per-record length noted; an opcode outside the decoded set is named (or reported by value) with its body raw. Native ‚Äî a byte read + an opcode dispatch + handle/UUID reads, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The Read Request (handle), the Read-By-Group-Type service discovery (start/end + Primary-Service UUID), the Write Request (handle + value), the Notification, the Error Response (request opcode + error), the Exchange-MTU and the 128-bit-UUID Read-By-Type unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/att`. Registered as `bt_att_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 599‚Üí600.
- `bt_smp_decode` Bluetooth LE SMP (Security Manager Protocol / pairing) ‚Äî BLE-pairing security recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.605.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the project's Bluetooth-stack decode chain (`bt_hci_decode` ‚Üí `bt_l2cap_decode` ‚Üí this). SMP, carried on L2CAP CID 0x0006, is where BLE security is established (or fails to be): the **Pairing Request / Response** exchange negotiates the pairing **method** and the keys to distribute, and the choice of method determines MITM protection. A captured SMP exchange is the recon headline for **BLE-pairing security**: it reveals each side's **IO capability**, whether **MITM protection** is requested, whether **LE Secure Connections** (vs the weaker Legacy pairing) is used, the **max encryption key size**, and which long-term / identity / signing keys are distributed ‚Äî answering "is this pairing **Just Works** (no MITM protection, trivially interceptable) or authenticated?". Decodes the SMP code; for Pairing Request/Response/Security Request the IO capability, OOB flag, AuthReq (bonding / MITM / Secure Connections / keypress), max key size and the initiator/responder key-distribution masks, with a derived **security-posture** note; the Pairing Failed reason; and the Identity Address (with the LE‚ÜíMSB-first BD_ADDR fix); key material (LTK / IRK / CSRK / Confirm / Random / public key) is surfaced raw. **No confidently-wrong output**: the SMP codes, IO-capability values, AuthReq bit-fields, key-distribution flags and Pairing-Failed reasons follow the Bluetooth Core specification (Vol 3 Part H); the posture note is derived only from the unambiguous AuthReq bits (MITM / Secure Connections) on the decoded PDU ‚Äî the exact Legacy method (Just Works vs Passkey vs OOB) also depends on **both** sides' IO capabilities, so the note states the single-PDU posture rather than over-claiming the method. Native ‚Äî a byte read + bit-field decode + small tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The authenticated Pairing Request (MITM+SC), the Just-Works Pairing Request (Legacy, no MITM), the Pairing Failed reason, the Security Request AuthReq, the Identity Address and the raw key material unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/smp`. Registered as `bt_smp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 598‚Üí599.
- `bt_l2cap_decode` Bluetooth L2CAP (channel-mux layer) ‚Äî Bluetooth-stack recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.604.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **bridge** between `bt_hci_decode` (the HCI transport below, v0.603) and the project's BLE / GATT tooling (above). L2CAP is the channel-multiplexing layer that rides inside HCI ACL data and carries the higher Bluetooth protocols; an L2CAP frame's **Channel ID (CID)** selects the protocol ‚Äî the **signaling** channel (connection / configuration / LE connection-parameter-update and credit-based-connection requests), **ATT** (the Attribute Protocol behind GATT), **SMP** (the Security Manager ‚Äî BLE pairing), or a dynamic channel. Decoding an L2CAP frame from a btsnoop / HCI-ACL capture reveals which Bluetooth sub-protocol is in flight and, for the signaling / ATT / SMP channels, the specific operation ‚Äî a GATT read / write / notification, a pairing request, a connection-parameter update. **No confidently-wrong output**: the basic-header layout, the fixed CIDs, the L2CAP signaling codes, the ATT opcodes and the SMP codes follow the Bluetooth Core specification; the channel is dispatched by CID, the signaling code / ATT opcode / SMP code is named from the spec tables, and everything past the named opcode (the per-operation parameters) is surfaced as **raw hex**; an unknown signaling code / ATT opcode / SMP code is reported by value, and a frame shorter than the 4-byte basic header is reported, not guessed. Native ‚Äî a byte read + a CID dispatch + opcode tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The ATT Read-Request + Notification (CID 0x0004), the SMP Pairing-Request (CID 0x0006), the LE-Signaling Connection-Parameter-Update (CID 0x0005), the dynamic-CID and unknown-ATT-opcode and truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/l2cap`. Registered as `bt_l2cap_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 597‚Üí598.
- `bt_hci_decode` Bluetooth HCI (Host Controller Interface / H4) ‚Äî Bluetooth-stack / btsnoop recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.603.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the transport layer beneath the project's BLE decoders (`internal/ble`, `btuuid`, the GATT / advertising tooling) and the **offline-decode companion to the live `bt_hci_info`**. HCI is the transport between a Bluetooth host stack and its controller, and exactly what a **btsnoop / hcidump** capture contains ‚Äî every Bluetooth and BLE operation passes through it, so decoding an HCI capture is the foundational view of what a host (or an attacker's host) is doing: scanning, advertising, connecting, reading a remote's features, setting advertising data. A captured HCI packet identifies the **operation** ‚Äî a **command** (with its OGF group + opcode, e.g. LE Set Scan Enable / LE Create Connection / LE Set Advertising Data / Reset), an **event** (Command Complete / Command Status ‚Äî both naming the embedded command opcode ‚Äî Disconnection Complete, or an **LE Meta** sub-event such as an Advertising Report or Connection Complete), or an **ACL** data fragment (with its connection handle + PB/BC flags). **No confidently-wrong output**: the H4 transport indicators, the OGF groups, the well-known command opcodes, the event codes and the LE-Meta sub-event codes follow the Bluetooth Core specification (scapy's HCI type field carries non-standard extras, so the spec is the authority); the well-known opcodes / events are named, an opcode outside the named set is reported by its **OGF group + OCF** (never guessed) and an unknown event by code, and the command / event **parameters are surfaced as raw hex** (per-command) except the unambiguous Command Complete/Status embedded opcode and the LE-Meta sub-event code. Native ‚Äî a byte read + bit-field splits + opcode/event tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The Reset + LE-Set-Scan-Enable commands (OGF/OCF), the Command Complete (embedded Reset opcode), the LE Meta Advertising Report sub-event, the ACL handle/flags, the unknown-opcode OGF/OCF fallback and the truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/hci`. Registered as `bt_hci_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 596‚Üí597.
- `pmbus_decode` PMBus (Power Management Bus over SMBus/I2C) ‚Äî power-rail / PMFault recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.602.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, a hardware-bus member alongside `spi_flash_decode` / `internal/jtag` / `internal/buspirate`, pairing with `i2c_scan`. PMBus is the SMBus/I2C command set that PSUs, voltage regulators (VRMs), battery chargers and hot-swap controllers expose to set and read their power rails ‚Äî and a real, current **hardware-attack surface**: the 2023 **PMFault** research showed that writing the PSU's **VOUT_COMMAND / OPERATION** over PMBus can **overvolt** a server's CPU rail to induce faults. A captured PMBus transaction (from an I2C/SMBus sniffer) is decoded into the **command** ‚Äî a voltage-setting OPERATION / VOUT_COMMAND / VOUT_MARGIN / fault-limit write (the attack-relevant operations, **flagged**), a READ_VIN / READ_IOUT / READ_TEMPERATURE telemetry read (with the decoded physical value), a STATUS query (with the decoded fault bits), or a manufacturer-ID query. **No confidently-wrong output**: the decoded command codes are the PMBus-specification standard set; a code outside it is reported as **unknown / manufacturer-specific** rather than guessed; the **LINEAR11** decode (deterministic two's-complement exponent √ó mantissa) is applied only to the LINEAR11-defined commands (current / power / temperature / input-voltage reads), while **VOUT** values (ULINEAR16, scaled by the device's VOUT_MODE exponent which is not on the wire) are surfaced raw with a note, and the STATUS bit-fields are decoded from the spec. Native ‚Äî a byte read + an opcode table + bit/float decodes, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The READ_VIN (12 V) + READ_TEMPERATURE (25 ¬∞C) LINEAR11 decodes (including a negative READ_IOUT ‚àí16 A), the VOUT_COMMAND + OPERATION security flags, the STATUS_BYTE / STATUS_WORD fault bits and the unknown-command case unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/pmbus`. Registered as `pmbus_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 595‚Üí596.
- `spi_flash_decode` SPI NOR flash transactions (command set + JEDEC RDID) ‚Äî chip-dump / firmware-extraction recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.601.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **chip-dump member** of the project's hardware-bus tooling (`internal/jtag`, `internal/buspirate`), decoding what `buspirate_spi_dump` captures. SPI NOR flash chips hold firmware on embedded devices, routers, IoT gear and the Flipper's own targets, and reading the chip (a **firmware dump**) is a core hardware-hacking activity: issue **RDID** (0x9F) to identify the chip, then **READ** (0x03) / FAST_READ (0x0B) to dump it (or WREN + PAGE_PROGRAM / ERASE to write). A captured SPI transaction is decoded into the **command name**, the **24-bit address** of a read / program / erase, and ‚Äî for RDID ‚Äî the **JEDEC manufacturer** (Winbond / Macronix / Micron / GigaDevice / ISSI / Spansion / SST / ‚Ä¶) and the typical **capacity**, which identifies the chip and its size (e.g. EF 40 18 = Winbond W25Q128, 16 MB). **No confidently-wrong output**: the decoded command opcodes are the universal / JEDEC-standard SPI NOR set (RDID, READ, FAST_READ, PAGE_PROGRAM, the erases, the status-register and write-enable commands, the dual/quad reads, SFDP, reset, 4-byte-address mode) shared across the major vendors and verified against their datasheets; an opcode outside the set is reported as **unknown / vendor-specific** rather than guessed; the RDID manufacturer byte is named from the well-known single-byte SPI manufacturer codes (unknown otherwise), and the capacity is the common **2^code** encoding labelled 'typical' (a few vendors deviate) with the raw memory-type and capacity bytes surfaced alongside. Native ‚Äî a byte read + an opcode lookup + a manufacturer table, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The Winbond + Macronix RDID, the READ / Sector-Erase / Page-Program addresses, the WREN (no address), the unknown-command and the RDID-without-readback cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/spiflash`. Registered as `spi_flash_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 594‚Üí595.
- `usb_pd_decode` USB Power Delivery (USB-C CC-line power negotiation) ‚Äî malicious-charger / cable recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.600.0 ‚Äî **new tool** extending the project's USB analysis stack (`usb_descriptor_decode`, `usb_hid_report_descriptor_decode`, `usbhid`) into **power delivery**, an emerging **hardware-attack surface**: a malicious charger or PD-capable cable can advertise bogus power capabilities, drive a sink to request out-of-spec voltage, or carry vendor-defined messages that trigger device-specific behaviour ‚Äî so a captured PD exchange (from a CC-line analyzer) is real recon. A USB-PD message identifies the **negotiation step** ‚Äî a **Source/Sink Capabilities** advertisement (and the offered voltages/currents), a Request, an Accept/Reject/PS_RDY, a role swap, a Vendor-Defined Message. Decodes the 16-bit header (message type ‚Äî with the control-vs-data dispatch driven by the data-object count ‚Äî spec revision, power/data roles, message id, extended flag) and, for Source/Sink Capabilities, each Power Data Object: **Fixed** (voltage + max current + the role flags), **Variable** and **Battery** (voltage range + current). **No confidently-wrong output**: the header bit layout, the control- and data-message type tables and the Fixed / Variable / Battery PDO layouts follow the USB Power Delivery specification ‚Äî deterministic and byte-checkable against spec-built PDOs (e.g. 5 V @ 3 A); only the standardised fields are decoded, an **Augmented PDO (PPS / AVS)** is surfaced by type with its 32-bit value raw, and the **Request RDO**, BIST, Vendor-Defined and other data messages' objects are surfaced as **raw hex** (their layouts are position-dependent and would be confidently-wrong without the prior Capabilities context). Native ‚Äî a bit-field read + a per-message-type walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The GoodCRC control message, the Source_Capabilities Fixed PDO (5 V/3 A + DRP/USB-comms flags), the Variable PDO (5‚Äì9 V / 2 A), the Request RDO (surfaced raw) and the truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/usbpd`. Registered as `usb_pd_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 593‚Üí594.
- `usb_hid_report_descriptor_decode` USB HID Report Descriptor (USB HID 1.11 ¬ß6.2.2) ‚Äî HID device-identity + BadUSB recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.599.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **deepest layer of USB device identity**, completing the project's USB analysis stack: `usb_descriptor_decode` (the device / interface / endpoint identity), this (the HID **usage** the device claims), and `usbhid` (the report **data** the device then sends). The HID Report Descriptor is the item-based structure a HID device returns to declare **what it is** ‚Äî its usage (keyboard / mouse / gamepad / vendor-defined), its collections, and the size/shape of its input/output/feature reports. It is the definitive **BadUSB tell**: a device whose report descriptor declares a **Generic Desktop / Keyboard** usage with a standard input report is a keyboard ‚Äî so a flash drive or 'charging cable' whose HID report descriptor declares a keyboard is a keystroke injector (Rubber Ducky / Bash Bunny / O.MG cable), which is flagged. Decodes each item ‚Äî **Main** (Input / Output / Feature with the decoded data-flag bits, Collection with its type, End Collection), **Global** (Usage Page with its name, Logical/Physical Min/Max, Report Size / ID / Count, Push / Pop), **Local** (Usage with its name, Usage Min/Max, ‚Ä¶) and long items ‚Äî and summarises the **declared usages** (e.g. 'Generic Desktop / Keyboard'). **No confidently-wrong output**: the item encoding, the Main / Global / Local tag tables, the Collection types and the Input/Output/Feature data-flag bits follow the USB HID 1.11 specification ‚Äî deterministic and byte-checkable against the canonical boot-keyboard report descriptor; usage-page and usage **values** are a vast, vendor-extensible registry, so only the well-known usage pages and the Generic-Desktop usages are named, any other usage page / usage is **surfaced by value** (never guessed), and a truncated item stops the walk. Native ‚Äî a byte walk + bit-field reads + tag-name tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The boot-keyboard descriptor (Usage Page / Usage / Application Collection + BadUSB flag), the Input data-flag bits (Data,Variable,Absolute), the mouse-descriptor (no BadUSB note), the Report Size/Count values and the truncated-item stop unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/hidreport`. Registered as `usb_hid_report_descriptor_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 592‚Üí593.
- `usb_descriptor_decode` USB descriptors (device / config / interface / endpoint / HID / string) ‚Äî USB device-fingerprinting + BadUSB recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.598.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **device-fingerprinting and BadUSB-analysis companion** to the project's `usbhid` (HID report decode) and BadUSB tooling (`badusb_*`, `usb_badusb_classify`). USB descriptors are the self-describing structures a device returns during enumeration; a captured blob (from `lsusb -v`, a USB sniffer, or the device) identifies the device ‚Äî its **idVendor / idProduct** (VID:PID fingerprint), its device and per-interface **class** (HID / Mass Storage / CDC / ‚Ä¶) and its endpoints. This is real recon: an unexpected **HID boot-keyboard interface** (class 3 / subclass 1 / protocol 1) is the signature of a **BadUSB / rubber-ducky** keystroke injector masquerading as a peripheral, and a **composite device** mixing (say) a keyboard with mass storage is a classic malicious-USB pattern ‚Äî **both are flagged**. Decodes the Device descriptor (USB version, class, VID:PID, device version, configuration count), the Configuration descriptor (total length, interface count, power attributes, max power), the Interface descriptor (number, class + subclass/protocol ‚Äî HID boot keyboard/mouse named), the Endpoint descriptor (address + direction, transfer type, max packet size, interval), the String descriptor (UTF-16LE) and the Interface-Association descriptor; a full configuration blob is walked descriptor-by-descriptor. **No confidently-wrong output**: the descriptor layouts and the USB-IF base class codes follow the USB specification (and match `lsusb`) ‚Äî deterministic and byte-checkable against spec-built vectors; a class-specific (0x24/0x25) or unknown descriptor type is surfaced by type with its body as **raw hex** (the class-specific layouts are many and vendor-defined), and a bLength that is zero or overruns the buffer stops the walk rather than guessing. Native ‚Äî a byte-slice walk + field reads + a class-code lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The device descriptor (VID 0x046A / PID 0x889F), the HID-keyboard config blob (BadUSB flag), the composite HID+Mass-Storage device (composite flag), the UTF-16 string descriptor and the malformed-length / truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/usbdesc`. Registered as `usb_descriptor_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 591‚Üí592.
- `erspan_decode` inner-frame decode + IP chaining ‚Äî full mirrored-traffic decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.597.0 ‚Äî **enhancement** to `erspan_decode`, extending the tunnel-decap family's **chain-to-inner-decoder** convention (cf. `gre`/`vxlan`/`geneve`/`nsh`‚Üí`ipdecode`) to ERSPAN, which was the last tunnel decoder surfacing its inner payload raw. ERSPAN (Encapsulated Remote SPAN) always encapsulates a **mirrored Ethernet frame** ‚Äî its whole purpose ‚Äî so the inner is reliably an Ethernet frame, and a capture is itself a finding (a SPAN/port-mirror session is exporting traffic over GRE ‚Äî lawful intercept, an IDS feed, or an attacker exfiltrating mirrored traffic). The mirrored frame is now **decoded inline**: dst/src MAC + EtherType, **one 802.1Q VLAN tag peeled**, and the IPv4/IPv6 payload **chained to `internal/ipdecode`** ‚Äî so the mirrored traffic (the recon headline: *what is being monitored*) is visible in one shot rather than requiring a second tool call. **No confidently-wrong output**: the raw `mirrored_frame_hex` is kept alongside the decoded fields, a non-IP EtherType leaves it raw (no IP chaining), and a failed IP parse degrades to an `inner_decode_error` + the raw hex (same shape as `nsh`). Native ‚Äî an internal decoder call, stdlib only (`net` for MAC formatting), no new go.mod dep (no import cycle: `ipdecode` does not import `erspan`). The Type-II inner IPv4 (dst/src MAC + chained packet) and the 802.1Q-tagged inner (VLAN 100 peel) are unit-pinned; existing ERSPAN header tests stay green; fuzz-clean. Not a new tool (no registry change) ‚Äî `erspan_decode` already Low risk; registry unchanged at 591. `internal/erspan`.
- `isotp_decode` UDS chaining for the reassembled PDU ‚Äî full ISO-TP‚ÜíUDS decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.596.0 ‚Äî **enhancement** to `isotp_decode`, the **CAN-side parallel to the v0.595 DoIP‚ÜíUDS chaining**: ISO-TP (ISO 15765-2) is the CAN transport for diagnostics, just as DoIP is the Ethernet transport. When the reassembly is **complete** (a Single Frame, or a First + Consecutive frames sequence), the application PDU is now **chained to the UDS decoder inline** (`internal/uds.DecodeBytes`) ‚Äî so the diagnostic service (ReadDataByIdentifier, SecurityAccess, RoutineControl, ECUReset, ‚Ä¶) is decoded in one shot, which is the recon headline of the most common automotive diagnostic capture (UDS-over-ISO-TP on classic CAN). Follows the project's **chain-to-inner-decoder** convention (cf. `nsh`/`gre`‚Üí`ipdecode`, `doip`‚Üí`uds`). **No confidently-wrong output**: ISO-TP is a **generic transport** (it also carries KWP2000 / OBD-II / raw data), so the UDS interpretation is an explicitly-**hedged best effort** flagged with a note, the raw `payload_hex` is kept alongside the structured `uds` object for handing to `obd2_*` / `kwp_decode` when the application protocol is not UDS, and a non-UDS payload degrades to an unknown-service result (or `uds_decode_error`); chaining only happens on a complete reassembly (never on a fragment). Native ‚Äî an internal decoder call, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (no import cycle: `uds` does not import `isotp`). The Single-Frame (ReadDataByIdentifier request, DID 0xF190) and the multi-frame FF+CF (positive-response normalised to base service 0x22 + positive_response direction) chains are unit-pinned; existing ISO-TP tests stay green; fuzz-clean. Not a new tool (no registry change) ‚Äî `isotp_decode` already Low risk; registry unchanged at 591. `internal/isotp`.
- `doip_decode` UDS chaining for diagnostic messages ‚Äî full DoIP‚ÜíUDS decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.595.0 ‚Äî **enhancement** to `doip_decode` (v0.593): a DoIP **diagnostic message** (payload type 0x8001) carries a UDS message as its user data, which v0.593 surfaced as raw hex with a "chain to uds_decode" note. It is now **chained to the UDS decoder** (`internal/uds.DecodeBytes`) so the diagnostic service is decoded **inline** ‚Äî the recon headline of a DoIP diagnostic capture (ReadDataByIdentifier, SecurityAccess, RoutineControl, ECUReset, ‚Ä¶) is now visible in one shot rather than requiring a second tool call. Follows the project's established **chain-to-inner-decoder** convention (cf. `nsh` / `gre` / `sflow` ‚Üí `ipdecode`): the raw `uds_payload_hex` is kept alongside the structured `uds` object, and a UDS decode failure degrades to a `uds_decode_error` + the raw hex (no confidently-wrong output). Native ‚Äî an internal decoder call, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (no import cycle: `uds` does not import `doip`). The diagnostic-message test now asserts the chained UDS service (10 03 ‚Üí DiagnosticSessionControl); existing DoIP tests stay green; fuzz-clean. Not a new tool (no registry change) ‚Äî `doip_decode` already Low risk; registry unchanged at 591. `internal/doip`.
- `ccp_decode` CCP ‚Äî CAN Calibration Protocol ‚Äî CAN-native ECU calibration/flash-bus recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.594.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **CAN-native predecessor of XCP** (`xcp_decode`) and the CAN-bus sibling in the project's automotive family (`uds_decode`, `kwp_decode`, `obd2_*`, `doip_decode`, `isotp_decode`, `canbus_fd_decode`). CCP is the ASAM protocol an ECU calibration tool uses to read and write an ECU's memory over CAN ‚Äî connect to a station, DAQ measurement, **download** calibration data, **flash** (PROGRAM) ‚Äî and is still in production ECUs (especially older GM / European powertrain modules). It is a real **automotive-security target**: it exposes direct ECU memory **UPLOAD** (read) / **DNLOAD** (write) and a **PROGRAM / CLEAR_MEMORY** flash sequence, with the only access control being the optional **GET_SEED / UNLOCK** seed-and-key handshake ‚Äî so an attacker on the CAN bus who speaks CCP can exfiltrate calibration/firmware, tamper with calibration, or reflash the ECU. A captured CCP frame identifies the **operation** ‚Äî a session CONNECT (and the target station address), a SEED & KEY auth, a memory UPLOAD, a calibration DNLOAD, a PROGRAM flash ‚Äî or, on the slave side, the Command Return Message (with its return code), an event, or DAQ measurement data; security-relevant commands (auth / memory read / memory write / flash) are flagged. **No confidently-wrong output**: the command table and the return-code table are **code-generated from scapy's authoritative CCP layer** (`scapy.contrib.automotive.ccp`); like XCP, CCP is **direction-dependent** (a command byte master ‚Üí slave and a DTO packet id slave ‚Üí master share the same byte space), so the caller supplies the direction and, without it, the command interpretation is used and the ambiguity is noted; only the command byte / packet id, the counter, the return code and (for CONNECT) the little-endian station address are decoded, the remaining parameters surfaced as **raw hex** (command-specific, address-granularity-dependent), never reinterpreted. Native ‚Äî a byte lookup + a small return-code table, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The CONNECT (LE station address + security) / GET_SEED / UPLOAD / PROGRAM commands, the CRM (ack / access-denied), the event + DAQ-DTO responses, the direction-ambiguity note and the bad-direction / truncation rejections unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/ccp`. Registered as `ccp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 590‚Üí591.
- `doip_decode` DoIP ‚Äî Diagnostics over Internet Protocol (ISO 13400) ‚Äî vehicle Ethernet-diagnostics recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.593.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the project's automotive family (`uds_decode`, `kwp_decode`, `obd2_*`, `xcp_decode`, `isotp_decode`, `canbus_fd_decode`). DoIP is the Ethernet/IP transport that carries **vehicle diagnostics (UDS)** in modern cars, replacing the OBD-II-over-CAN link: a tester reaches the vehicle's diagnostic gateway over TCP/UDP 13400, discovers it (vehicle identification), authorises a session (routing activation), then tunnels UDS diagnostic messages to the ECUs. DoIP is a real, growing **automotive-security target**: it is the network entry point to the whole diagnostic surface, the vehicle-identification response broadcasts the **VIN / EID / GID / logical address** (asset identification), and routing activation is the access-control gate (its "denied due to missing authentication" response reveals the posture). Decodes the 8-byte header (protocol version + validated inverse version + payload type + length) and the payload-type body: vehicle identification request/response (VIN + EID + GID + logical address + further-action + VIN/GID-sync status), routing activation request (source address + activation type) / response (tester + entity logical addresses + the response code), alive check, DoIP entity status (node type + socket counts), diagnostic power mode, and the diagnostic message / ACK / NACK ‚Äî for which the **source + target addresses and the UDS payload** are surfaced (the UDS payload as raw hex for handoff to `uds_decode`). **No confidently-wrong output**: the header layout, the payload-type table and the sub-code tables (generic NACK, routing-activation type / response, further-action, VIN/GID status, diagnostic NACK) are **code-generated from scapy's authoritative DoIP layer** (`scapy.contrib.automotive.doip`) and verified field-for-field against ISO 13400 vectors; only standardised fields are decoded, the diagnostic-message user data is surfaced raw (never reinterpreted), the inverse-version byte is validated (one's-complement of the version), and a declared payload length disagreeing with the buffer or a body too short for the payload type is reported not guessed. Native ‚Äî a byte-slice walk + a payload-type lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The vehicle announcement (VIN/EID/GID), routing-activation request + response (denied-missing-auth), the diagnostic message (UDS payload), the generic + diagnostic NACKs and the invalid-inverse-version / truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/doip`. Registered as `doip_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 589‚Üí590.
- `xcp_decode` ASAM XCP ‚Äî Universal Measurement and Calibration Protocol ‚Äî ECU calibration/flash-bus recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.592.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the project's automotive family (`uds_decode`, `kwp_decode`, `obd2_*`, `isotp_decode`, `canbus_fd_decode`). XCP is the master/slave protocol an ECU calibration tool uses to **read and write an ECU's memory**: measurement (DAQ / STIM), calibration (download) and **flash programming** (PROGRAM); it runs over CAN (XCP-on-CAN), Ethernet, FlexRay and others. XCP is a real **automotive-security target**: it exposes direct ECU memory **UPLOAD** (read) / **DOWNLOAD** (write) and a **PROGRAM** reflash sequence, and access protection is the optional **SEED & KEY** (GET_SEED / UNLOCK) handshake that is frequently weak or absent ‚Äî so an attacker on the bus who speaks XCP can exfiltrate calibration/firmware, tamper with calibration values, or reflash the ECU. A captured XCP packet identifies the **operation** ‚Äî a session CONNECT, a SEED & KEY auth, a memory UPLOAD, a calibration DOWNLOAD, a PROGRAM flash sequence ‚Äî or, on the slave side, the positive response (RES), the negative response (ERR + decoded error code), an event (EV) or a service request (SERV); the security-relevant commands (auth / memory read / memory write / flash) are flagged. **No confidently-wrong output**: the command-code table (0xC7-0xFF), the error-code table and the event-code table are **code-generated from scapy's authoritative XCP layer** (`scapy.contrib.automotive.xcp`); XCP is **direction-dependent** (the same PID 0xFC-0xFF is a command master ‚Üí slave but a response/event/service class slave ‚Üí master), so the caller supplies the direction and, without it, the command interpretation is used and the ambiguity is noted; only the PID + (for ERR/EV) the sub-code are decoded, the command/response parameters are surfaced as **raw hex** (their layout is command-specific and address-granularity-dependent), never reinterpreted. Native ‚Äî a byte lookup + small sub-code tables, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The CONNECT / GET_SEED / UPLOAD / PROGRAM commands (with security flags), the ERR (access-denied) / EV (session-terminated) / RES responses, the STIM-vs-DAQ direction split, the direction-ambiguity note and the bad-direction / truncation rejections unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/xcp`. Registered as `xcp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 588‚Üí589.
- `nfc_tcl_decode` ISO/IEC 14443-4 T=CL block transmission protocol ‚Äî NFC transport-layer recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.591.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **T=CL transport member** of the project's NFC family, completing the 14443 stack: ATQA + SAK identify the card (`nfc_iso14443a_identify`), the ATS advertises its capabilities (same tool, v0.590), **T=CL frames the exchange (this tool)**, and the APDUs inside are decoded by the ISO 7816 APDU tools. T=CL is the half-duplex block transmission protocol that carries APDUs between a contactless reader (PCD) and a Type-4 proximity card (PICC) after activation. Every T=CL frame starts with a **Protocol Control Byte (PCB)** selecting one of three block types: an **I-block** (information ‚Äî carries an APDU, possibly chained), an **R-block** (receive-ready ‚Äî ACK / NAK for chaining flow control) or an **S-block** (supervisory ‚Äî WTX waiting-time-extension or DESELECT). Decoding the PCB of a captured T=CL exchange reveals the block type, the block number / chaining state, the CID (card identifier) and NAD (node address) usage, the R-block ACK/NAK and the S-block WTX/DESELECT, and lifts out the **INF field** (the APDU fragment) for handoff to the APDU decoder. **No confidently-wrong output**: the PCB coding follows ISO 14443-4 ¬ß7.1 and was reconciled against the canonical PCB values used by Proxmark / libnfc (I-block 0x02 / chaining 0x12, R(ACK) 0xA2 / R(NAK) 0xB2, S(DESELECT) 0xC2 / S(WTX) 0xF2, CID bit 0x08); the block type is taken from the top two bits (00 = I, 10 = R, 11 = S; 01 is RFU and reported as such); only the standardised PCB + CID + NAD + S(WTX) parameter are decoded, the **INF field (the APDU fragment or proprietary payload) is surfaced as raw hex** for handoff to the APDU decoder (never reinterpreted here), and a PCB with wrong fixed bits or a frame truncated before a promised CID / NAD byte is reported not guessed. Native ‚Äî a bit read + two optional byte reads, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The I-block (with APDU / chaining / CID / NAD), R(ACK) / R(NAK) / R(ACK)+CID, S(DESELECT) / S(WTX), the RFU prefix, and the invalid-fixed-bit / truncation rejections unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/tcl`. Registered as `nfc_tcl_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 587‚Üí588.
- `nfc_iso14443a_identify` ATS interface-byte decode to parity with Type B (ISO 14443-4 ¬ß5.2) ‚Äî NFC card-capability recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.590.0 ‚Äî **enhancement** to the existing `nfc_iso14443a_identify`, closing a consistency gap: the Type-A ATS (Answer To Select) decode previously stopped at the TA1/TB1/TC1 **presence flags** (surfacing the interface bytes as raw hex), while the Type-B `nfc_iso14443b_decode` sibling already fully decoded the equivalent ATQB protocol-info (FSCI / FWI / bit-rate / NAD / CID). Now the Type-A ATS is decoded to **parity**: the **TA(1) bit-rate capability** (the divisors supported each direction ‚Äî 106 / 212 / 424 / 848 kbit/s, plus the same-both-directions flag), the **TB(1)** FWI ‚Üí FWT frame-waiting time and SFGI ‚Üí SFGT start-up-guard time, and the **TC(1)** NAD / CID protocol options ‚Äî alongside the existing FSCI ‚Üí FSC max-frame-size and the historical bytes (hex + ASCII, which often fingerprint the card OS). This deepens NFC card-capability recon: the ATS reveals a Type-4 card's speed, timing and protocol options, and the historical bytes are a card fingerprint (e.g. the DESFire EV1 ATS `06 75 77 81 02 80`). **No confidently-wrong output**: all fields follow ISO 14443-4 ¬ß5.2.2/¬ß5.2.4/¬ß5.2.5 (the FWT/SFGT base constant 0.302064 ms √ó 2^n, fc = 13.56 MHz, matches the Type-B decoder); a declared TL exceeding the buffer is reported, and RFC/RFU-range values degrade gracefully. Native ‚Äî bitfield decode, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The DESFire-EV1 ATS (TA1 0x77 asymmetric DS/DR + TB1 0x81 FWI/SFGI + TC1 0x02 CID) and the historical-bytes / FSCI cases are unit-pinned; existing tests stay green. Not a new tool (no registry change) ‚Äî `nfc_iso14443a_identify` already Low risk; registry unchanged at 587. `internal/iso14443a`.
- `nfc_felica_decode` FeliCa / NFC-F / NFC Forum Type 3 (JIS X 6319-4) ‚Äî transit + payment card recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.589.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **NFC-F member** of the project's NFC family (alongside the type 2 / 4A / 4B / V decoders) and the notable missing NFC tag type. FeliCa is the Sony contactless protocol behind the huge **transit and payment** deployments of East Asia (Suica / PASMO, Octopus, EZ-Link, nanaco, Edy, WAON) and the NFC Forum Type 3 Tag ‚Äî the Flipper Zero and Proxmark read it. A captured FeliCa frame is **NFC reconnaissance**: the polling response carries the card's **IDm** (Manufacture ID ‚Äî the unique identifier used for anti-collision and access logging), its **PMm** (Manufacture Parameter ‚Äî IC type + timing) and the **System Code** that names the on-card application system (transit / payment / NDEF / FeliCa Lite-S); a Read Without Encryption response carries the requested **block data**. Decodes the frame: LEN, the command/response code + name (Polling, Request Service, Read/Write Without Encryption, Request System Code, Authentication, ‚Ä¶), the IDm (+ 2-byte manufacturer code), the PMm (+ IC code), the polling System Code, the read status flags + block data, and the Request-System-Code list. **No confidently-wrong output**: the frame layout + code table follow the authoritative Sony FeliCa Card User's Manual / JIS X 6319-4 ‚Äî **there is no scapy model for FeliCa**, so verification is by the deterministic, byte-checkable structural walk against spec-built vectors (the same approach as `goose_decode` / `sampled_values_decode`); only the standardised deterministic fields are decoded, a handful of **well-known System Codes are named** and any other System Code / IC code / unhandled command body is surfaced as **raw hex** (the per-vendor value spaces are not enumerated), a declared LEN that disagrees with the buffer or a body too short for the code's fixed fields is reported not guessed, and the **Polling command (which uniquely has no IDm) is special-cased**. Native ‚Äî a byte-slice walk + a code lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The polling command, polling response (IDm/PMm/system-code NDEF), Read-Without-Encryption success (block data) + error (status flags), Request-System-Code response, generic-command IDm-surface, and unknown-code / truncation rejections unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/felica`. Registered as `nfc_felica_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 586‚Üí587.
- `esmc_decode` ESMC ‚Äî Ethernet Synchronization Messaging Channel / SyncE (ITU-T G.8264, EtherType 0x8809 subtype 0x0A) ‚Äî timing-network recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.588.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **frequency-sync companion to `ptpv2_decode`** (PTP / IEEE 1588 phase/time sync). SyncE distributes a physical-layer frequency reference across an Ethernet network (the way SDH/SONET did over TDM); ESMC is the small Slow-Protocol frame that advertises the **Synchronization Status Message (SSM)** ‚Äî the **Quality Level (QL)** of the clock each node is traceable to. Together ESMC + PTP carry the **timing plane** that 5G fronthaul, power-grid teleprotection and broadcast depend on, and timing is an emerging **attack surface** ‚Äî degrading or spoofing the advertised QL can push a network onto a worse clock or trigger a sync-loss reconfiguration ‚Äî so a captured ESMC frame reveals the timing hierarchy: the advertised clock **Quality Level** (PRC / SSU / EEC / DNU), whether the frame is a periodic **information** heartbeat or an **event** (a QL change), and (in the enhanced TLV) the source clock identity. Decodes the 10-byte header (subtype, ITU OUI, ITU subtype, version, event flag) and the TLV stream (Quality Level + Enhanced Quality Level). **No confidently-wrong output**: the header + QL / Enhanced-QL TLVs were verified field-for-field against scapy's ESMC layer (`scapy.contrib.esmc`); the one genuine ambiguity is the SSM-code ‚Üí QL name ‚Äî ITU-T G.781 defines option tables (Option I = ETSI/SDH, Option II = ANSI/SONET) that assign **different** names to the same 4-bit code, and the in-use option is a deployment setting **not carried on the wire**, so the raw SSM code is surfaced together with **both** the Option-I and Option-II names rather than a confidently-wrong single answer; a non-ESMC Slow-Protocol subtype is rejected and a malformed TLV stops the walk. Native ‚Äî a byte/bit read + a TLV walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The information-frame (QL-PRC, Option I) + event-frame (QL-DNU, both options) + non-ESMC-subtype rejection + no-TLV / truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/esmc`. Registered as `esmc_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 585‚Üí586.
- `sampled_values_decode` IEC 61850-9-2 / 9-2LE Sampled Values (SV / SMV, EtherType 0x88BA) ‚Äî substation process-bus recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.587.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **sampled-measurement sibling of `goose_decode`** (explicitly flagged out-of-scope in the goose package doc) and the SV member of the project's OT/ICS decoder family. SV is the substation-automation multicast that streams digitised **current and voltage samples** from a **merging unit** to the protection / measurement IEDs over the process bus, directly over Ethernet (no IP / no UDP) at a high fixed sample rate. It is a real **substation-security target**: SV is unauthenticated by default, so an attacker on the process bus who injects forged SV frames ‚Äî replaying an old sample block or spoofing the **sample counter** ‚Äî can feed protection relays false current/voltage and trigger or block a trip (the SV-injection attack class). A captured SV frame identifies the **stream** (svID ‚Äî the merging unit), the **sample counter** (smpCnt ‚Äî the per-sample sequence number replay / spoof attacks manipulate), the configuration revision, the **synchronisation source** (smpSynch ‚Äî whether GPS-disciplined), and surfaces the raw sampled-value block. Decodes the 8-byte APPID / length / reserved header and the ASN.1 BER savPdu (tag 0x60) ‚Üí seqASDU (0xA2) ‚Üí ASDUs (0x30): noASDU, the optional IEC 62351 security field (raw), and each ASDU's svID / datSet / smpCnt / confRev / refrTm / smpSynch (+ clock-source name) / smpRate / smpMod. **No confidently-wrong output**: the savPdu / ASDU tag layout follows the authoritative IEC 61850-9-2 ASN.1 (matching Wireshark's sv dissector) ‚Äî **there is no scapy model for SV (nor GOOSE)**, so verification is by the deterministic, byte-checkable BER tag/length/value walk against spec-built vectors; the **sampled-value data block itself (the `sample` field) is dataset-configuration-dependent and is surfaced as raw hex** (decoding individual channel values without the dataset definition would be confidently-wrong), exactly as `goose_decode` surfaces allData; the security field is surfaced raw; a missing 0x60 outer tag or a truncated TLV is reported, not guessed. Native ‚Äî a BER walk reusing the same approach as `internal/goose`, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The single-ASDU frame (svID / smpCnt / confRev / smpSynch=Global / raw sample), the two-ASDU frame with all optional fields (datSet / refrTm / smpRate) and the wrong-outer-tag / truncation rejections are unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/sv`. Registered as `sampled_values_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 584‚Üí585.
- `mld_decode` MLD ‚Äî Multicast Listener Discovery (RFC 2710 MLDv1 + RFC 3810 MLDv2) ‚Äî IPv6 multicast-membership recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.586.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **IPv6 companion** to the project's `igmp_decode` (v1/v2) and `igmpv3_decode` (IPv4 multicast), and the MLD member of the ICMPv6 family alongside `ndp_decode`. MLD is the IPv6 multicast-group membership protocol carried in ICMPv6: a host emits an MLD **Report** to tell the on-link router which IPv6 multicast groups it wants to receive, and routers emit **Queries** to refresh that state. It is a **network-reconnaissance** source ‚Äî an MLD Report reveals exactly which multicast groups a host has joined (and, via the MLDv2 source-filter records, which senders it includes / excludes), exposing the host's multicast-based services: **mDNS / Bonjour** (ff02::fb), **LLMNR** (ff02::1:3), SSDP / UPnP, PTP, IPTV / streaming. Decodes the MLDv1 Query / Report / Done (max-response-delay + multicast address + general-query detection), the MLDv2 Query (the S / QRV / QQIC fields + querier source list) and the MLDv2 Report group records (record type ‚Äî MODE_IS_INCLUDE / EXCLUDE / CHANGE_TO_* / ALLOW_NEW_SOURCES / BLOCK_OLD_SOURCES ‚Äî multicast address + source list). **No confidently-wrong output**: the MLDv1 / MLDv2 layouts and the MLDv2 Max-Response-Code + QQIC floating-point encodings (RFC 3810 ¬ß5.1.3/¬ß5.1.9) were verified field-for-field against scapy's MLD layers (ICMPv6MLQuery / MLReport / MLDone / MLQuery2 / MLReport2 / MLDMultAddrRec) + RFC 2710 / RFC 3810 ‚Äî a **50-row MLDv2-Report differential** (random record types / groups / source lists) decoded identically, **zero mismatches**; a type-130 Query is dispatched to MLDv1 vs MLDv2 by length (RFC 3810 ¬ß8.1: MLDv2 ‚â• 28 bytes), a non-MLD ICMPv6 type is rejected, and the ICMPv6 checksum (computed over an IPv6 pseudo-header absent from a bare MLD capture) is surfaced as raw hex without a validity claim (matching `ndp_decode`). Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + two walks, stdlib only (net for IPv6 formatting), no new go.mod dep. The MLDv1 general query, v1 Report (LLMNR), v1 Done (mDNS), MLDv2 Query (S/QRV/QQIC + source), MLDv2 Report (with + without sources), the Max-Resp-Code float and the non-MLD rejection unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/mld`. Registered as `mld_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 583‚Üí584.
- `ndp_decode` SeND option decode + Type-13 mislabel fix (RFC 3971) ‚Äî IPv6 ND security-posture recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.585.0 ‚Äî **enhancement + bug fix** to the existing `ndp_decode`, deepening the project's IPv6 ND family (`ndp_decode` / `ipv6_eui64_recover` / `dhcpv6_decode`). **Bug fixed**: the NDP option type-name table mislabelled **option Type 13 as `Nonce`** ‚Äî per RFC 3971 ¬ß5.3.1/¬ß5.3.2 Type 13 is the **Timestamp** option and **Type 14** is the Nonce option (a confidently-wrong label, now corrected; the package doc carried the same error in two places). **Capability added**: the four SeND (SEcure Neighbor Discovery, RFC 3971) options are now field-decoded rather than surfaced raw ‚Äî **CGA** (Type 11: pad length + 16-byte modifier + 64-bit subnet prefix rendered as an IPv6 /64 + collision count + the DER public-key blob raw), **RSA Signature** (Type 12: the 16-byte SHA-1 key hash + the signature blob raw), **Timestamp** (Type 13: the 8-byte anti-replay value) and **Nonce** (Type 14). SeND is a real IPv6-security attack surface ‚Äî THC-IPv6's `sendpees6` floods a victim with bogus CGA/RSA options to exhaust its CPU ‚Äî so decoding the SeND framing surfaces whether ND is cryptographically secured (CGA present / RSA-signed / timestamped) and is the recon headline. **No confidently-wrong output**: the option framing was hand-built per the RFC ¬ß5 layouts and the Nonce / RSA-Signature / CGA framing cross-checked against `scapy.contrib.send`; **scapy's Timestamp field size is non-conformant** (4 bytes vs the RFC's 8), so the RFC layout is the authority for Type 13 and the public-key + signature blobs are surfaced raw (cryptographic CGA / signature validation is higher-level work). Native ‚Äî a TLV walk + fixed-field reads, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. The CGA / RSA-Signature / Timestamp / Nonce option decodes are unit-pinned and the corrected option-type-name table is asserted; fuzz-clean. `internal/ndp`. Not a new tool (no registry change) ‚Äî `ndp_decode` already Low risk; registry unchanged at 583.
- `icmp_extension_decode` ICMP multipart extension (RFC 4884) + MPLS Label Stack (RFC 4950) ‚Äî traceroute MPLS-topology recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.584.0 ‚Äî **new tool** pairing with the project's `icmp_packet_decode` and `mpls_decode`. When a router sends an ICMP **Time Exceeded** (TTL expired) or **Destination Unreachable** message, RFC 4884 lets it append an extension structure, and RFC 4950 defines the **MPLS Label Stack** object carrying the label stack the dropped packet was traversing ‚Äî so a **traceroute through an MPLS core** elicits Time-Exceeded messages whose extensions **leak the MPLS labels (and TTLs) at each hop**, exposing the label-switched path and the provider's MPLS topology the tunnel would otherwise hide (a real network-recon technique). RFC 5837 adds Interface Information / Identification objects (egress interface index / IP / name / MTU) that enumerate a router's interfaces. Decodes the 4-byte extension header (version + checksum) and walks the TLV objects; the **MPLS Label Stack object is fully decoded** into its 32-bit entries (label / traffic class / bottom-of-stack / TTL). **No confidently-wrong output**: the extension header, the object TLV framing and the MPLS object were verified field-for-field against scapy's ICMP-extensions layer + RFC 4950; the **Interface Information / Identification objects (RFC 5837) carry intricate conditional fields** (a bit-flagged c-type selecting an optional ifIndex / IP sub-object / length-framed ifName / MTU), so their payload is **deliberately surfaced as raw hex** with the class name rather than risk a wrong field decode ‚Äî the Extended Information and any unknown class likewise, and a malformed object length stops the walk and surfaces the remainder raw. Native ‚Äî a byte walk + a bit-field read, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Extension header + TLV framing + MPLS object verified field-for-field against scapy** (`scapy.contrib.icmp_extensions` + `scapy.contrib.mpls`) ‚Äî the single-label (label 16000) + the two-label stack (outer 100/TC5/TTL255 ‚Üí inner 200/S/TTL10) decode identically; the raw-surfaced Interface-Information object, the malformed-length raw fallback and the truncation / header-only cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/icmpext`. Registered as `icmp_extension_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 582‚Üí583.
- `roce_decode` RoCE / InfiniBand Base Transport Header (RoCEv2, UDP 4791) ‚Äî RDMA datacenter-fabric recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.583.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **InfiniBand transport member** of the project's network-decoder family, a distinct domain (RDMA / datacenter fabric). RoCE (RDMA over Converged Ethernet) carries the InfiniBand transport over UDP, letting one host **read and write another host's memory directly**, bypassing the remote CPU ‚Äî the fabric under high-performance storage (NVMe-oF), GPU clusters (NCCL / GPUDirect) and HPC. RDMA is a real, often-overlooked **attack surface**: the wire protocol is unencrypted and unauthenticated by default, isolation rests only on the 16-bit **Partition Key** (P_Key) and the Queue-Pair number, and an attacker on the fabric who can forge a BTH can issue RDMA READ / WRITE operations against a remote host's registered memory. A captured RoCE BTH identifies the **RDMA operation** in flight ‚Äî an RDMA **READ / WRITE** (direct remote memory access), an **atomic** compare-swap / fetch-add, a SEND, an ACK or a **congestion-notification** (CNP) ‚Äî with the **transport service** (RC / UC / RD / UD), the **destination Queue Pair**, the **Partition Key** (the fabric isolation domain), the FECN/BECN congestion flags and the PSN; the recon headline for RDMA-fabric reconnaissance. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the always-present fixed 12-byte BTH is decoded ‚Äî the per-opcode extended transport headers (RETH for RDMA, AETH for ACKs, AtomicETH, ImmDt) and payload vary by opcode and are surfaced as raw hex (the trailing 4 bytes are the ICRC); the transport-service type is derived from the opcode's top three bits per the IBA spec, and an opcode outside the known table is reported by value with a note. The **57-entry opcode name table is code-generated from scapy's authoritative map** (`scapy.contrib.roce`), not hand-transcribed. Native ‚Äî a byte/bit read + an opcode lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **12-byte BTH layout + opcode table verified field-for-field against scapy's RoCE layer** ‚Äî an 80-row differential (random opcode / flags / P_Key / QP / PSN) decoded identically, **zero mismatches**; the RDMA-READ-request, the UD-send flags, the CNP, the trailing-payload surface and the unknown-opcode / truncation cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/roce`. Registered as `roce_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 581‚Üí582.
- `homepluggp_decode` HomePlug Green PHY SLAC (EtherType 0x88E1) ‚Äî EV-charging pairing recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.582.0 ‚Äî **new tool** extending the powerline domain opened by `homeplugav` into **EV charging**. SLAC (Signal Level Attenuation Characterization) is the HomePlug Green PHY handshake that pairs an **electric vehicle to a charging station** over the CCS / ISO 15118 (DIN 70121) Control Pilot line, before any high-level EV ‚Üî EVSE communication ‚Äî it works out which charger the car is physically plugged into (attenuation-based matching) and establishes a private logical network. SLAC is a hot **EV-charging-security** target: the handshake is unauthenticated, the matching is attackable by signal injection, and the **CM_SLAC_MATCH.CNF / CM_SET_KEY** messages carry the Network Membership Key (NMK) **in the clear** ‚Äî capturing one yields the charging link's network credential. A captured SLAC frame identifies the **step** of the pairing handshake (parm ‚Üí start-atten ‚Üí M-sound ‚Üí atten-char ‚Üí match ‚Üí set-key) and surfaces the session **Run ID**, the **EV / EVSE MAC addresses and IDs**, and the **NID + NMK** key material. These are the **0x60xx CCo SLAC MMEs**, distinct from the 0xAxxx vendor MMEs that `homeplugav` covers; both ride EtherType 0x88E1 with the same version + LE-MMTYPE envelope. **No confidently-wrong output**: unlike the vendor-specific HomePlug AV bodies (surfaced raw), the SLAC bodies are **standardised** by ISO 15118-3, so the recon-relevant fields are decoded; each message decode is **length-gated** ‚Äî a body that does not match the SLAC layout is surfaced as raw hex with a note, and an MMTYPE outside the SLAC set is rejected. Native ‚Äî a byte-slice walk + an MMTYPE lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Envelope + SLAC body layouts verified field-for-field against scapy's HomePlug Green PHY layer** (`scapy.contrib.homepluggp`) and the ISO 15118-3 SLAC layout ‚Äî the CM_SLAC_PARM_REQ, the CM_SLAC_MATCH_CNF (NID + NMK extraction), the CM_SET_KEY_REQ (NID + NMK), the CM_START_ATTEN_CHAR_IND, the sub-type/step mapping, the non-SLAC rejection and the short-body raw-surface unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/homepluggp`. Registered as `homepluggp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 580‚Üí581.
- `homeplugav_decode` HomePlug AV / IEEE 1901 powerline (EtherType 0x88E1) ‚Äî powerline (PLC) management recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.581.0 ‚Äî **new tool** opening a distinct domain (powerline networking) alongside the project's RF / wireless decoders. HomePlug AV / IEEE 1901 is the powerline (PLC) adapter protocol; its **MAC Management Entry** envelope is the control plane, and powerline is a real, often-overlooked **attack surface** ‚Äî the medium is shared across a building's wiring, and the management messages drive network membership, key exchange and diagnostics. A captured HomePlug AV management frame identifies the **management operation** in flight ‚Äî a **Set Encryption Key** (the powerline Network Membership Key exchange), a **Sniffer** enable, a **Network Information** query (station / network enumeration), a **Read MAC Memory** firmware dump, a device reset ‚Äî the recon headline for powerline reconnaissance. Decodes the envelope: the MM **version** (1.0 / 1.1), the **MMTYPE** (little-endian) + name (77-entry table), the request/confirmation/indication/response **sub-type** (the two LSBs) and the MMTYPE **category** range; the Set-Encryption-Key (NMK) and Sniffer messages are flagged. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the envelope is decoded ‚Äî the message bodies are many, version-specific (the v1.1 fragmentation header) and largely vendor-specific (Qualcomm/Intellon), so they are surfaced as raw hex; the **MMTYPE name table is code-generated from scapy's authoritative map** (`scapy.contrib.homeplugav`), not hand-transcribed. Native ‚Äî a byte read + an MMTYPE lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Version + MMTYPE verified field-for-field against scapy's HomePlugAV layer** ‚Äî 60 random frames (30 MMTYPEs √ó both versions) decode identically, zero mismatches; the Set-Encryption-Key (NMK warning), the Network-Info confirmation (sub-type), the Sniffer request (warning), the v1.1 frame and the unknown-MMTYPE / bad-version cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/homeplugav`. Registered as `homeplugav_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 579‚Üí580.
- `nsh_decode` Network Service Header (NSH, RFC 8300) ‚Äî SFC service-chain decap recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.580.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the project's tunnel-decap decoder family (`gre`, `geneve`, `vxlan`, `mpls`, `sflow`, `etherip`). NSH is the **Service Function Chaining (SFC)** encapsulation that steers a packet through an ordered chain of service functions (firewalls, DPI, NAT, load-balancers) in SDN / NFV / cloud fabrics ‚Äî so a captured NSH packet reveals the **service path** (SPI) and current **service index** (SI) a packet is being steered along (the SFC routing topology), and carries the original packet inside, so decoding it decaps the steered inner flow. Decodes the 4-byte base header (version, OAM flag, TTL, length, MD type, next protocol) and the 4-byte service-path header (SPI + SI); surfaces the context headers as raw hex; and chains the inner packet via `internal/ipdecode` when next protocol is IPv4 / IPv6 (an Ethernet inner has its L2 header surfaced + its IP payload chained; other next protocols left raw). **No confidently-wrong output**: the base + service-path header was verified against scapy's NSH layer; the context headers (MD type 1 = fixed 16 bytes; MD type 2 = varied TLVs) are surfaced raw rather than field-decoded, and an inner IP parse failure degrades to an `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. Native ‚Äî a byte/bitfield read + the existing inner-IP decode path, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (same chain-to-ipdecode pattern as `gre` / `sflow` / `etherip`). **Base + service-path header verified field-for-field against scapy's NSH layer** (`scapy.contrib.nsh`) ‚Äî the MD-type-1 IPv4-inner vector + 60 random frames (varied SPI / SI / OAM) decode identically, zero mismatches; the IPv4-inner chain, the Ethernet-inner chain, the raw context headers and truncation unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/nsh`. Registered as `nsh_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 578‚Üí579.
- `rtps_decode` RTPS / DDS wire protocol ‚Äî ROS2 / autonomous / industrial pub-sub recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.579.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the **DDS member** of the project's OT/ICS decoder family (`modbus`, `dnp3`, `iec104`, `s7comm`, `enip`, `profinetdcp`, `opcua`, `ethercat`, `knxnetip`, `hicp`). RTPS (Real-Time Publish-Subscribe) is the wire protocol of OMG DDS, the pub/sub middleware that runs **ROS 2 robotics, autonomous vehicles, naval combat systems and industrial control**. It is a recon-rich OT target: DDS discovery (SPDP / SEDP) and data flow are unauthenticated by default, so a captured RTPS message **fingerprints the DDS vendor** (RTI Connext / eProsima FastDDS / Eclipse Cyclone / OpenDDS / ‚Ä¶), identifies the **participant** (GUID prefix), and maps the submessage flow (discovery vs data, heartbeats, ACKNACKs). Decodes the 20-byte header (magic, protocol version, vendor id + name, GUID prefix split into host / app / instance) and walks the **submessages** ‚Äî each kind (DATA / HEARTBEAT / ACKNACK / GAP / INFO_TS / INFO_DST / SEC_* / ‚Ä¶), endianness and length (octetsToNextHeader) ‚Äî lifting out the INFO_DST destination GUID prefix. **No confidently-wrong output**: the header was verified field-for-field against scapy's RTPS layer (and the vendor-id table is scapy's authoritative map), and the submessage walk follows the RTPS-spec octetsToNextHeader boundary read in each submessage's own endianness; the submessage **bodies** (SPDP/SEDP parameter lists, serialized data) are surfaced as raw hex rather than decoded into possibly-wrong vendor/QoS fields ‚Äî only the framing + INFO_DST GUID are decoded. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + a submessage walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Header verified field-for-field against scapy's RTPS layer** (`scapy.contrib.rtps`), which also confirmed the INFO_TS + DATA submessage boundaries; the multi-submessage walk (INFO_TS/DATA/HEARTBEAT), the INFO_DST GUID, the big-endian submessage and the non-RTPS rejection unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/rtps`. Registered as `rtps_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 577‚Üí578.
- `hicp_decode` HICP (HMS Anybus Host IP Configuration Protocol, UDP 3250) ‚Äî industrial device-discovery / reconfiguration recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.578.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the project's OT/ICS decoder family (`modbus`, `dnp3`, `iec104`, `s7comm`, `enip`, `profinetdcp`, `opcua`, `ethercat`, `knxnetip`) as an industrial **device-discovery** decoder ‚Äî the HMS-Anybus analogue of `profinetdcp`. HICP discovers and (re)configures HMS Anybus / X-gateway industrial Ethernet modules, and is an OT attack surface: a broadcast **Module Scan** enumerates every Anybus gateway on the segment, a **Configure** message can change a module's IP / subnet / gateway / hostname, and the **Module Scan Response** advertises whether the module is password-protected (**PSWD = OFF** ‚áí reconfiguration is unauthenticated). A captured HICP exchange is industrial-asset inventory + a hijack / misconfiguration signal. Decodes the message type (Module Scan / Module Scan Response / Configure / Reconfigured / Invalid Configuration / Invalid Password / Wink) and the **Key = value** fields ‚Äî fieldbus type, module version, MAC, IP, subnet, gateway, DHCP, password state, hostname, DNS ‚Äî surfacing every pair found and flagging an unauthenticated-reconfig (PSWD = OFF) module. **No confidently-wrong output**: HICP's specification is not public (scapy itself is built from the Wireshark dissector + the HMS DLL), so the parser is deliberately generic ‚Äî it surfaces all Key=value pairs, normalises the protocol's inconsistent MAC separators ('-' vs ':'), and rejects an unrecognised payload. Native ‚Äî a prefix check + a key-value split, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified against scapy's HICP layer** (`scapy.contrib.hicp`) ‚Äî the Module Scan Response (full device inventory), the Module Scan request, the Configure (re-IP) request, the Reconfigured / Invalid-Configuration / Invalid-Password / Wink statuses, hex-input handling and the PSWD=OFF warning unit-pinned on scapy's exact wire output; fuzz-clean. `internal/hicp`. Registered as `hicp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 576‚Üí577.
- `aoe_decode` ATA over Ethernet (AoE, EtherType 0x88A2) ‚Äî unauthenticated L2 raw-disk attack-surface recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.577.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for a genuinely dangerous, under-decoded protocol: AoE (the CORAID protocol) exposes **raw ATA disk commands directly over an Ethernet segment with no authentication and no IP layer** ‚Äî any host on the same L2 segment can issue ATA **READ / WRITE** to an exposed target, a major unauthenticated **data-theft / data-destruction** surface. A captured AoE frame is storage-reconnaissance: it reveals the target disk (**shelf.slot**), the **ATA command** (READ / WRITE / IDENTIFY / DMA / FLUSH), the 48-bit **LBA** + sector count being transferred, or ‚Äî via **Query Config Information** ‚Äî the target's **config string** + firmware. Decodes the 10-byte header (version, Response / Error flags, error code, shelf=major, slot=minor, command, tag) and the command body: Issue ATA Command (aflags, sector count, ATA command + name, 48-bit little-endian LBA) and Query Config Information (buffer count, firmware, AoE version, config command, config string); MAC Mask List / Reserve-Release are named with their body surfaced raw. **No confidently-wrong output**: the structural fields were cross-checked against scapy's AoE layer; the Response / Error flags follow the **AoE spec / Wireshark** (bit 3 / bit 2) because **scapy maps those flag bits incorrectly** (a real scapy bug ‚Äî the raw flag nibble is also surfaced), and the under-specified ATA aflags byte is surfaced raw rather than mis-labelled (read-vs-write intent is already unambiguous from the ATA command). Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + a command switch, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Structural fields verified field-for-field against scapy's AoE layer** (`scapy.contrib.aoe`) ‚Äî the ATA-READ + Query-Config vectors + 80 random ATA frames (10 ATA commands √ó varied shelf/slot/tag/sector/48-bit-LBA) decode identically, zero mismatches; the ATA READ, the WRITE EXT, the Query-Config (CORAID config string), the Response+Error flags and truncation unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/aoe`. Registered as `aoe_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 575‚Üí576.
- `etherip_decode` EtherIP (RFC 3378) ‚Äî L2-over-IP tunnel / exfil decap recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.576.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the project's **tunnel-decap decoder family** alongside `gre`, `geneve`, `vxlan`, `mpls` and `sflow`. EtherIP tunnels a whole **Ethernet frame inside an IP packet** (IP protocol 97) ‚Äî used for transparent bridging / L2 VPNs, and as a **data-exfiltration / pivot** encapsulation ‚Äî so a captured EtherIP packet is an L2-over-IP tunnel whose inner frame is the recon payload. Decodes the 2-byte EtherIP header (version, reserved), the inner Ethernet header (dst/src **MAC** + **EtherType** + name), and chains an IPv4 / IPv6 inner payload to the full IP decode (`internal/ipdecode`), surfacing the **encapsulated flow's** addresses / protocol / ports; a non-IP EtherType (ARP, VLAN, MPLS, PPPoE, ‚Ä¶) leaves the inner frame as raw hex. **No confidently-wrong output**: the version is required to be 3 (RFC 3378) ‚Äî a non-EtherIP packet is rejected, not mis-decoded; an inner IP payload that fails to parse degrades to an `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + the existing inner-IP decode path, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (same chain-to-ipdecode pattern as `gre` / `sflow`). **Verified field-for-field against scapy's EtherIP layer** (`scapy.contrib.etherip`) ‚Äî the canonical EtherIP-over-IPv4/UDP vector + 60 random frames (varied MACs, IPv4 inner flows) decode identically, zero mismatches; the IPv4-inner chain, the ARP-inner (raw, not IP-decoded), the bad-version rejection and the truncated-frame cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/etherip`. Registered as `etherip_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 574‚Üí575.
- `socks_decode` SOCKS proxy (SOCKS4 / 4a / 5, RFC 1928) ‚Äî proxy / pivot / exfil-channel recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.575.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, an application-layer capture decoder distinct from the protocol families built so far. A captured SOCKS exchange is a network-reconnaissance source: the **request reveals the proxied destination** (host or IP + port) a client is reaching *through* the proxy ‚Äî exactly what matters when analysing a capture for **data-exfiltration channels**, **malware command-and-control** over a SOCKS proxy, or an attacker **pivoting** through a compromised host's proxy. Decodes the SOCKS5 **greeting** (offered auth methods) and **method selection**; the SOCKS5 **request / reply** ‚Äî command (CONNECT / BIND / UDP-ASSOCIATE) or reply code, address type and the **destination / bound address + port** (IPv4, IPv6 or domain name); and SOCKS4 / SOCKS4a requests (command, destination, user-id, the 4a domain) and the 8-byte SOCKS4 reply. **No confidently-wrong output**: implemented to RFC 1928 (the SOCKS5 domain is a 1-octet length + name per ¬ß5, not DNS labels; a SOCKS4 reply is 8 bytes) ‚Äî and because a lone SOCKS5 message does not always distinguish a request from a reply (both share cmd/rep + rsv + atyp + addr + port, and 1-3 are valid as either), the unambiguous **destination address + port** is always surfaced and the leading byte is reported as a command when it can only be one, a reply when it can only be that, and with both readings noted when genuinely ambiguous. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verification**: the SOCKS5 IPv4 / IPv6 request+reply and the SOCKS4 request were cross-checked against scapy's SOCKS layer (120 random messages, zero mismatches); the SOCKS5 **domain** address and the SOCKS4 **reply** were hand-verified against RFC 1928 because scapy's layer is non-standard for both (it encodes the domain as DNS labels and omits the SOCKS4-reply bound address ‚Äî a real scapy bug caught during verification). The greeting, method-selection, SOCKS4a-domain and request/reply ambiguity cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/socks`. Registered as `socks_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 573‚Üí574.
- `nlm_decode` ONC RPC NFS Lock Manager v4 (NLM, RPC program 100021, rpc.lockd) ‚Äî lock-contention recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.574.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the fourth member of the project's Sun-RPC decoder suite (`portmap` / `mount` / `nfs` / `nlm`), sharing the `internal/oncrpc` framing extracted in v0.573.0 ‚Äî the refactor's first payoff (NLM dropped in cleanly). NLM is NFS's byte-range / advisory-locking sidecar; **rpc.lockd** is a long-standing remote attack surface, and a captured NLM exchange is recon in its own right: a **LOCK / TEST / CANCEL / UNLOCK** call carries the **caller name** (the client host identity it announces), the **file handle** being locked, the **lock owner** (a client / process identity string), the locked **byte range** (offset + length) and whether the lock is **exclusive** ‚Äî so an NLM stream maps which hosts are contending for which files. Decodes the ONC RPC header (xid, CALL vs REPLY), the procedure name (TEST / LOCK / CANCEL / UNLOCK / GRANTED / *_MSG / *_RES / SHARE / UNSHARE / ‚Ä¶) and, for the four core lock calls, the lock argument; a **reply** is decoded as its cookie + the **nlm4_stats** result (GRANTED / DENIED / BLOCKED / DENIED_GRACE_PERIOD / ‚Ä¶). **No confidently-wrong output**: the lock argument is decoded for the four procedures whose XDR layout is unambiguous (the per-procedure leading flag fields ‚Äî LOCK/CANCEL prefix block + exclusive, TEST exclusive only, UNLOCK neither ‚Äî are handled); the async *_MSG / *_RES variants and SHARE / UNSHARE / FREE_ALL are named with their body surfaced raw, and a reply status is reported only for a defined nlm4_stats code. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + bounded XDR walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's NLM + ONC RPC layers** (`scapy.contrib.nlm` / `oncrpc`) ‚Äî 120 random messages (LOCK / TEST / CANCEL / UNLOCK calls across varied callers / owners / file-handle lengths / offsets / exclusive flags + replies across all 10 nlm4_stats codes) decode identically, zero mismatches; the LOCK, TEST (no block field), UNLOCK (no flags) and the graced reply unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/nlm`. Registered as `nlm_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 572‚Üí573.
- `nfs_decode` ONC RPC NFS v3 (RFC 1813, RPC program 100003) ‚Äî file-access / filename recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.572.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the project's **NFS-reconnaissance chain**: `portmap_decode` (rpcbind ‚Äî locate the service) ‚Üí `mount_decode` (get the export root file handle) ‚Üí `nfs_decode` (the file access itself). A captured NFS call stream is the record of what a client actually does on the share: the **dir-operation calls carry filenames** ‚Äî a **LOOKUP / CREATE / REMOVE / RENAME / MKDIR / RMDIR** names the exact file being accessed ("a client is reading /etc/shadow off the export"), and **READ / WRITE** expose the file handle + offset + length being transferred. Decodes the ONC RPC header (xid, CALL vs REPLY), the **procedure name** (all 22 NFSv3 procedures) and, for calls, the recon-bearing leading arguments ‚Äî the **file handle**, the operand **filename(s)** (two for RENAME) and the **offset + count** for READ / WRITE. **No confidently-wrong output**: arguments are decoded only for the calls whose leading XDR fields are unambiguous; an NFS **reply** is large, procedure-specific and not self-identifying (the client correlates by xid), so it is reported as its accept status + a recognised nfsstat3 code with the body surfaced raw. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + bounded XDR walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's NFS + ONC RPC layers** (`scapy.contrib.nfs` / `oncrpc`) ‚Äî 106 random calls (LOOKUP / REMOVE / RMDIR / MKDIR / READ / RENAME / GETATTR across varied file-handle lengths, filenames and offsets) decode identically, zero mismatches; the LOOKUP (passwd), the READ (offset/count), the REMOVE, the RENAME (two names + two handles) and the GETATTR (handle-only) unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/nfs`. Registered as `nfs_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 571‚Üí572.
