- `mount_decode` NFS MOUNT protocol v3 (RFC 1813, RPC program 100005) ‚Äî export / file-handle / weak-auth recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.571.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the NFS-reconnaissance companion to `portmap_decode` (rpcbind). mountd is the service that hands a client the root **file handle** for an NFS export, so after `rpcinfo` locates it a captured MOUNT exchange exposes the NFS attack surface: the exact **export path** a client mounts (`MNT` / `UMNT` call), the **result** (a successful mount vs an **MNT3ERR_ACCES** denial ‚Äî the export's access control in action), the **file handle** the server returns (a captured / guessable NFS file handle enables the classic **file-handle-reuse** attack), and the **auth flavors** the server accepts (**AUTH_NULL / AUTH_SYS** are trivially spoofable ‚Äî the root of most NFS compromises). Decodes the ONC RPC header (xid, CALL vs REPLY), the procedure (NULL / MNT / DUMP / UMNT / UMNTALL / EXPORT), the mount path on a call, and on a reply the status (the full mountstat3 set), the file handle and the auth-flavor list. **No confidently-wrong output**: an RPC reply does not carry the procedure it answers, so a reply body is typed as a MOUNT reply only when its first word is a defined mountstat3 code and the file-handle + flavor structure parses within the body ‚Äî else surfaced raw; **EXPORT / DUMP (showmount) are deliberately not decoded** because scapy does not model them and they cannot be differentially verified. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + bounded XDR walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's NFS-MOUNT + ONC RPC layers** (`scapy.contrib.mount` / `oncrpc`) ‚Äî 110 random messages (50 MNT/UMNT calls across 7 export paths + 60 MOUNT replies: OK with random file-handle lengths + 1-3 auth flavors, and all 10 mountstat3 denial codes) decode identically, zero mismatches; the MNT call, the OK reply (file handle + AUTH_SYS), the ACCES denial and the non-mountstat3 reply gate unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/mount`. Registered as `mount_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 570‚Üí571.
- `portmap_decode` ONC RPC portmapper / rpcbind v2 (port 111) ‚Äî Sun-RPC service enumeration (rpcinfo recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.570.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the classic **`rpcinfo -p` LAN-reconnaissance** technique. The portmapper (Sun RPC program 100000, UDP/TCP 111) is the RPC service directory, and its **DUMP reply** lists every RPC program a host has registered ‚Äî **NFS**, **mountd**, **NIS/yp**, nlockmgr, statd ‚Äî with the program number, version, transport and **port**, mapping out the host's RPC attack surface; a **GETPORT call** reveals which specific service a client is locating. Decodes the ONC RPC header (xid, CALL vs REPLY) and, for a CALL, the RPC version, the **program** (named ‚Äî portmapper / nfs / mountd / ypserv / nlockmgr / statd / ‚Ä¶), program version, the **procedure** (named for portmap: NULL / SET / UNSET / GETPORT / DUMP / CALLIT) and auth flavor, plus the GETPORT query; for a REPLY the accept status and result ‚Äî the **DUMP reply mapping list** (program + version + tcp/udp + port per registered service) being the recon headline. **No confidently-wrong output**: an RPC reply does not carry the program/procedure it answers (the client correlates by xid), so a reply body is typed by **structure** ‚Äî a DUMP list is reported only when it parses exhaustively to a clean value-follows terminator with sane transports, and a bare 4-byte accepted result as a GETPORT port (an all-zero one is noted as byte-identical to an empty DUMP ‚Äî a genuine ambiguity surfaced, not hidden). Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + bounded XDR walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's ONC RPC + portmap layers** (`scapy.contrib.oncrpc` / `portmap`) ‚Äî 160 random messages (60 GETPORT calls across 10 programs √ó versions √ó tcp/udp + 40 GETPORT replies + 60 DUMP replies with 0-6 mappings) decode identically, zero mismatches; the GETPORT call (NFSv3/UDP query), the GETPORT reply (port 2049), the 3-service DUMP list, the denied reply and the port-0 / empty-DUMP ambiguity unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/portmap`. Registered as `portmap_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 569‚Üí570.
- `oam_decode` Ethernet OAM / CFM (802.1ag / Y.1731, EtherType 0x8902) ‚Äî L2 connectivity-fault / service-topology recon ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.569.0 ‚Äî **new tool** adding the L2 connectivity-fault / service-topology leg to the project's LAN decoder family (`dtp`, `vtp`, `vqp`, `gxrp`, `stp`, `maccontrol`). Ethernet **CFM** is the L2 operations-and-maintenance framework, and its **Continuity Check Message (CCM)** is a frame a maintenance endpoint multicasts continuously, advertising the Maintenance Domain **level**, the Maintenance Entity Group (**MEG / MA**) identifier and the source **MEP ID** ‚Äî so a captured CCM stream maps the L2 maintenance topology (which bridges are MEPs, at which level, in which association), and the **RDI** flag signals a remote defect; Loopback (LBM/LBR) and Linktrace (LTM/LTR) are the L2 ping / traceroute of the same framework. Decodes the 4-byte common header ‚Äî MD level, version, the **opcode name** (all 24 CFM functions: CCM / LBM / LBR / LTM / LTR / AIS / LCK / TST / APS / R-APS / LMM / DMM / SLM / ‚Ä¶), the flags byte, the TLV offset ‚Äî for every opcode, and for a **CCM** additionally the RDI flag, the transmission period (+ name), the sequence number, the 13-bit MEP ID and the MEG ID (raw hex + a best-effort printable extraction). **No confidently-wrong output**: CFM has 24 opcodes with varied, often vendor-extended bodies, so only the universally-present common header and the CCM body are decoded ‚Äî every other opcode's body, and the trailing TLV list, are surfaced as raw hex with the opcode named. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + an opcode switch, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's OAM layer** (`scapy.contrib.oam`) ‚Äî 208 random PDUs (120 CCM with random level / RDI / period / sequence / MEP / MEG ID + 88 other-opcode headers across 11 opcodes) decode identically, zero mismatches; the RDI-set CCM, the LBM raw-body case, the opcode-name table and the TLV split unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. The differential harness initially flagged 64 CCM "mismatches" that were a harness bug (the test passed RDI into scapy's 5-bit flags field as bit 7 instead of bit 4, overflowing it) ‚Äî the decoder was correct, confirmed once the harness set the RDI bit in the right position. `internal/oam`. Registered as `oam_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 568‚Üí569.
- `maccontrol_decode` IEEE 802.3 MAC Control (EtherType 0x8808) ‚Äî L2 flow-control DoS + EPON MPCP (L2-DoS recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.567.0 ‚Äî **new tool** adding the **L2 denial-of-service** leg to the project's LAN-attack decoder family (`dtp`, `vtp`, `vqp`, `gxrp`, `stp`). MAC Control is the Ethernet flow-control + EPON access-control sublayer, and its two flow-control opcodes are recognised DoS surfaces: **PAUSE** (802.3x, opcode 0x0001) halts the upstream port for pause_time √ó 512 bit-times ‚Äî a **flood of PAUSE frames with the maximum quanta (0xFFFF) is the classic switch-port flow-control DoS** (it can stall the port indefinitely); **PFC / Priority-based Flow Control** (802.1Qbb, opcode 0x0101) is the per-priority version used in lossless datacenter fabrics (RoCE / FCoE), where a **PFC storm causes head-of-line blocking and can collapse a converged fabric**. The remaining opcodes are **EPON MPCP** (GATE / REPORT / REGISTER_REQ / REGISTER / REGISTER_ACK ‚Äî the time-slot grant + discovery handshake of an Ethernet PON). Decodes the PAUSE quanta, the PFC per-class enable vector + eight pause times, and the MPCP timestamp / flags / port / grant fields. **No confidently-wrong output**: MAC Control frames are padded to the 60-byte minimum Ethernet payload, so the decoder reads only the defined opcode fields and **reports any non-zero trailing bytes** rather than guessing; an unknown opcode is named by number with its body surfaced as raw hex. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + an opcode switch, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's MACControl layer** (`scapy.contrib.mac_control`) ‚Äî 200 random frames (all 7 opcodes: PAUSE / PFC with random enable vectors + per-class times / GATE / REPORT / REGISTER_REQ / REGISTER / REGISTER_ACK with random MPCP fields) decode identically, zero mismatches; the max-quanta PAUSE, the multi-class PFC, the MPCP REPORT and the trailing-byte / unknown-opcode edge cases unit-pinned; fuzz-clean. `internal/maccontrol`. Registered as `maccontrol_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 567‚Üí568.
- `gxrp_decode` GARP / GVRP / GMRP (IEEE 802.1D) ‚Äî dynamic VLAN + multicast registration (VLAN-hopping recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.566.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the project's Cisco/L2 **VLAN-attack** decoder family alongside `dtp` (trunk-negotiation VLAN-hopping), `vtp` (VLAN-database tampering) and `vqp` (VMPS VLAN assignment). **GARP** (Generic Attribute Registration Protocol) and its applications **GVRP** (VLAN) and **GMRP** (multicast) are an L2 attack surface: a host that emits GVRP **JoinIn** attributes can **register arbitrary VLANs onto the trunk** it is attached to (extending the trunk's allowed-VLAN set), a VLAN-hopping primitive; GMRP does the equivalent for multicast group membership. A captured PDU reveals which VLANs / multicast groups are being registered or withdrawn and by which **event** (Join / Leave / LeaveAll). Decodes the GARP framing ‚Äî protocol id and the nested list of **messages** (each a type + a list of **attributes**: length, event + name, value), interpreting the attribute value by length: a 2-byte value is a **VLAN id** (GVRP), a 6-byte value a **group MAC** (GMRP), a 1-byte value a **GMRP service**. **No confidently-wrong output**: the GVRP-vs-GMRP application is keyed in the standard by the L2 destination MAC (01:80:c2:00:00:21 = GVRP, ...:20 = GMRP), which is **not carried in the PDU**, so the attribute kind is inferred from the value length (the lengths are non-overlapping and deterministic) and the **raw value is always surfaced** alongside, with a note naming the definitive signal; unknown value lengths are surfaced as raw hex only. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + two nested walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's GARP layer** (`scapy.contrib.gxrp`) ‚Äî 200 random PDUs (1-3 messages √ó 1-4 attributes mixing GVRP VLAN / GMRP group-MAC / GMRP service values across all 6 events incl. LeaveAll) decode identically, zero mismatches; the multi-attribute GVRP PDU, the GMRP group, the GMRP service and the bad-length edge case unit-pinned. `internal/gxrp`. Registered as `gxrp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 566‚Üí567.
- `ripng_decode` RIPng (RFC 2080) ‚Äî IPv6 distance-vector routing (routing recon / route-injection) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.565.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the IPv6 sibling of the project's `rip` (RIPv1/v2, IPv4). **RIPng** (UDP 521) is a routing-reconnaissance and route-injection surface: it carries no authentication, so a captured **Response** reveals every route a router advertises (each IPv6 prefix, route tag and hop-count metric), and because the protocol trusts any Response on the segment, an on-link attacker can **inject or blackhole routes**. Decodes the 4-byte header (command ‚Äî request / response, version) and the array of 20-byte **route table entries** (128-bit prefix, route tag, prefix length, metric), correctly handling the two RFC 2080 special entries ‚Äî the **next-hop RTE** (metric 0xFF ‚Äî the address field is a gateway, not a route) and the **infinity metric** (16 ‚Äî an unreachable / withdrawn route); the RFC 2080 whole-table request (a single `::/0`, metric-16 entry) is flagged. **No confidently-wrong output**: every byte maps to a defined field, and trailing bytes that do not form a whole entry are noted rather than guessed. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + an array walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's RIPng layer** (`scapy.contrib.ripng`) ‚Äî 200 random messages (request / response, 1-5 entries mixing next-hop RTEs and routes with random prefix / tag / prefix-length / metric incl. infinity) decode identically, zero mismatches; the multi-route response (next-hop + route + infinity), the whole-table request and the bad-command / trailing-byte edge cases unit-pinned. `internal/ripng`. Registered as `ripng_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 565‚Üí566.
- `tzsp_decode` TZSP (TaZmen Sniffer Protocol) ‚Äî remote wireless-capture encapsulation (MikroTik sniffer recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.564.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the project's wireless tooling (`ieee80211`, `marauder`) and tunnel-decap decoders (`gre`, `geneve`, `vxlan`, `mpls`). **TZSP** is the UDP encapsulation (default port 37008 / 0x9090) that **MikroTik RouterOS**, Aruba and other gear use to **stream sniffed wireless frames to a remote analyser** ‚Äî a captured TZSP stream is a remote packet-capture feed: each datagram wraps one sniffed frame (802.11 / Ethernet / Prism / AVS) together with the radio metadata the sensor observed (RX **channel**, **RSSI**, SNR, link rate, FCS-error flag), so decoding it surfaces both the wireless-recon metadata and the encapsulated frame. Decodes the 4-byte header (version, **packet type** ‚Äî RX / TX / CONFIG / KEEPALIVE / PORT, **encapsulated protocol**) and the tag list ‚Äî RAW_RSSI / SNR (both signed), DATA_RATE (named Mb/s), TIMESTAMP, CONTENTION_FREE, DECRYPTED, **FCS_ERROR**, **RX_CHANNEL**, PACKET_COUNT, RX_FRAME_LENGTH, WLAN sensor id ‚Äî lifting RSSI / SNR / rate / channel / FCS to top-level fields. **No confidently-wrong output**: standard tags are decoded by type; the complete encapsulated frame is surfaced as raw hex with its protocol named (for `ieee80211_decode` etc.) rather than partially parsed here, and unknown tags are surfaced as raw hex. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + a tag walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's TZSP layer** (`scapy.contrib.tzsp`) ‚Äî 200 random datagrams (all packet types √ó all encapsulations, with byte/short RSSI, SNR, all 19 data-rate codes, channel, FCS and a random encapsulated frame) decode identically, zero mismatches; the RX-packet metadata set, the keepalive, the short-form signed RSSI and the data-rate table unit-pinned. `internal/tzsp`. Registered as `tzsp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 564‚Üí565.
- `igmpv3_decode` IGMPv3 (RFC 3376) ‚Äî IPv4 multicast group membership v3 (multicast recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.563.0 ‚Äî **new tool**, the v3 companion to the project's `igmp` (v1/v2), whose group-record + source-list structure differs enough to warrant its own decoder. **IGMPv3** is a network-reconnaissance source: a **Membership Report** reveals exactly which multicast groups a host has joined and ‚Äî via the source-filter group records (**INCLUDE / EXCLUDE** mode) ‚Äî which senders it accepts or blocks, exposing the host's multicast-based services (mDNS 224.0.0.251, SSDP 239.255.255.250, PTP, IPTV / streaming groups); a **Membership Query** reveals the active querier and its robustness / query-interval parameters. Decodes the header (type, **verified** checksum) and, for a **Query**, the Max-Resp-Time, group address, S flag, **QRV**, **QQIC** (both Max-Resp and QQIC via the RFC 3376 ¬ß4.1 floating-point code), the source list and the **query type** (general / group-specific / group-and-source-specific); for a **Report**, each **group record** ‚Äî record type (MODE_IS_INCLUDE / EXCLUDE / CHANGE_TO_* / ALLOW_NEW_SOURCES / BLOCK_OLD_SOURCES), the multicast address and its source list. **No confidently-wrong output**: the 16-bit one's-complement checksum is verified and surfaced as `checksum_valid` (a failure is flagged, not hidden), and rare auxiliary record data is surfaced as raw hex. Native ‚Äî byte-field reads + two array walks, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's IGMPv3 layer** (`scapy.contrib.igmpv3`) ‚Äî 200 random messages (120 Reports with 1-4 group records of all 6 record types √ó varied source lists + 80 Queries incl. general / group / group-and-source with random QRV / QQIC / Max-Resp / S) decode identically with valid checksums, zero mismatches; the report, the group-and-source query, the general query and the ¬ß4.1 float encoding unit-pinned. `internal/igmpv3`. Registered as `igmpv3_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 563‚Üí564.
- `vqp_decode` Cisco VQP / VMPS ‚Äî dynamic VLAN assignment by MAC (VLAN-assignment recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.562.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the project's **Cisco VLAN-attack** decoder family alongside `dtp` (DTP trunk-negotiation VLAN-hopping) and `vtp` (VTP VLAN-database tampering). **VQP** is the wire protocol of **VMPS** (VLAN Membership Policy Server, UDP 1589): a switch asks a server "what VLAN should this source MAC be on?" and the server answers with a VLAN name. Dynamic VLAN-by-MAC is an attack surface ‚Äî a host that **spoofs a MAC the server maps to a privileged VLAN** (e.g. a voice / management VLAN ‚Äî the **voiphopper / yersinia** technique) lands its access port in that VLAN, and a server that replies with **shutdownPort / accessDenied** is the lockout response. A captured exchange reveals the queried **MAC**, the switch **port** name, the VTP **domain** and the assigned **VLAN name**. Decodes the 8-byte header (version, **opcode** ‚Äî requestPort / responseVLAN / requestReconfirm / responseReconfirm, **response code** ‚Äî none / accessDenied / shutdownPort / wrongDomain, flag, sequence) and the list of **data entries** (each `datatype(4)+len(2)+value`): clientIPAddress ‚Üí IPv4, Req/ResMACAddress ‚Üí MAC, portName / VLANName / Domain ‚Üí text; a denied response is flagged. **No confidently-wrong output**: typed entries are decoded by datatype, and the ethernetPacket / unknown entry bodies (plus any non-printable name) are surfaced as raw hex. Native ‚Äî a byte-field read + a TLV walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's VQP layer** (`scapy.contrib.vqp`) ‚Äî 200 random messages (all 4 opcodes √ó all response codes, with Domain / portName / Req|ResMAC / VLANName / IP entries) decode identically, zero mismatches; the VMPS request, the responseVLAN, and the accessDenied lockout response unit-pinned. `internal/vqp`. Registered as `vqp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 562‚Üí563.
- `rpl_decode` RPL (RFC 6550) ‚Äî IPv6 routing for 6LoWPAN / 802.15.4 IoT mesh (routing-attack recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.561.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the IoT decoder set (`ieee802154`, `zigbee`, `ndp`). **RPL** is the IPv6 routing protocol that builds the mesh (the "DODAG") of a low-power IoT network ‚Äî 6LoWPAN over IEEE 802.15.4 ‚Äî and is carried in **ICMPv6 type 155**. It is a recognised **IoT-routing attack** surface: a malicious node can advertise a forged low **rank** in a DIO to draw the mesh's traffic through itself (a **sinkhole / on-path** attack), or bump the DODAG **version** number to force a costly network-wide rebuild (a **DoS**) ‚Äî both attacks are directly visible in a captured DIO. Decodes the ICMPv6 RPL header (type + the **message name** ‚Äî DIS / DIO / DAO / DAO-ACK / DCO) and, for a **DIO**, the RPLInstanceID, **version**, **rank**, Grounded flag, **Mode of Operation** (+ name: storing / non-storing / ‚Ä¶), DODAG preference, DTSN and **DODAGID**; for **DAO / DAO-ACK** the InstanceID, sequence, status and (when the D-flag is set) the DODAGID ‚Äî with the headline rank + version surfaced under an attack note. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the fixed message header is decoded ‚Äî the trailing RPL options (DODAG Config, Prefix / Transit / Target Info) are a varied TLV list and are surfaced as raw hex, and the ICMPv6 checksum (which covers an IPv6 pseudo-header not present in the message alone) is not verified. Native ‚Äî bitfield/byte extraction, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's RPL layer** (`scapy.contrib.rpl` + `ICMPv6RPL`) ‚Äî 250 random messages (200 DIO with random instance / version / rank / MOP / prf / DTSN / DODAGID + 50 DAO) decode identically, zero mismatches; DIS, the DIO field set, DAO, separator-tolerance and non-RPL/truncation rejection unit-pinned. `internal/rpl`. Registered as `rpl_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 561‚Üí562.
- `skinny_decode` Skinny / SCCP ‚Äî Cisco IP-phone signalling (VoIP recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.560.0 ‚Äî **new tool** joining the VoIP / signalling decoders (`sip`, `rtp`, `rtcp`). Skinny (SCCP) is the Cisco-proprietary protocol between a Cisco IP phone and a CallManager / CUCM (TCP 2000); it is unencrypted in many deployments, so a captured exchange is a **VoIP-reconnaissance** goldmine ‚Äî the message stream reveals the **call flow** (Register, OffHook, KeypadButton, CallInfo, Ring, Connect, OnHook) and, via the **KeypadButton** messages, the **actual digits the user dials** (the numbers being called). Decodes the self-delimiting little-endian Skinny stream: per message the **length**, the **message ID** and its **name** (from the full 132-entry SCCP message table), and ‚Äî for KeypadButton ‚Äî the **dialed digit** (0-9, `*`, `#`); multiple concatenated messages decode to a list. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the KeypadButton body is decoded ‚Äî Skinny has ~130 message types with varied, version-specific bodies, so every other body is surfaced as raw hex with the message named. Native ‚Äî a framed little-endian walk + an ID lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep; the **132-entry message-name table is code-generated from scapy.contrib.skinny** (not hand-transcribed). **Verified field-for-field against scapy's Skinny layer** ‚Äî 150 random messages (KeypadButton with all key codes + random message IDs / body lengths) decode identically, zero mismatches; the KeypadButton (digit + `#`), OffHook, and the OffHook+Keypad two-message stream unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/skinny`. Registered as `skinny_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 560‚Üí561.
- `pfcp_decode` PFCP ‚Äî 5G N4 / 4G CUPS control protocol (session-manipulation recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.559.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the **5G-core-security** space, joining the cellular decoder set (`gtp_decode`, `gtpv2_decode`, `gsmtap_decode`, `diameter_decode`). PFCP (3GPP TS 29.244) is the control protocol of the **5G N4 interface (SMF‚ÜîUPF)** and the 4G CUPS Sxa/Sxb/Sxc interfaces, by which the control plane programs the user-plane function's packet-forwarding rules (PDRs/FARs/QERs/URRs) over UDP 8805. It is a recognised attack surface: a host that can reach N4 can forge PFCP **Session Modification / Deletion** messages to tear down or redirect a subscriber's bearer (a 5G-core DoS / on-path attack), so decoding a captured PFCP exchange surfaces the message type, the session endpoint identifier (**SEID**) and the rule IEs being programmed. Decodes the header (version, message-priority / SEID flags, the **message type** named from the TS 29.244 table ‚Äî Heartbeat, Association Setup, Session Establishment / Modification / Deletion / Report, ‚Ä¶, the length, the optional 64-bit **SEID**, the sequence number) and the body as a list of **Information Elements** (each TLV's 2-octet type ‚Äî named from the full TS 29.244 IE table ‚Äî length, value); the **Cause** IE is decoded. **No confidently-wrong output**: grouped IEs (those that nest further IEs) and non-Cause IE values are surfaced as raw hex ‚Äî the IE value formats are numerous and release-specific, so only the structure + Cause are decoded. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + a TLV walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep; the **message-type + IE name tables (161 IE types) are code-generated from scapy.contrib.pfcp** rather than hand-transcribed (avoiding the IE-numbering errors that hand-transcription invites). **Verified field-for-field against scapy's PFCP layer** ‚Äî 109 random messages (12 message types, with/without SEID, varied seq, IE list) decode identically, zero mismatches; the Heartbeat (Recovery-Time-Stamp IE), the Session-Establishment header, and the Cause IE unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~8s). `internal/pfcp`. Registered as `pfcp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 559‚Üí560.
- `gtpv2_decode` GTPv2-C cellular control plane (IMSI-harvesting recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.558.0 ‚Äî **new tool** closing the **GTP-C gap explicitly deferred by `gtp_decode`** (which decodes the GTP-U user plane, TS 29.281, and defers the control plane). GTPv2-C (TS 29.274) signals EPS bearer/session management across the LTE & 5G-NSA core (S11 MME‚ÜîSGW, S5/S8 SGW‚ÜîPGW, S10/S16; UDP 2123) and is a recognised telecom-security target ‚Äî the roaming/core GTP plane has been abused for **IMSI harvesting**, subscriber tracking and the GTPdoor backdoor, and a captured Create-Session / Modify-Bearer exchange carries the subscriber's **IMSI, MSISDN and MEI in the clear** (chains into `imsi_decode`). Decodes the header (version, the piggyback / TEID / message-priority flags, the **message type** with a TS 29.274 name table ‚Äî Create/Modify/Delete Session, Create/Update/Delete Bearer, Echo, Release Access Bearers, ‚Ä¶, the length, the optional **TEID**, the sequence number) and the body as a list of **Information Elements** (each TLV's type ‚Äî named from the TS 29.274 table ‚Äî length, instance, value). The **TBCD-encoded subscriber identifiers (IMSI / MSISDN / MEI) are decoded to their digit strings**; every other IE value is surfaced as raw hex. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the TBCD identifiers + the Cause code are decoded ‚Äî the IE value formats are many and version-specific, so the rest are left raw rather than guessed. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + a TLV walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's GTPv2 layer** ‚Äî 150 random messages (12 message types, with/without TEID, varied seq, IMSI) decode identically, zero mismatches; the canonical Create-Session-Request (IMSI 262011234567890), the no-TEID Echo Request, and the TBCD decode unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/gtpv2`. Registered as `gtpv2_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 558‚Üí559.
- `erspan_decode` ERSPAN (Encapsulated Remote SPAN) header ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.557.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for port-mirror / traffic-interception recon, pairing with `gre_decode` (the tunnel that carries it). ERSPAN is Cisco's protocol for shipping a port-mirror (SPAN) session across a routed network inside a **GRE tunnel**; seeing it in a capture is itself a finding ‚Äî traffic on some switch is being **mirrored and exported** (lawful intercept, an IDS feed, or an attacker exfiltrating mirrored traffic) ‚Äî and the encapsulated payload is the **original mirrored Ethernet frame in the clear**, so the capture both exposes the monitoring topology (session id, source VLAN) and lets the mirrored frame be **peeled out** for further analysis. Decodes the **Type II** (8-octet) and **Type III** (12-octet) headers: version, source VLAN, class of service, the truncated flag, the session id, and (II) the port index / (III) the 32-bit timestamp; accepts the ERSPAN header itself or a **GRE packet** (proto 0x88BE / 0x22EB) whose payload is ERSPAN (the GRE header is stripped); the mirrored frame is surfaced as hex. **No confidently-wrong output**: the Type III platform-specific sub-header flags beyond the timestamp are left in the raw remainder rather than decoded into possibly-wrong fields. Native ‚Äî fixed bitfield bit-masking, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's ERSPAN_II / ERSPAN_III layers** ‚Äî 150 random headers (varied vlan / cos / encap / session-id / index / timestamp) decode identically, zero mismatches; canonical Type II (incl. max fields), Type III, and the GRE-wrapped form unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/erspan`. Registered as `erspan_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 557‚Üí558.
- `carp_decode` Common Address Redundancy Protocol (FHRP-hijacking recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.556.0 ‚Äî **new tool completing the FHRP-decoder triad** with `hsrp_decode` (Cisco HSRP) and `vrrp_decode` (IETF VRRP). CARP is the **open** FHRP used by OpenBSD / FreeBSD / **pfSense / OPNsense** for gateway/firewall HA, and is decoded for the same reason the others are: **FHRP hijacking is a classic on-path (MITM) attack** ‚Äî a host that advertises for the virtual router with a better election metric becomes master and draws the LAN's default-gateway traffic through itself. Decodes the advertisement: version/type, the **VHID** (redundancy group), **advskew** + **advbase** (and the derived advertisement interval = advbase + advskew/256 s), auth length, demotion, checksum, the 64-bit counter, and the 20-octet SHA-1 HMAC; accepts the CARP PDU or an IPv4 packet (protocol 112, shared with VRRP) whose payload is CARP. **The advskew is the attack signal**: lower skew advertises more often and wins the master election, so a low/zero advskew is the CARP hijack/preemption (MITM) tell ‚Äî the same FHRP attack class as HSRP/VRRP priority 255. **No confidently-wrong output**: the 20-octet **HMAC is surfaced as hex and not verified** ‚Äî it is an SHA-1 HMAC keyed by the CARP passphrase, which is not on the wire. Native ‚Äî fixed 36-octet byte-field extraction, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's CARP layer** ‚Äî 200 random advertisements (varied vhid / advskew / advbase / authlen / demotion) decode identically, zero mismatches; canonical advertisement, the zero-advskew hijack signal, and the IPv4-wrapped form unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/carp`. Registered as `carp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 556‚Üí557.
- `vtp_decode` Cisco VLAN Trunking Protocol (VLAN-database-attack recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.555.0 ‚Äî **new tool** continuing the switch-L2 security set (`cdp`/`lldp`/`stp`/`lacp`/`vlan_decode`/`macsec_decode`/`dtp_decode`). VTP synchronises the VLAN database across a domain's switches, and is a notorious hazard: a VTP server (or a rogue host reaching a trunk) advertising a **higher configuration-revision number** overwrites every switch's VLAN database in the domain ‚Äî a Subset advertisement with a high revision + a forged/empty VLAN list deletes or rewrites all VLANs domain-wide (a classic L2 DoS). Decoding a captured VTP frame surfaces the **domain name**, the message type, and the all-important **configuration revision** ‚Äî the recon a switch-security audit needs. Decodes the header (version, **code** ‚Äî Summary / Subset / Advertisement-Request / Join ‚Äî and domain) and the bodies: **Summary** (followers, the config revision, updater identity IPv4, update timestamp, MD5) and **Subset** (sequence number, config revision, and the full **VLAN list** ‚Äî each VLAN's id / name / status / type / MTU, switch-recon gold). Accepts the PDU or any frame carrying the LLC/SNAP VTP signature (OUI 0x00000C, PID 0x2003). **No confidently-wrong output**: the **MD5 digest is surfaced as hex and not verified** ‚Äî it is computed over the VLAN database + the VTP password, which is not on the wire; Advertisement-Request / Join bodies are surfaced raw. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + a record walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's VTP layer** ‚Äî 120 random Summary/Subset PDUs (varied domain / revision / updater / VLAN-lists) decode identically, zero mismatches; canonical Summary/Subset/AdvRequest + the SNAP-wrapped form unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/vtp`. Registered as `vtp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 555‚Üí556.
- `dtp_decode` Cisco Dynamic Trunking Protocol (VLAN-hopping recon) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.554.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for switch-security pentesting, joining the L2 decoder set (`cdp`, `lldp`, `stp`, `lacp`, `vlan_decode`, `macsec_decode`). DTP is the L2 protocol a Cisco switch port uses to negotiate whether a link becomes an 802.1Q/ISL **trunk**, and is the basis of the classic **VLAN-hopping** attack: a port left in a negotiating mode (dynamic desirable / dynamic auto ‚Äî the default on many switches) can be talked into forming a trunk by a rogue host, giving it reach into every VLAN. Decoding a captured DTP frame surfaces the **VTP domain name** (an info leak), the **neighbour MAC** and the raw trunk-negotiation status ‚Äî the recon a switch-security audit needs. Decodes the **version** + the Domain (0x0001) / Status (0x0002) / DTP-Type (0x0003) / Neighbour (0x0004 ‚Üí MAC) TLVs; accepts the PDU itself or any frame carrying the LLC/SNAP DTP signature (OUI 0x00000C, PID 0x2004). **No confidently-wrong output**: DTP is Cisco-proprietary and reverse-engineered, and its status-bit semantics (the exact dynamic-desirable / dynamic-auto / trunk encoding) are **not authoritatively standardised**, so the status and trunk-type octets are surfaced **raw** (hex + decimal) rather than decoded into a named mode that could be wrong ‚Äî while the certain, high-value signal *is* stated: the mere presence of DTP means the port is participating in trunk negotiation (not 'nonegotiate'), the VLAN-hopping prerequisite. Native ‚Äî a short TLV walk, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's DTP layer** ‚Äî 200 random PDUs (varied domain / status / type / neighbour, versions 1-2) decode identically, zero mismatches; canonical vectors + the SNAP-wrapped form unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/dtp`. Registered as `dtp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 554‚Üí555.
- `macsec_decode` IEEE 802.1AE (MACsec) SecTAG ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.553.0 ‚Äî **new tool** bodying out a wired-L2 EtherType the existing decoders only *named*: the `vlan_decode` / VXLAN / Geneve EtherType tables already label `0x88E5` as "MACsec (802.1AE)", but nothing decoded its Security TAG. MACsec gives hop-by-hop L2 confidentiality + integrity on a wired LAN (keyed by 802.1X / MKA); the SecTAG is sent **in the clear**, so decoding it from a capture exposes the secure-channel identity, association number, replay-protection packet number and whether the user data is encrypted ‚Äî the visibility a **network-access-control / MACsec-deployment audit** needs (fits the project's wired-L2 decoder set alongside LLDP/CDP/STP/LACP). Decodes the **TCI flags** (Version, End-Station, SCI-present, Single-Copy-Broadcast, **Encryption** E, Changed-text C) + the 2-bit **Association Number**, the **Short Length**, the 32-bit **Packet Number**, and (when SC is set) the 64-bit **Secure Channel Identifier** split into its 48-bit system MAC + 16-bit port id; accepts either the SecTAG onward or a **full Ethernet frame** (0x88E5 ‚Üí outer dst/src MACs surfaced too), and splits the trailing data into Secure Data + the 16-octet ICV. **No confidently-wrong output**: the encrypted Secure Data is surfaced opaque and the ICV is *not* verified ‚Äî both need the Secure Association Key (SAK), which MKA derives and never puts on the wire (deferred, like the lorawan / wmbus encrypted payloads); the 16-octet ICV split assumes the mandatory GCM-AES cipher and says so. Native ‚Äî fixed public bit/byte layout (802.1AE-2006 ¬ß9.3), stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field against scapy's MACsec layer** ‚Äî 200 random SecTAGs (all TCI-flag combinations, SCI present/absent, SL, PN) decode identically, zero mismatches; canonical hand-built vectors unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/macsec`. Registered as `macsec_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 553‚Üí554.
- `bcbp_decode` IATA Bar Coded Boarding Pass (Resolution 792) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.552.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the travel-OSINT space (companion to `mrz_decode`): decodes the text encoded in the PDF417 / Aztec / QR barcode on a boarding pass. Boarding passes are routinely photographed, posted to social media and discarded intact, and the barcode leaks the **passenger name**, the **booking reference (PNR)** ‚Äî which with the surname is often enough to open the full reservation on the airline's site ‚Äî the **itinerary**, **seat**, **check-in sequence** and frequent-flyer data; decoding it is a recognised privacy-exposure / recon check. Decodes the mandatory fields (format code, leg count, passenger name, e-ticket indicator, and per leg the PNR, from/to airports, operating carrier, flight number, flight day-of-year, compartment class, seat, check-in sequence, passenger status); multi-leg passes supported. **No confidently-wrong output**: the mandatory fields are fixed-width (verified against the canonical IATA Resolution 792 example), and because every leg's conditional section is **length-prefixed** the leg boundaries are found from the declared hex sizes ‚Äî a multi-leg pass cannot be mis-sliced. The variable **conditional (airline-use) section is surfaced raw** rather than decoded field-by-field (its layout is version-dependent and airline-extensible, so guessing it would risk a wrong decode); the flight date is a day-of-year (1-366) with **no year encoded**, so it is surfaced as the raw day count and not resolved to a calendar date. Native ‚Äî fixed-width slicing driven by the self-describing length markers, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified against the canonical IATA 792 example** (`M1DESMARAIS/LUC‚Ä¶EABC123 YULFRAAC 0834 226F001A0025 100` ‚Üí DESMARAIS/LUC, PNR ABC123, YUL‚ÜíFRA on AC 0834, day 226, seat 001A) plus multi-leg and conditional-section round-trips. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/bcbp`. Registered as `bcbp_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 552‚Üí553.
- `mrz_decode` ICAO 9303 Machine Readable Zone (passport / ID / visa) ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.551.0 ‚Äî **new tool** decoding the `<`-padded OCR-B lines at the bottom of a travel document. **Directly relevant to the NFC tooling**: the MRZ is the input to the **Basic Access Control (BAC)** key derivation that unlocks an e-passport / e-ID **NFC chip** ‚Äî the document number, date of birth and date of expiry (each with its check digit) are hashed into the BAC seed ‚Äî so an MRZ read off the printed page is what lets a reader talk to the chip (a natural companion to the `iso14443*` / `nfc_*` tooling). Also a core OSINT / border-forensics artefact. Auto-detects the format (**TD3** passport 2√ó44, **TD1** ID card 3√ó30, **TD2** 2√ó36) and breaks out document type, issuing country, surname + given names, document number, nationality, date of birth, sex, date of expiry and the optional/personal-number field. **No confidently-wrong output**: every check digit (document number, DOB, expiry, optional field, composite) is independently recomputed with the ICAO **7-3-1 weighted-modulo-10** algorithm and compared ‚Äî per-field and overall `valid` are surfaced with a note naming any field that fails, and a valid check digit is *not* asserted to prove the document genuine (an MRZ can be mistyped or altered); the check digits are the verification anchor, as for the IMEI/ICCID Luhn and the VIN check digit. Dates are surfaced as raw YYMMDD plus an ISO rendering with the **century left unresolved** (the MRZ does not encode it, so 19xx/20xx is not guessed). Native ‚Äî fixed-width slicing + the public check-digit algorithm, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Verified field-for-field and check-digit-for-check-digit against the `mrz` reference library** for all three formats (e.g. the canonical ICAO TD3 `P<UTOERIKSSON<<ANNA<MARIA‚Ä¶` ‚Üí ERIKSSON / ANNA MARIA, doc L898902C3, DOB 740812, all check digits valid; the ICAO worked example `D23145890`‚Üí7, `740812`‚Üí2 is unit-pinned). Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/mrz`. Registered as `mrz_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 551‚Üí552.
- `iccid_decode` ICCID SIM-card-serial decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.550.0 ‚Äî **new tool completing the cellular identifier triad**: with `imei_decode` (the device) and `imsi_decode` (the subscriber, shipped v0.549), `iccid_decode` adds the **SIM card itself** ‚Äî the Integrated Circuit Card Identifier (ITU-T E.118 / ISO-IEC 7812) printed on and stored in every SIM/USIM. The three together are the identities a SIM-swap / forensic seizure / IMSI-catcher engagement enumerates. Breaks the ICCID into the **MII** (the leading `89` = telecom; a non-89 MII is flagged), the **E.164 country code** (1-3 digits after the MII ‚Üí issuing country / ISO region; E.164 codes are a prefix-free set so the code is parsed unambiguously by longest valid prefix, and a code shared by several territories ‚Äî NANP `+1`, the `+44` British-Isles group ‚Äî is flagged with its primary country), the **issuer + account** digits, and the trailing **Luhn check digit**. **The Luhn check digit is the verification anchor** (recomputed and compared ‚Äî a mismatch is reported as `luhn_valid=false` with a note, never asserted as definitively fake), exactly like the IMEI Luhn and VIN check-digit anchors. No confidently-wrong output: the issuer identifier and individual account number are **not split** from each other (the issuer-identifier length varies by operator with no public fixed rule ‚Äî surfaced combined, like `imei_decode` defers TAC‚Üídevice and `imsi_decode` defers the operator name). Native ‚Äî Luhn arithmetic + a prefix-table lookup, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep; the **E.164 calling-code ‚Üí country table is code-generated** from Google libphonenumber + pycountry (215 calling codes, machine-readable authoritative source) rather than hand-transcribed (`internal/iccid/callingcode_table.go`). Verified against an independent Luhn reference (the canonical `79927398713` vector) and machine-minted valid ICCIDs whose country resolves correctly (e.g. `89440000000000000002` ‚Üí +44 United Kingdom, Luhn-valid). Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/iccid`. Registered as `iccid_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 550‚Üí551.
- `imsi_decode` IMSI cellular subscriber-identity decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.549.0 ‚Äî **new tool** closing the **IMSI gap explicitly deferred by `imei_decode`**: the International Mobile Subscriber Identity is the up-to-15-digit number on a SIM/USIM that uniquely names a cellular subscriber, disclosed in plaintext in a GSM/LTE Identity Response ‚Äî the message an **IMSI-catcher** / cell-site simulator forces a handset to send (visible in a `gsmtap` capture). It is the subscriber-identity companion to `imei_decode` (the device identity); the two together are exactly what an IMSI-catcher harvests, and both are now decodable offline. Splits the IMSI into **MCC** (first 3 digits ‚Üí country, via the authoritative ITU-T E.212 assignment table), **MNC** (the 2- or 3-digit operator code, length country-determined) and **MSIN** (subscriber digits). **No confidently-wrong output**: the MCC‚Üícountry map is authoritative; the MNC/MSIN split was verified against the python-stdnum reference library across **all 2543 assigned MNCs of the 215 single-MNC-length countries ‚Äî zero mismatches**; the 22 countries that assign *both* 2- and 3-digit MNCs (e.g. USA 310, India 405) use the predominant length and are **flagged** (`mnc_length_assumed`) rather than asserted; and the operator (MNC‚Üícarrier name) lookup is **deferred** (proprietary, churns as carriers rename/merge ‚Äî like `imei_decode` defers the TAC‚Üídevice GSMA lookup), surfacing the numeric MNC instead. IMSI carries no check digit, so validity is structural (length + a known MCC). Native ‚Äî table lookup + a digit-field split, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep; the **MCC‚Üícountry + per-MCC MNC-length table is code-generated** from python-stdnum's `imsi.dat` (a machine-readable authoritative source) rather than hand-transcribed (`internal/imsi/mcc_table.go`, 237 MCCs). Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/imsi`. Registered as `imsi_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 549‚Üí550.
- `gps_nmea_decode` marine-instrument NMEA sentences ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.548.0 ‚Äî extended the NMEA decoder beyond the GPS/GNSS position sentences (GGA/RMC/GLL/VTG/GSA/GSV/GST/ZDA) with the **marine-instrument sentences** carried on a vessel's NMEA 0183 bus: **HDT** (true heading), **HDG** (magnetic heading + deviation + variation), **VHW** (water speed + true/magnetic heading), **DBT** (depth below transducer, feet/metres/fathoms), **DPT** (depth + transducer offset), **MTW** (water temperature), **MWV** (wind speed + angle, relative or true), **MWD** (wind direction + speed, true/magnetic, knots + m/s) and **ROT** (rate of turn). Maritime-cyber angle: NMEA 0183 is an **unauthenticated** bus, so a spoofed depth / heading / wind value injected onto it can mislead an autopilot or crew ‚Äî the maritime counterpart to GPS spoofing ‚Äî which makes decoding a captured marine NMEA stream a genuine integrity-analysis surface (companion to `ais_nmea_decode`, and the same "NMEA has no auth" problem that motivates the AIS work). Native ‚Äî string-split + the existing XOR-checksum / float-pointer helpers, stdlib only, no new dep; absent fields decode to null (never a zero), and E/W deviation/variation are sign-resolved. **Anchored field-for-field to pynmea2 1.19.0** ‚Äî the canonical example sentence for each type reproduces its decoded heading / depth / wind / temperature / rate-of-turn fields exactly (e.g. `$SDDBT,17.5,f,5.3,M,2.9,F` ‚Üí 17.5 ft / 5.3 m / 2.9 fathoms; `$HCHDG,98.3,0.0,E,12.6,W` ‚Üí heading 98.3¬∞, variation ‚àí12.6¬∞ W). Fuzz-clean (~3.3M execs). `internal/nmea`. No new tool (extends `gps_nmea_decode`) ‚Äî registry unchanged at 549.
- `rtcm_decode` RTCM 3.x differential-GNSS messages ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.547.0 ‚Äî **new tool** completing the **GNSS protocol triad**: after `gps_nmea_decode` (text output) and `ubx_decode` (u-blox binary input), `rtcm_decode` handles the *corrections* leg ‚Äî the messages a GNSS **base station** broadcasts (over radio / NTRIP / serial) to feed real-time RTK corrections to rovers. **GNSS-integrity angle**: injecting forged RTCM corrections (a false 1005 reference-station position, or fabricated observables) is a known way to pull an RTK rover off its true fix ‚Äî decoding a stream surfaces the reference-station id, the broadcast base ECEF position, and which message types / constellations a stream carries, flagging an anomalous or spoofed correction source. Decodes + validates: the **transport frame** (`0xD3` preamble + 10-bit length + the **CRC-24Q** poly 0x1864CFB over the whole frame; a stream of back-to-back frames decodes to a list, leading non-preamble bytes are skipped, and a frame whose CRC fails is not emitted ‚Äî a bad CRC reads as a false sync); the **message type** (DF002) with names for the common types (1001-1004/1009-1012 legacy RTK observables, 1005/1006 station ARP, 1007/1008/1033 descriptors, 1019/1020/1042-1046 ephemerides, the 107x-112x MSM families per constellation, 1230 GLONASS biases) plus the **reference-station id** (DF003) for the types that carry it; and the **1005/1006 Stationary RTK Reference Station ARP** body ‚Äî the base antenna reference point as ECEF X/Y/Z (metres, from the 38-bit 0.0001 m fields), the GPS/GLONASS/Galileo service indicators, and (1006) the antenna height. The CRC-24Q gate means no confidently-wrong output; observable/ephemeris/MSM bodies are CRC-validated + type/station-named with the per-satellite payload surfaced as raw hex rather than guessed (1005/1006 are bodied out because they carry the base position an integrity check cares about). Native ‚Äî fixed public wire format + a bit reader + a CRC loop, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored to the pyrtcm reference library**: a real 1005 frame reproduces its decoded station-id (2003) + ECEF (1114104.60 / ‚àí4850729.71 / 3975521.46 m) exactly, and a 1006 frame (1005 + 1.5 m antenna height) round-trips through pyrtcm; the CRC-24Q check value (0xCDE703, distinct from the OpenPGP CRC-24's 0x21CF02) is unit-pinned. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/rtcm`. Registered as `rtcm_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 548‚Üí549.
- `ubx_decode` UBX NAV-SAT + NAV-STATUS body decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.546.0 ‚Äî extended the UBX decoder beyond NAV-PVT with the two messages that complete the GNSS picture: **NAV-SAT** (per-satellite signal info ‚Äî for every tracked SV the constellation (GPS / SBAS / Galileo / BeiDou / QZSS / GLONASS / NavIC), satellite id, C/N0, elevation / azimuth, pseudorange residual, the signal-quality indicator, whether it is used in the solution and its 2-bit health) and **NAV-STATUS** (fix type + the gnssFixOK / differential-solution / week-number / time-of-week status flags + time-to-first-fix + receiver uptime). NAV-SAT is the highest-value addition for this project: anomalous per-satellite C/N0 or geometry is the primary tell of **GPS spoofing / jamming**, so it is the UBX counterpart to the NMEA GSV decode and directly serves the GPS-spoof-detection use case for a tracking / wardriving rig. Native ‚Äî variable-length per-SV bit-field extraction (8 + 12¬∑numSvs) + a 4-byte flags dword (qualityInd bits 0-2, svUsed bit 3, health bits 4-5, ephAvail bit 11), stdlib only, no new dep. **Anchored field-for-field to pyubx2 1.3.1** ‚Äî a 2-satellite NAV-SAT frame (a used/healthy GPS SV with qualityInd 7 + a unused/unhealthy GLONASS SV) and a NAV-STATUS frame (3D fix, fixOK, week+TOW set, TTFF 3500 ms) minted by pyubx2 reproduce its decoded fields exactly. The previously-undecoded-message test now pins NAV-POSLLH (still frame-only). Fuzz-clean (~8s). `internal/ubx`. No new tool (extends `ubx_decode`) ‚Äî registry unchanged at 548.
- `ubx_decode` u-blox UBX binary GNSS protocol ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.545.0 ‚Äî **new tool** closing the binary half of the GPS/GNSS decode space: u-blox receivers (the NEO-6/7/8/9 family ‚Äî the dominant GNSS chips, in countless wardriving / drone / GPS-tracker rigs, including modules paired with the Flipper / Marauder) speak the compact **UBX binary protocol** as the alternative to NMEA text, and a UBX capture is undecodable by `gps_nmea_decode`. `ubx_decode` is its **binary counterpart**: decodes the UBX frame envelope (`0xB5 0x62` sync, class+id named for the common NAV/RXM/CFG/MON classes, little-endian length) and validates the **8-bit Fletcher checksum** (CK_A/CK_B over class+id+length+payload); a stream of back-to-back frames decodes to a list and leading non-sync bytes are skipped so a mid-stream capture still parses. **NAV-PVT** (the flagship position/velocity/time message) is fully bodied out: iTOW, UTC date/time + validity flags + time accuracy, fix type (no-fix / DR / 2D / 3D / GNSS+DR / time-only) + gnssFixOK, satellites used, lon/lat, height (ellipsoid + MSL), horizontal/vertical accuracy, the NED velocity vector, ground speed, heading of motion, and position DOP ‚Äî with the raw integer units (mm, mm/s, deg√ó1e-7, deg√ó1e-5, 0.01 DOP) converted to metres / m¬∑s‚Åª¬π / degrees. Other UBX messages are frame-decoded + class/id-named with the body surfaced as raw hex rather than guessed (NAV-PVT is the one message that carries a whole fix; others can land later against a vector). Native ‚Äî fixed public wire format + a two-byte checksum loop, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep. **Anchored field-for-field to pyubx2 1.3.1**: a NAV-PVT frame minted by pyubx2 from known values (Munich, 3D fix, 9 SV) reproduces its decoded time/position/velocity/accuracy fields exactly, and the Fletcher checksum + bad-checksum-flagging + leading-garbage-skip + back-to-back-stream paths are unit-tested. Fuzz-clean (~9s). `internal/ubx`. Registered as `ubx_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 547‚Üí548.
- `ais_nmea_decode` AIS Type 9 + Type 27 body decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.544.0 ‚Äî rounded out the AIS decoder's **dynamic position coverage** with the last two position-bearing message types that were name-labelled only: **Type 9 SAR Aircraft Position Report** (the broadcast from a search-and-rescue helicopter / fixed-wing ‚Äî altitude in place of nav status, whole-knot speed, position, course, timestamp, DTE/assigned/RAIM) and **Type 27 Long-Range Position Report** (the compressed broadcast meant for satellite reception ‚Äî nav status, coarse 1/10-minute position, whole-knot speed, whole-degree course, RAIM, and the GNSS position-latency flag). With these, every AIS *position* report an offline receiver sees (Types 1/2/3/9/18/19/27) now bodies out fully. Native ‚Äî bit-field extraction reusing the package's signed-coordinate / nav-status helpers, stdlib only, no new dep. Note the resolution/units differences these two types carry vs the Class-A reports: Type 9 speed and Type 27 speed are *whole knots* (not deciknots), Type 27 course is *whole degrees*, and Type 27 position is the coarse 1/10-minute scale (`/600`, not `/600000`) with 18/17-bit signed lon/lat. **Anchored field-for-field to pyais 3.0.1** ‚Äî Type 27 against a real satellite-AIS sentence (137.02¬∞E/4.84¬∞N, 57 kn, Not-under-command), Type 9 against a sentence minted by pyais's *encoder* from known values (350 m / 95 kn SAR aircraft) then cross-decoded, so the bit layout is checked against independent code. Fuzz-clean (~8s). `internal/ais`. No new tool (extends `ais_nmea_decode`) ‚Äî registry unchanged at 547.
- `ais_nmea_decode` AIS Type 19 + Type 21 body decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.543.0 ‚Äî extended the existing AIS decoder (which bodied out Types 1/2/3/4/5/18/24) with two more high-traffic message types that were previously name-labelled only: **Type 19 Extended Class B Position Report** (Type-18's position fields *plus* vessel name, ship type and dimensions ‚Äî a single 312-bit message that doubles as static data for small craft) and **Type 21 Aid-to-Navigation Report** (how buoys, lighthouses, RACONs, beacons and *virtual* AtoNs broadcast ‚Äî full 32-entry aid-type table per ITU-R M.1371-5 Table 76, name with the 0-88-bit extension field, position, dimensions, EPFD, timestamp, and the off-position / virtual-aid / assigned flags). Maritime recon: Type 21 enumerates the navigation marks (and exposes spoofed/virtual AtoNs ‚Äî a known AIS attack surface), Type 19 ties small-craft identity to position. Native ‚Äî bit-field extraction reusing the package's existing 6-bit-ASCII / signed-coordinate / ship-type / EPFD helpers, stdlib only, no new dep. **Anchored field-for-field to pyais 3.0.1** decode() of real sentences (Type 19 `CAPT.J.RIMES` cargo vessel at 29.54¬∞N/‚àí88.81¬∞E; Type 21 multi-fragment AtoN incl. the `EXTENDED NAME` overflow field) ‚Äî and the decoder correctly rejects the bad NMEA checksums that the widely-circulated AtoN test vector ships with (pyais skips checksum validation; we don't, so the corrected `*79`/`*62` suffixes are used). Fuzz-clean (~3.3M execs). `internal/ais`. No new tool (extends `ais_nmea_decode`) ‚Äî registry unchanged at 547.
- `meshtastic_decode` Meshtastic LoRa-mesh packet header ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.542.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the LoRa-mesh decode space (and the fire that broke a two-hold lull by finding an *accessible-reference* target): **Meshtastic**, the dominant off-grid LoRa mesh-comms project. The 16-byte packet header is sent in the clear before the AES-encrypted payload, so decoding it from a Flipper Sub-GHz / SDR LoRa capture **enumerates the nodes in mesh range** (source + destination node IDs in the `!xxxxxxxx` form), reveals the **channel hash** (fingerprints which channel a packet belongs to ‚Äî same name+PSK ‚Üí same hash), and exposes the hop / want-ack / via-MQTT routing flags (hops-taken = hop_start ‚àí hop_limit) ‚Äî passive mesh reconnaissance without touching the air. Also surfaces packet ID, next-hop and relay-node bytes, and the encrypted payload (length + hex). **Verified against the Meshtastic firmware wire layout** (RadioInterface.h PacketHeader ‚Äî little-endian uint32 to/from/id, then flags/channel/next_hop/relay_node ‚Äî and the PACKET_FLAGS_* masks, both fetched from the firmware source): broadcast (0xFFFFFFFF ‚Üí `^all`) and directed (`!a1b2c3d4`) headers, the flag decode (hop_limit/want_ack/via_mqtt/hop_start) and hops-taken, channel hash and routing bytes all anchored. The AES-256-CTR (or PKI, for DMs) encrypted MeshPacket payload needs the channel PSK / node key (not on the wire) and is deferred ‚Äî surfaced as ciphertext. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + bit-masking, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `meshtastic_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 546‚Üí547.
- `lin_frame_decode` LIN automotive body-bus frame ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.541.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the automotive decode space: **LIN** (Local Interconnect Network, ISO 17987 / LIN 2.x), the low-cost single-wire sub-bus that hangs off CAN for body electronics ‚Äî door / mirror / seat modules, climate flaps, wiper and rain/light sensors, switch panels. LIN is a real automotive reverse-engineering / pentest surface (cheap to tap, usually unauthenticated) and is **distinct from the CAN family** the existing automotive decoders cover (canbus_fd_decode / isotp_decode / uds_decode / obd2_*). Decodes the **Protected Identifier** (6-bit frame ID + the two parity bits, with the parity recomputed ‚Äî P0 = ID0^ID1^ID2^ID4, P1 = !(ID1^ID3^ID4^ID5) ‚Äî and reported valid/invalid) + the frame class (signal / master-request or slave-response diagnostic [0x3C/0x3D] / user-defined / reserved); the data bytes; and the **checksum**, computing both the classic (data-only, LIN 1.x + diagnostics) and enhanced (PID + data, LIN 2.x) inverted carry-folded sums and reporting which the frame uses (or invalid). An optional leading 0x55 sync byte is tolerated. **Verified against the standard LIN PID constants** (frame ID 0x3C‚ÜíPID 0x3C, 0x3D‚Üí0x7D, 0x00‚Üí0x80, 0x01‚Üí0xC1, 0x02‚Üí0x42 ‚Äî anchoring the error-prone parity-bit positions to real LIN values) and the carry-folded checksum (the carry-fold edge case 0x80+0x80‚Üí0x01‚Üí0xFE distinguishing it from a plain sum); enhanced / classic-diagnostic / sync-byte / bad-parity / bad-checksum paths all covered. Signal (LDF/DBC) interpretation of the data bytes (needs the vehicle's LIN Description File) is deferred ‚Äî raw data surfaced. Native ‚Äî two parity XOR equations + one carry-folded checksum, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `lin_frame_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 545‚Üí546.
- `wmbus_decode` transport header + encryption detection ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.540.0 ‚Äî extended the v0.539 wM-Bus radio decoder with the **transport-protocol-layer (TPL) header** (EN 13757-3) that follows the CI field ‚Äî and, the headline, **encryption detection**: short (CI 0x7A) / long (0x72) / none (0x78) header dispatch, the access number + status byte, and the **encryption mode** decoded from the configuration word (`mode = (cfg>>8)&0x1F`): plaintext (0) vs **AES-128-CBC** (mode 5 dynamic-IV / mode 7 no-IV), with the encrypted-block count and the bidirectional / accessibility / synchronous flags. The long-header (0x72) embedded device address (which can differ from the link-layer M/A) is surfaced too. Whether a meter's payload is readable or AES-encrypted (and which mode) is the first thing a smart-meter RF assessment needs ‚Äî it determines whether the consumption is directly readable or requires key recovery. **Verified** against CRC-valid Format-A frames carrying complete short TPL headers: an unencrypted one (config 0x0000 ‚Üí mode 0, plaintext) and an AES-CBC one (config 0x0520 ‚Üí mode 5, 2 encrypted blocks); the config-word bit layout (`cfg2<<8|cfg1`, mode/flags/block-count) ported from the wmbusmeters reference. AES decryption itself needs the meter key (not in the frame) and is deferred ‚Äî the mode is reported. Native ‚Äî pure byte-field extraction, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `wmbus_decode` (`internal/wmbus`); registry unchanged.
- `wmbus_decode` Wireless M-Bus (868 MHz) radio frame ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.539.0 ‚Äî **new tool** filling the wM-Bus radio-framing gap that `internal/mbus` **explicitly deferred** ("wM-Bus radio framing (mode S/T/C, 3-of-6 / Manchester) is out of scope"): **Wireless M-Bus** (EN 13757-4), the 868 MHz over-the-air framing smart water / heat / gas / electricity meters broadcast and a Flipper Sub-GHz capture lifts off the air. The wired decoder handles the shared application layer; this adds the radio-specific frame ‚Äî and reading these telegrams **enumerates the meters in radio range** (manufacturer, ID, type) and validates integrity, the passive-recon start of a smart-meter RF assessment. Decodes (Format A): the L (length) field + the block layout with **every block's CRC-16** (EN 13757 poly 0x3D65, init 0, final XOR 0xFFFF) recomputed and validated; **block 1** ‚Äî the C (control) field (+ name SND-NR / SND-IR / ‚Ä¶), the **manufacturer** (3-letter FLAG code from the M field), the **BCD meter ID**, version and **device/medium type** (+ name water / gas / heat / electricity / ‚Ä¶); and the **de-chunked application payload** (CRCs stripped, concatenated) + its CI field, ready to feed into `mbus_decode`. **Verified** against a CRC-valid Format-A frame (Elster gas, ID 12345678, payload 7A2A0020) and, crucially, the **CRC-16 anchored to a real meter header block** `2e449315785634123303` ‚Üí 0x3363 (the header decoding cleanly to a genuine Elster gas meter confirms it is real-world data, not a self-constructed vector); manufacturer FLAG (0x1593‚ÜíELS, 0x2C2D‚ÜíKAM) and corrupt-CRC detection also covered. Format B (single trailing CRC) is detected by CRC mismatch and noted; the line coding (upstream) and DIF/VIF app decode (`mbus_decode`'s job) are deferred. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + one standard CRC-16, stdlib only, no new dep; reimplemented from EN 13757-4, not wrapped. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `wmbus_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 544‚Üí545.
- `dsmr_p1_decode` DSMR / P1 smart-meter telegram ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.538.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the smart-metering / energy-IoT decode space: **DSMR / P1**, the ASCII data stream a Dutch / Belgian (and increasingly EU) smart electricity / gas meter pushes out of its P1 customer port every second. Reading the P1 stream is the energy-side data-exfiltration / monitoring surface ‚Äî per-tariff energy import & export, instantaneous and per-phase power, per-phase voltage / current, gas volume, power-outage counters and the meter equipment IDs. Per DSMR 5.0 / IEC 62056-21. Decodes the meter identifier line, the **CRC-16/ARC** (over `/`‚Ä¶`!` inclusive ‚Äî recomputed and validated, so a tampered/truncated telegram is caught; CRLF endings normalised first so an LF-only paste still validates), and every **OBIS object line** (`C-D:E.F.G(value*unit)`) with its documented meaning + parsed value/unit (energy per tariff, +P/-P power, per-phase V/A/W, sag/swell + power-failure counters, the gas M-Bus channel, IDs, timestamp, active tariff); unknown OBIS codes surfaced raw. **Verified byte-for-byte against the dsmr_parser reference telegram** (KFM5KAIFA-METER): the CRC-16/ARC reproduces the telegram's published `!6796` exactly, energy import tariff-1 = 001581.123 kWh, instantaneous power 02.027 kW, gas reading 00981.443 m3, L2 current 006 A ‚Äî plus the LF-normalisation and tamper-detection paths. Native ‚Äî string parse + one standard CRC-16 + a documented OBIS table, stdlib only, no new dep; the field interpretation reference parsers leave implicit is implemented directly. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `dsmr_p1_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 543‚Üí544.
- `enocean_decode` EnOcean ESP3 / ERP1 building-automation radio ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.537.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the sub-GHz building-automation decode space: **EnOcean** (the self-powered 868 / 902 / 315 MHz protocol behind batteryless light switches, occupancy / window-contact / temperature sensors and actuators ‚Äî a real RF pentest surface, squarely in the Flipper sub-GHz wheelhouse). A USB gateway (USB300/USB400J) or an SDR emits ESP3 frames; decoding them gives the device identity (32-bit sender ID), telegram type, signal strength and an integrity check ‚Äî the recon a building-automation RF pentest starts from. Decodes the **ESP3 framing** (0x55 sync + 16-bit data length + optional length + packet type [+ name] + a **header CRC-8 and a data CRC-8**, both recomputed and validated) and the **RADIO_ERP1 telegram**: the **RORG** type with its name (RPS rocker-switch 0xF6, 1BS contact 0xD5, 4BS sensor 0xA5, VLD 0xD2, MSC, UTE teach-in, secure 0x30/0x31/0x35), the payload, the 32-bit sender ID, the status byte + repeater count, and the optional data (sub-telegram count, destination ID, **RSSI in -dBm**, security level). **Verified against a CRC-8-valid RADIO_ERP1 reference frame** `55 00 07 07 01 7A F6 30 00 29 28 9C 30 03 FF FF FF FF 3D 00 DD` ‚Üí RPS from sender 0029289C, header CRC-8 0x7A + data CRC-8 0xDD both valid, RSSI -61 dBm; the CRC-8 (poly 0x07) reproduced byte-for-byte. EEP (device-profile) payload decode is deferred ‚Äî the meaning of the data bytes depends on the FUNC/TYPE profile the telegram does not carry, so decoding it would be a confidently-wrong guess; raw payload + RORG are surfaced. Native ‚Äî byte-field extraction + a table-driven CRC-8, stdlib only, no new dep; reimplemented from the ESP3 spec / kipe enocean reference, not wrapped. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `enocean_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 542‚Üí543.
- `eas_same_decode` EAS / SAME emergency-alert header ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.536.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the RF-broadcast / SDR decode space: **EAS / SAME** (Specific Area Message Encoding), the AFSK digital header that prefixes every Emergency Alert System and NOAA Weather Radio alert (the `ZCZC‚Ä¶` burst at 520.83 baud on 162 MHz weather radio / broadcast EAS). A demodulator (multimon-ng, rtl_fm) recovers the raw header string; this **interprets its fields** ‚Äî the part multimon-ng leaves to the operator. Per NWS NWSI 10-1712 / FCC 47 CFR 11.31, format `ZCZC-ORG-EEE-PSSCCC‚Ä¶+TTTT-JJJHHMM-LLLLLLLL-`: originator (PEP/CIV/WXR/EAS/EAN), the FCC/NWS event-code table (RWT/RMT tests, TOR/SVR/FFW/HUW/TSW weather warnings, watches, statements, and civil events like CAE child-abduction, CEM, EVI, NUW ‚Äî with a third-letter fallback for unrecognised codes: ‚Ä¶W warning / ‚Ä¶A watch / ‚Ä¶E emergency / ‚Ä¶S statement), the FIPS location codes (part-of-county digit + state FIPS ‚Üí state name + county FIPS), the valid/purge duration (TTTT hhmm) and issue time (JJJHHMM ordinal-day + UTC), and the 8-char callsign. **Verified against the documented NWS worked example** `ZCZC-EAS-RWT-012057-012081-012101-012103-012115+0030-2780415-WTSP/TV-` ‚Üí EAS Participant / Required Weekly Test / 5 Florida counties (FIPS state 12) / valid 30 min / day 278 04:15 UTC / WTSP/TV ‚Äî plus a WXR/TOR Texas tornado example and the unknown-suffix fallback. County-FIPS‚Üíname (~3200 entries) and ordinal-day‚Üícalendar-date (no year in the header) are deferred ‚Äî state name + raw FIPS surfaced. Native ‚Äî deterministic string parse + three documented lookup tables (originator / event / state-FIPS), stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. Registered as `eas_same_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 541‚Üí542.
- `osdp_packet_decode` reply payload decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.535.0 ‚Äî extended the v0.534 OSDP dissector with **typed reply-payload field decode** for the codes that carry a well-defined plaintext layout: **osdp_RAW** (card-read ‚Äî reader number, format [raw/wiegand/ascii], bit count, and the **card data** itself, the actual badge bits to feed into `wiegand_decode` / `rfid_pacs_decode`), **osdp_PDID** (device fingerprint ‚Äî vendor OUI, model, version, serial number, firmware version), **osdp_COM** (address + baud rate), **osdp_KEYPAD** (PIN key presses, rendered ASCII) and **osdp_LSTATR** (tamper + power). The wire layouts are ported verbatim from the libosdp reference reply builder (`src/osdp_pd.c`), which states each field's width and endianness explicitly (bwrite_u16_le / u24_le / u32_le / u24_be ‚Äî e.g. PDID's firmware is u24 **big**-endian while its serial is u32 little-endian). Verified by decoding packets constructed field-by-field to that exact layout with a valid CRC (the framing CRC itself was independently anchored to libosdp's own phy vectors in v0.534): card-read bit-count 26 + 4 card bytes, PDID vendor 0x00A1B2 / serial 0x12345678 / firmware 1.2.3, COM 9600 baud, keypad "1234", LSTATR tamper/power. Command (CP‚ÜíPD) parameter decode (LED/BUZ/OUT/TEXT) and secure-channel-encrypted payloads remain deferred (surfaced as hex). Native ‚Äî pure byte-field extraction, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `osdp_packet_decode` (`internal/osdp`); registry unchanged.
- `osdp_packet_decode` OSDP reader-bus dissector ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.534.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the physical access-control decode space: **OSDP** (Open Supervised Device Protocol, SIA / IEC 60839-11-5), the RS-485 serial protocol modern access-control readers speak to their controllers ‚Äî the secure successor to Wiegand. An OSDP bus tap is a stream of these packets; dissecting them shows the poll/reply traffic, the card-read replies, the secure-channel handshake and any integrity failures ‚Äî a staple of an access-control pentest. Decodes the full frame: optional 0xFF driver mark + 0x53 SOM + address byte (bit 7 = reply direction, low 7 = PD address, 0x7F broadcast) + 16-bit length + control byte (2-bit sequence number, CRC-vs-checksum mode, secure-channel-block flag); the security control block (length + type + meaning, SCS_11..SCS_18) when present; the command (CP‚ÜíPD) / reply (PD‚ÜíCP) code with its name (osdp_POLL / osdp_ID / osdp_RAW card-read / osdp_ACK / osdp_NAK / ‚Ä¶); the NAK error code with its meaning; and **trailer integrity** ‚Äî the CRC-16/AUG-CCITT (poly 0x1021, init 0x1D0F) or the 1-byte two's-complement checksum is recomputed and reported valid/invalid. **Verified byte-for-byte against the libosdp phy-layer reference test vectors** (`tests/unit-tests/test-cp-phy.c`): the POLL command `53 65 08 00 04 60 60 90` (CRC 0x9060), the ID command with data, the ACK reply in checksum mode (`53 e5 07 00 01 40 80`, checksum 0x80), and the NAK reply with error 0x01 ‚Üí "message check error" (`53 e5 09 00 05 41 01 0e 8f`, CRC 0x8f0e) ‚Äî plus the mark-byte and corrupt-trailer paths. Native ‚Äî pure byte-field extraction + the standard CRC, stdlib only, no new dep; the libosdp reference is reimplemented, not wrapped. Fuzz-clean (2.6M execs). Registered as `osdp_packet_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 540‚Üí541. Per-payload field decode (osdp_RAW card-data layout etc.) and secure-channel-encrypted payloads are deferred (data surfaced as hex, code name identifies it).
- `rds_decode` group 0A alternative frequencies ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.533.0 ‚Äî decoded the **alternative-frequency (AF) list** in group 0A ‚Äî the VHF frequencies a station simulcasts on (EN 50067 Annex D), the other half of the most-common RDS group (PS being the first). The AF codes in block C are decoded to a flat, de-duplicated kHz list (code 1-204 ‚Üí 87.5 MHz + code√ó0.1 MHz), the "N AFs follow" count filler (225-249) is surfaced as `af_count`, and the LF/MF marker (250) is noted without a confidently-wrong VHF mis-decode. **Verified byte-for-byte against the redsea Method A test vector**: YLE Yksi ‚Üí {87900, 90900, 89800, 89200, 93200, 88500, 89500} kHz with count 7 (all seven distinct codes check against the linear formula). **Clock-time (group 4A) was investigated and deliberately re-deferred**: the redsea reference produces its clock_time via `mktime`/`localtime` with the UTC offset stuffed into `tm_sec`, making its output timezone/implementation dependent (the negative-offset vector keeps the UTC calendar date rather than rolling back) ‚Äî there is no trustworthy deterministic oracle to verify a port against, so a wrong datetime would be worse than none. The AF Method B same-programme/regional-variant structuring is also deferred (a Method B station's flat list still contains its tuned frequency; clearly noted). Native ‚Äî pure bit-field extraction + the standard AF formula, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `rds_decode` (`internal/rds`); registry unchanged.
- `rds_decode` group 1A + 10A ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.532.0 ‚Äî rounded out the v0.531 RDS decoder with two more of the common groups: **group 1A** (Programme Item Number ‚Äî the day + time the current programme started ‚Äî plus the linkage flag and the slow-labelling variants: extended country code, **language** name, TMC identification, SLC broadcaster bits, emergency-warning field) and **group 10A Programme Type Name** (the 8-character long-form programme-type label). **Verified byte-for-byte against the redsea reference test vectors** (`test/components-hex.cc`): programme item 31828 ‚Üí day 15 / 17:20 with ECC 0xE1 + PI country nibble 6 (YLE Yksi); language "Finnish" (code 0x27); SLC broadcaster bits 0x5AB (RTL 102.5); and Programme Type Name "CRI.CN " ‚Äî the last exercising the exact RDS terminator-rendering semantics (expected length runs to the first 0x0D, which itself renders as a blank, and unlike RadioText the PTYN is **not** right-trimmed, so the trailing space is preserved). The 128-entry RDS language table is ported verbatim. The ECC‚Üícountry-name table (a 300-cell 2D lookup with only one reachable test cell) is deliberately deferred ‚Äî the raw extended country code + PI country nibble are surfaced instead, rather than ship 299 unverified cells. Native ‚Äî pure bit-field extraction + the language table, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean (2.8M execs). No new tool ‚Äî extends `rds_decode` (`internal/rds`); registry unchanged. Clock-time (4A), AF lists, ODA/TMC, EON and the country-name table remain deferred (group type still reported).
- `rds_decode` RDS / RBDS FM Radio Data System ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.531.0 ‚Äî **new tool** for the FM-broadcast / SDR decode space: **RDS / RBDS** (Radio Data System), the 57 kHz digital sub-carrier riding on every FM station ‚Äî the data an rtl_fm ‚Üí redsea pipeline (or any RDS tuner) pulls off the air, and a staple of broadcast-RF spectrum survey. Per IEC 62106 (RDS) / NRSC-4 (RBDS). Decodes from the post-demod block hex (four 16-bit blocks A/B/C/D per group): **PI** code + the **RBDS four-letter call sign** derived from it (K/W stations, e.g. PI 0x4569 ‚Üí KUFX); group type (0A..15B) + **TP** flag + **PTY** programme type with both the European RDS and North American RBDS name tables; **group 0A/0B Programme Service name** (8 chars, assembled across segments) + TA / MS / DI flags; **group 2A/2B RadioText** (up to 64 chars, assembled + truncated at the 0x0D terminator); and the full **RDS G0 character set** (Annex E) so non-ASCII station text renders correctly. **Verified byte-for-byte against the redsea reference test vectors** (`test/components-hex.cc`): Programme Service "YLE X3M" (PI 0x6204, PTY "Varied", TA on) and "  KRKA"; RadioText "JACK 96.9", "Robbie Williams - Feel", and "Vega Kv√§ll" (the last exercising the G0 charset's 0x91‚Üí√§); RBDS call sign KUFX. Native ‚Äî pure bit-field extraction + the G0 charset + PTY tables + the RBDS PI‚Üícall-sign arithmetic, stdlib only, no DSP, no crypto, no new dep; the redsea decoder is reimplemented, not wrapped. Fuzz-clean (2.8M execs). Registered as `rds_decode` (Low risk, pure offline parser); registry 539‚Üí540. Deferred (group type still reported): clock-time (4A), alternative-frequency lists, ODA/TMC (3A/8A), EON (14), PIN (1A), PTYN (10A), legacy three-letter/linked call signs.
- `adsb_mode_s_decode` surveillance altitude + squawk ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.530.0 ‚Äî decoded the **AC13 pressure altitude** (DF0/4/16/20) and **ID13 Mode-A squawk** (DF5/21) from the 13-bit field at message bits 20-32 ‚Äî the surveillance header fields the v0.529 Comm-B note had left deferred, and which apply across all six surveillance downlink formats (not just Comm-B). Altitude decodes all three ICAO encodings: the 25-ft Q-bit form, the **Gillham (Mode C) gray-coded 100-ft** form (gray2alt + gray2int ported from pyModeS), and the metric M-bit form. Squawk decodes the 4-digit octal Mode-A code and **flags the three reserved emergency codes ‚Äî 7500 (unlawful interference / hijack), 7600 (radio failure), 7700 (general emergency)** ‚Äî a genuinely useful passive security signal. **Verified byte-for-byte against the pyModeS reference** (py_common.altcode / idcode): squawks 1200/4721 + all three emergency codes; altitudes 5000ft & -1000ft (25-ft), 38000ft & 25000ft & -1200ft (Gillham Q=0); plus the real DF20 Comm-B frames cross-checked at 3300 / 30275 / 5450 ft. Vectors generated by brute-forcing the 13-bit field against the pyModeS oracle for each target value, then truncated to valid short/long frames and re-confirmed. Native ‚Äî extends the existing Mode S decoder, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean (3.7M execs, DF4/DF5 seeds added). No new tool ‚Äî extends `adsb_mode_s_decode` (`internal/adsb`); registry unchanged. The Mode S decode is now comprehensive across the civil DF set: ADS-B ES (DF17/18) + Comm-B BDS (DF20/21) + surveillance altitude/identity (DF0/4/5/16/20/21).
- `adsb_mode_s_decode` Comm-B BDS register decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.529.0 ‚Äî decoded the **Mode S Comm-B (DF20/21) BDS registers** (ICAO Doc 9871), the data-link replies that carry aircraft *intent* and state ADS-B doesn't ‚Äî and the one DF20/21 capability the package explicitly flagged as deferred ("a separate ~600 LoC effort"). A Comm-B reply's 56-bit MB field is **not self-describing**: the same bits could be any BDS register and the frame says nothing about which. So the register is **inferred via validity gates** (reproducing pyModeS `is10/is17/is20/is40/is50/is60`): a register is only reported when its status bits are internally consistent and its decoded values fall in the physically valid range, and when more than one gate passes the result is flagged ambiguous rather than guessed ‚Äî the no-confidently-wrong ethos applied structurally. Decodes **BDS 2,0** (aircraft identification / callsign), **BDS 4,0** (selected vertical intention ‚Äî MCP/FCU + FMS selected altitude + barometric pressure setting), **BDS 5,0** (track + turn report ‚Äî roll, true track, ground speed, track-angle rate, true airspeed), **BDS 6,0** (heading + speed report ‚Äî magnetic heading, IAS, Mach, barometric + inertial vertical rate), and **BDS 1,7** (GICB capability list); BDS 1,0 participates in inference. **Verified byte-for-byte against the official pyModeS reference test vectors** (`tests/test_commb.py`): KLM1017_ / IBK2873_ callsigns, 3008ft MCP+FMS / 1020mb (BDS40), roll 2.109375¬∞ / track 114.258¬∞ / gs 438 / tas 424 (BDS50), heading 42.715¬∞ / IAS 252 / Mach 0.42 / vertical rate -1920fpm (BDS60) ‚Äî each frame validating under exactly its own gate. Caught a real cross-version subtlety: pyModeS v2.18 added an all-ones "no-data" sentinel guard to the track-angle-rate field that older releases lack ‚Äî the newer/correct behaviour is implemented. Native ‚Äî extends the existing Mode S decoder, stdlib only, no new dep. Fuzz-clean (3.2M execs). No new tool ‚Äî extends `adsb_mode_s_decode` (`internal/adsb`); registry unchanged. The Gillham-coded DF20/21 altitude/squawk header fields and meteorological BDS 4,4 / 4,5 remain deferred.
- `quic_long_header_decode` Retry integrity verification ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.528.0 ‚Äî added **QUIC Retry Integrity Tag verification** (RFC 9001 ¬ß5.8), the last unverified element of QUIC long-header forensics (after v0.526 Initial decryption + v0.527 JA4-q). A server's Retry packet ends with a 16-byte AES-128-GCM tag computed, with empty plaintext, over the Retry Pseudo-Packet (`ODCID-length ‚Äñ original-DCID ‚Äñ Retry-without-tag`) under a fixed per-version key/nonce ‚Äî no secret involved, so anyone with the packet bytes and the client's original DCID can recompute it.
