The decoder previously surfaced the tag as opaque hex; now, when the operator supplies `original_dcid` (the connection ID the client chose in its first Initial ‚Äî echoed by the integrity check but absent from the Retry packet itself), the tag is recomputed and reported as `integrity_verified` true/false, flagging forged / corrupt / off-path Retries (Retry-injection detection). **Verified byte-for-byte against the RFC 9001 Appendix A.4 worked example** ‚Äî the A.4 Retry (`ff000000010008f067a5502a4262b574‚Ä¶`) with original DCID `8394c8f03e515708` reproduces the published tag `04a265ba2eff4d829058fb3f0f2496ba`; tampering any byte of the tag or token, or supplying the wrong DCID, fails verification (constant-time compare). Only QUIC v1 is verified (v2/drafts use different Retry keys with no anchoring vector ‚Üí reported, not guessed); fuzz-clean (3.5M execs). Native ‚Äî Go-stdlib AES-128-GCM, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `quic_long_header_decode` (`internal/quic`) with an optional `original_dcid` param; registry unchanged. **QUIC long-header forensics is now complete: decode (all 5 packet types) + Initial decryption + JA4/JA4S-q fingerprinting + Retry authentication.**
- `quic_long_header_decode` JA4 QUIC fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.527.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4 QUIC fingerprint** (FoxIO, protocol prefix `q`) on top of last fire's Initial decryption, **completing the JA4+ family across the QUIC/HTTP3 transport**. Now that v0.526 decrypts the QUIC Initial ‚Üí ClientHello/ServerHello, the JA4 is computed over the recovered handshake and surfaced as `decrypted.ja4` ‚Äî JA4 for a client Initial, JA4S for a server Initial. Per the FoxIO spec the QUIC JA4 is **identical to the TLS-over-TCP JA4 bar the leading protocol character** (`q` not `t`), so `internal/tlsdecode`'s `computeJA4` / `computeJA4S` were parameterised on the protocol prefix (the existing TLS path still passes `t`, anchors unchanged) and a new exported `tlsdecode.QUICHandshakeJA4` parses the bare CRYPTO-stream handshake message (no TLS record envelope, RFC 9001 ¬ß4.1) and computes the `q` fingerprint, which `internal/quic` calls only for a complete contiguous handshake (a partial ClientHello would fingerprint wrong ‚Üí surface nothing, no confidently-wrong output). **Verified end-to-end against FoxIO's own QUIC pcap**: extracted the QUIC Initial from `pcap/quic-tls-handshake.pcapng`, decrypted it with our v0.526 code, reassembled the Chrome ClientHello, and reproduced FoxIO's published snapshot JA4 `q13d0310h3_55b375c5d22e_cd85d2d88918` byte-for-byte (the full pcap‚Üídecrypt‚ÜíClientHello‚ÜíJA4 chain, the real-world dog-food of the decryptor); the JA4S `q` variant is anchored to the same snapshot's `q130200_1301_234ea6891581` (the `q`-prefix of the already-verified TCP `t130200_1301_234ea6891581`). Native ‚Äî extends the existing JA4 machinery + the v0.526 decryptor, stdlib + already-present `golang.org/x/crypto/hkdf`, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `quic_long_header_decode` (`internal/quic` ‚Üí `internal/tlsdecode`); registry unchanged. The JA4+ family now spans every layer **and** both transports: TCP (JA4T) / TLS (JA4/JA4S) / HTTP (JA4H) / cert (JA4X) over TCP, plus JA4/JA4S over QUIC.
- `quic_long_header_decode` Initial decryption ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.526.0 ‚Äî **decrypts the QUIC v1 Initial packet** ‚Äî the one long-header packet whose protection keys are *public* (HKDF-derived from the clear-text Destination Connection ID + a fixed per-version salt, RFC 9001 ¬ß5.2, with no TLS-handshake secret), so it is fully decryptable offline from the packet bytes alone. The package previously surfaced the Initial payload as protected hex and explicitly deferred decryption; now `internal/quic` derives the client/server Initial keys (HKDF-Extract + HKDF-Expand-Label), removes header protection (AES-128-ECB over the 16-byte sample ‚Üí mask ‚Üí unprotect the first byte's low nibble + the 1-4 packet-number bytes), runs AES-128-GCM (nonce = iv XOR padded packet number, AAD = the unprotected header), then dissects the cleartext frames (PADDING run-collapsed / PING / ACK+ACK-ECN parsed-to-skip / CRYPTO / CONNECTION_CLOSE) and **reassembles the CRYPTO stream into the TLS ClientHello / ServerHello** ‚Äî the bytes QUIC otherwise hides, ready to paste into `tls_handshake_decode` for the full JA4 / ALPN / SNI view. `Decode` tries the client role then the server role automatically. **Verified byte-for-byte against the RFC 9001 Appendix A.2 worked example**: the full 1200-byte protected client Initial (DCID `8394c8f03e515708`) reproduces every documented intermediate ‚Äî key `1f369613‚Ä¶`, iv `fa044b2f‚Ä¶`, hp `9f50449e‚Ä¶`, sample `d1b1c98d‚Ä¶`, mask `437b9aec36`, unprotected first byte `c3`, AAD `c300‚Ä¶0002`, nonce `fa04‚Ä¶255e` ‚Äî and decrypts to the documented CRYPTO frame (offset 0, length 241) carrying the ClientHello, followed by 917 padding-zero bytes. Wrong-role decryption fails GCM authentication (integrity holds). Only QUIC v1 is decrypted ‚Äî v2 / drafts use a different salt + `quicv2 ` key labels with no published vector to anchor, so they're held rather than risk a wrong decode. Native ‚Äî stdlib AES/GCM + `golang.org/x/crypto/hkdf` (already a dependency); no new runtime dep, no shell-out. Fuzz-clean (4.4M execs, no panic). No new tool ‚Äî extends `quic_long_header_decode` (`internal/quic`); registry unchanged.
- `geneve_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.479.0 ‚Äî **completes the tunnel-decap sweep** (GRE ‚Üí GTP-U ‚Üí VXLAN ‚Üí Geneve). Geneve (RFC 8926; VMware NSX-T / OVN / Antrea overlays, UDP 6081) is the richest case: its protocol-type field gives both forms ‚Äî 0x6558 (Transparent Ethernet Bridging) wraps an inner Ethernet frame (decoded like VXLAN: when its EtherType is IP, the L3 packet is decoded via `internal/ipdecode`), while 0x0800 / 0x86DD wrap an IP packet directly (decoded like GRE). Either way the encapsulated flow's addresses / protocol / ports surface in place. Non-IP forms (MPLS / NSH, or non-IP inner EtherTypes like 802.1Q) are left as hex; an IP-typed payload that fails to parse ‚Üí `inner_decode_error` + raw hex. Verified with direct-IPv4/IPv6 + TEB-inner-IPv4 + non-IP + garbage cases; added a geneve fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through both inner‚Üíipdecode paths. No new tool ‚Äî extends `geneve_decode` (`internal/geneve` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`). **Tunnel-decap family now complete.**
- `vxlan_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.478.0 ‚Äî third of the tunnel-decap sweep, and the first **inner-Ethernet** case: a VXLAN packet (overlay networks / cloud / Kubernetes CNI / NSX, UDP 4789) encapsulates an Ethernet frame, and when its EtherType is IPv4 (0x0800) / IPv6 (0x86DD) the inner L3 packet is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode` (the decoder already parsed the inner Ethernet header ‚Äî dst/src MAC + EtherType ‚Äî so the L3 bytes start at the known payload offset), surfacing the overlaid flow's addresses / protocol / ports. Non-IP inner frames (ARP, 802.1Q, MPLS, ‚Ä¶) are left for their own decoders; an IP-typed inner frame that fails to parse is reported with `inner_decode_error` + raw hex preserved. Verified with inner IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP + ARP-not-decoded + garbage cases; added a vxlan fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through the inner‚Üíipdecode path. No new tool ‚Äî extends `vxlan_decode` (`internal/vxlan` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`). (Geneve is the last sibling; its inner is also Ethernet.)
- `gtp_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.477.0 ‚Äî second of the tunnel-decap sweep: a GTP-U **G-PDU** (message type 0xFF ‚Äî the 4G/5G mobile-core user-plane tunnel) carries the subscriber's IP packet directly, now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode` (the version nibble is self-describing ‚Äî GTP-U has no protocol-type field), surfacing the tunnelled flow's addresses / protocol / ports. Gated on message type 0xFF (Echo / Error-Indication / End-Marker etc. carry no IP payload and are left alone); a G-PDU payload that fails to parse as IP is reported with `inner_decode_error` + raw hex preserved. Verified with inner IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP vectors + non-G-PDU + garbage cases; fuzz-clean through the inner‚Üíipdecode path (existing gtp harness). No new tool ‚Äî extends `gtp_decode` (`internal/gtp` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`). (Geneve / VXLAN remain ‚Äî their inner is Ethernet, needing an L2 strip first.)
- `gre_decode` inner-IP decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.476.0 ‚Äî extended the chain-to-existing-decoder seam to **tunnel decapsulation**: a GRE packet (PPTP / VPN / MPLS-over-GRE ‚Äî IP protocol 47) encapsulates an inner packet, and when the GRE protocol-type field marks it IPv4 (0x0800) or IPv6 (0x86DD) the inner packet is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode`, surfacing the tunnelled flow's source/dest addresses, protocol and ports directly in the GRE decode. Non-IP payload kinds (Transparent Ethernet 0x6558, ARP, MPLS, ‚Ä¶) are left as hex (no confidently-wrong output), and an IP-typed payload that fails to parse is reported with `inner_decode_error` + raw hex preserved. Verified with inner IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP vectors (inner addresses + ports asserted) + non-IP-not-decoded + IP-typed-garbage cases; added a gre fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through the inner‚Üíipdecode path. The first of the tunnel family (GTP-U / Geneve / VXLAN are the natural follow-on sweep). No new tool ‚Äî extends `gre_decode` (`internal/gre` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`).
- `icmp_packet_decode` embedded-packet decode ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.475.0 ‚Äî continued the chain-to-existing-decoder seam: an ICMP **error** message (Destination Unreachable / Time Exceeded / Parameter Problem / Redirect / Packet-Too-Big) quotes the original IP packet that triggered it (the IP header + ‚â•8 bytes of payload), and that quote was previously surfaced as raw hex "to feed into `ip_packet_decode`". It is now **decoded in place** via `internal/ipdecode`, so the offending flow's source/dest addresses, protocol and (for UDP, or a long-enough TCP quote) ports appear directly in the ICMP decode. Also added v6 Destination Unreachable (type 1) / Time Exceeded (type 3) ‚Äî previously raw-hex ‚Äî routing their embedded IPv6 packet through the same path. No confidently-wrong output: a quote that doesn't parse as IP is reported with `embedded_decode_error` and the raw hex preserved (truncated TCP quotes degrade gracefully ‚Äî IP layer + ports as available). Verified with embedded IPv4/UDP + IPv6/UDP vectors (inner addresses + ports asserted) + a garbage-quote fallback; added an icmp fuzz harness, fuzz-clean through the embedded‚Üíipdecode path. No new tool ‚Äî extends `icmp_packet_decode` (`internal/icmp` ‚Üí `internal/ipdecode`).
- `dtls_decode` Certificate body ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.474.0 ‚Äî sibling-swept the v0.473 TLS Certificate decode into **DTLS**: the DTLS Certificate handshake message (msg_type 11) body uses the same TLS 1.2 layout, so each DER cert is chained through `internal/x509decode` (subject / issuer / validity / SAN / fingerprints / CA). Gated on the DTLS handshake message being **unfragmented** (the existing dispatch already returns early on a fragment, so a partial cert is never mis-decoded); mismatched list-length ‚Üí note; unparseable DER ‚Üí raw + `decode_error`. Self-verified with `crypto/x509`-generated certs (single + chain) wrapped in a DTLS 1.2 Certificate record; added a DTLS fuzz harness (cert‚Üíx509 seed), fuzz-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `dtls_decode` (`internal/dtls` ‚Üí `internal/x509decode`).
- `ip_packet_decode` JA4T fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.525.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4T TCP-SYN fingerprint** (FoxIO) to `ip_packet_decode` ‚Äî a **passive OS / TCP-stack fingerprint**, the modern p0f analogue and a genuinely distinct capability class from the TLS/HTTP/cert JA4 members. From a SYN it emits `window_size_option-kinds_MSS_window-scale` (e.g. `65535_2-1-3-1-1-8-4-0-0_1460_6`): the TCP window size, the exact wire sequence of TCP option *kinds* (every NOP and EOL/padding byte included, in order), the MSS, and the window scale. **No hashes ‚Äî pure structural extraction**, so there's no confidently-wrong hash risk; the only subtlety was that the display option-list stops at the first EOL while JA4T counts every trailing padding byte, so JA4T gets its own option walk. Computed only for SYN packets (the options are negotiated at setup). **Verified byte-for-byte against the FoxIO `macos_tcp_flags` snapshot** by extracting the actual SYN's IP packet from FoxIO's pcap and confirming the parse reproduces `65535_2-1-3-1-1-8-4-0-0_1460_6` exactly (both trailing zeros included). Native ‚Äî extends the existing TCP-header+options decode, stdlib only, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `ip_packet_decode` (`internal/ipdecode`); registry unchanged. The full JA4+ family is now JA4 / JA4S / JA4X / JA4H / JA4T ‚Äî five members, all byte-for-byte verified, fingerprinting the TCP, TLS, HTTP, and certificate layers.
- `http_message_decode` JA4H fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.524.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4H HTTP-client fingerprint** (FoxIO), **completing the entire JA4+ family**: JA4 (client TLS, v0.521) + JA4S (server TLS, v0.522) + JA4X (cert, v0.523) + JA4H (HTTP, this) now fingerprint every layer a connection touches. JA4H identifies the HTTP client stack (browser / library / bot / malware) and is computed for requests in `internal/httpmsg`: `method + version + cookie/referer flags + header-count + Accept-Language` `_` `hash12(header names)` `_` `hash12(cookie names)` `_` `hash12(cookie name=value)` ‚Äî header names hashed in **wire case + order** (a client signal, not lower-cased), Cookie/Referer/pseudo-headers excluded from the count and the header hash, cookies sorted by name. JA4H had been **HELD three fires running** as "needs tshark" ‚Äî this fire I cracked it by reading the full `ja4h.py` reference algorithm, then **extracting the actual HTTP requests as plaintext directly from FoxIO's own test pcaps** (`http-empty-useragent.pcap`, `http1-with-cookies.pcapng`) and anchoring byte-for-byte against the snapshot outputs: a 1-header GET ‚Üí `ge10nn010000_b8bcd45ac095_‚Ä¶` (which revealed the rule I'd been getting wrong ‚Äî header names are hashed in **original case**: `sha256("User-Agent")` = `b8bcd45ac095`, not `sha256("user-agent")`), and a curl GET with Referer + 2 cookies + `Accept-Language: da` ‚Üí `ge11cr04da00_8ddaef5d77af_280f366eaa04_c2fb0fe53442` (all three sub-hashes reproduced exactly, anchoring the cookie-name-sort + name=value + language transform). Native ‚Äî `crypto/sha256` + field assembly over the already-parsed request, stdlib only, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `http_message_decode` (`internal/httpmsg`); registry unchanged. **The JA4+ family is now complete and every member is byte-for-byte verified.**
- `x509_certificate_decode` JA4X fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.523.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4X X.509-certificate fingerprint** (FoxIO), completing the **verifiable JA4+ family** alongside JA4 (client, v0.521) and JA4S (server, v0.522): JA4 ‚Üí JA4S ‚Üí JA4X fingerprint the client stack, the server stack, and the **certificate-generation stack** respectively ‚Äî and malware C2 / phishing infrastructure reuses cert-generation patterns across deployments, making JA4X a real threat-intel pivot. JA4X = `hash12(issuer RDN OIDs)_hash12(subject RDN OIDs)_hash12(extension OIDs)`, each the comma-joined hex of the OID DER content-octets **in certificate order** (not sorted). Computed in `internal/x509decode` from the already-parsed cert, so it surfaces in both `x509_certificate_decode` and every cert in a `tls_handshake_decode` chain. **Verified by the same reverse-engineering approach that cracked JA4S**: three recurring RDN hashes from the FoxIO browsers-x509 snapshot were reproduced byte-for-byte ‚Äî `hash12("550406,55040a,550403")` = `a373a9f83c6b` (C,O,CN), C,O,OU,CN = `7d5dbb3783b4`, C,ST,L,O,CN = `2bab15409345` ‚Äî plus an end-to-end anchor (a generated C,O,CN self-signed cert with SKI/AKI/BasicConstraints decodes to `a373a9f83c6b_a373a9f83c6b_795797892f9c`). Cross-confirmed against the FoxIO rust reference (`ja4x/src/lib.rs`: OIDs as `hex(attr_type().as_bytes())`, joined, not sorted). Native ‚Äî `crypto/x509` ordered RDN/extension OIDs + `encoding/asn1` OID marshaling + SHA-256, stdlib only, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `x509_certificate_decode` (`internal/x509decode`); registry unchanged. Only JA4H (HTTP) now remains deferred (no inline vectors; needs tshark).
- `tls_handshake_decode` JA4S fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.522.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4S TLS *server* fingerprint** (FoxIO), the server-side counterpart to v0.521's JA4 client fingerprint ‚Äî together they fingerprint **both ends** of a TLS session (client-stack + server-stack / C2 identification). Computed from the ServerHello (which `tls_handshake_decode` already decodes): JA4S = `protocol(t) + TLS-version + 2-digit server-extension-count + chosen-ALPN` `_` `negotiated-cipher(4-hex)` `_` `SHA256(server extensions in WIRE ORDER)[:12]`. **The crucial difference from JA4: the server extensions are NOT sorted** ‚Äî the server's extension order is itself the fingerprint signal. I'd HELD on JA4S two fires earlier (FoxIO publishes no inline worked example), then **cracked the verification by reverse-engineering it against two real FoxIO snapshot outputs**: the same two TLS-1.3 ServerHello extensions (key_share 0x0033 + supported_versions 0x002b) appear in **opposite order** for two server stacks ‚Äî `SHA256("0033,002b")[:12]` = `234ea6891581` (Google ‚Üí `t130200_1301_234ea6891581`) and `SHA256("002b,0033")[:12]` = `a56c5b993250` (LastPass ‚Üí `t130200_1302_a56c5b993250`) ‚Äî which both reproduce exactly *and* prove the wire-order rule. Cross-confirmed against the FoxIO rust reference source (`tls.rs`: "preserving the original order of server's TLS extensions"). An end-to-end ServerHello decode caught a real bug ‚Äî the server's `supported_versions` extension is a bare 2-byte version (not the client's length-prefixed list), so the JA4S version is now driven from the parsed negotiated version. Native ‚Äî SHA-256 + field assembly over the already-parsed ServerHello, stdlib only, no new dep. No new tool ‚Äî extends `tls_handshake_decode` (`internal/tlsdecode`); registry unchanged. JA4H / JA4X remain deferred (no inline vectors; need tshark).
- `tls_handshake_decode` JA4 fingerprint ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.521.0 ‚Äî added the **JA4 TLS client fingerprint** (FoxIO LLC), the modern successor to the JA3 the decoder already computed and increasingly the preferred client / C2 / malware fingerprint for threat-intel (JA3 is being retired in its favour). It was explicitly listed as deferred in the package doc; now implemented from the already-parsed ClientHello. JA4 = `protocol + TLS-version + SNI-flag + non-GREASE-cipher-count + non-GREASE-extension-count + first-ALPN` `_` `SHA256(sorted ciphers)[:12]` `_` `SHA256(sorted extensions, SNI+ALPN removed, + signature_algorithms in order)[:12]`, with GREASE ignored throughout. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the FoxIO worked example** `t13d1516h2_8daaf6152771_e5627efa2ab1` ‚Äî both truncated SHA-256 hashes reproduce the spec's exact pre-hash strings, the GREASE-exclusion is unit-tested, and an end-to-end real-ClientHello decode yields a well-formed `t13d‚Ä¶h2_‚Ä¶_‚Ä¶`. Raw `signature_algorithms` and `supported_versions` code points are now captured (alongside their existing name forms) to feed JA4_c and the JA4 version. Only the TLS-over-TCP client JA4 is computed; JA4S/JA4H/JA4X and the QUIC/DTLS variants remain deferred. No new tool ‚Äî extends `tls_handshake_decode` (`internal/tlsdecode`); registry unchanged.
- `tls_handshake_decode` Certificate body ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.473.0 decoded the TLS **Certificate handshake message** (previously labelled-but-deferred): the TLS 1.2 (and earlier) certificate_list is walked and each DER certificate is chained through `internal/x509decode`, so a captured handshake now yields the server's full cert chain ‚Äî subject / issuer / validity / SAN / fingerprints / CA flag ‚Äî in one decode (the network-pentest analogue of the NDEF‚ÜíWSC/BT-OOB carrier wirings). In TLS 1.3 the Certificate message is encrypted (post-key-exchange), so the plaintext form in a passive capture is the pre-1.3 layout decoded here; a body that doesn't match it is reported with a note, never mis-parsed; a cert whose DER fails to parse is surfaced raw with a `decode_error` rather than a confident decode. Self-verified by wrapping `crypto/x509`-generated certs (single + chain) in a Certificate record and asserting the chained x509 fields, plus malformed-list-length / garbage-DER cases; fuzz-clean (5M execs through the cert‚Üíx509 path, 0 panics). No new tool ‚Äî extends `tls_handshake_decode` (`internal/tlsdecode` ‚Üí `internal/x509decode`).
- `epc_decode` SGTIN-198 ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.472.0 extended `epc_decode` with **SGTIN-198** (header 0x36), the 198-bit SGTIN whose serial is a variable-length **alphanumeric** 7-bit-ASCII string (up to 20 chars) rather than a numeric value ‚Äî used where the GS1 serial isn't purely numeric (e.g. pharmaceutical serialisation), and previously reported "unsupported". `Decode` now dispatches by length: 12 bytes ‚Üí the 96-bit schemes, 25/26 bytes ‚Üí SGTIN-198 (the word-aligned form a RAIN reader emits; the 140-bit serial is twenty null-padded 7-bit chars). Company prefix / item reference / GTIN-14 reconstruction are shared with SGTIN-96; only the serial decode differs. Anchored byte-for-byte against the epc-encoding-utils oracle ‚Äî `3614257BF7194E60C286C5933‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `sgtin-198:0.0614141.812345.ABC123` and `‚Ä¶6C59B4B5C8‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `‚Ä¶812345.XYZ-9`. The other 198-bit variants (GRAI-170 / GIAI-202 / SGLN-195) remain reported-unsupported. No new tool. Fuzz-clean. (`internal/epc`)
- `epc_decode` SGLN-96 / GRAI-96 / GIAI-96 ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.471.0 **completed the 96-bit EPC family** in `epc_decode` by adding the three GS1-keyed schemes deferred at v0.470 (the prior fire HELD on these for lack of an authoritative source): **SGLN-96** (header 0x32, location ‚Äî company prefix + location reference + extension), **GRAI-96** (0x33, returnable asset ‚Äî company prefix + asset type + serial), and **GIAI-96** (0x34, individual asset ‚Äî company prefix + asset reference). The remaining-source problem was solved with the **venv-oracle technique**: the `epc-encoding-utils` Python library was installed and used as an oracle to extract the authoritative partition tables and generate decoded vectors, anchoring each scheme byte-for-byte ‚Äî `3214257BF460720000000190` ‚Üí `sgln-96:0.0614141.12345.400`, `3314257BF40C0E400000162E` ‚Üí `grai-96:0.0614141.12345.5678`, `3414257BF400000000003039` ‚Üí `giai-96:0.0614141.12345` (+ a 12-digit-prefix GIAI partition-0 vector). Each decodes filter / partition / company prefix / reference fields + the EPC tag and pure-identity URIs, matching the oracle's formatting exactly (per-scheme zero-padding rules). `epc_decode` now covers all six 96-bit schemes (SGTIN/SSCC/SGLN/GRAI/GIAI/GID); 198-bit variants remain reported-unsupported. No new tool. Fuzz-clean. (`internal/epc`)
- `epc_decode` GID-96 ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.470.0 extended `epc_decode` with **GID-96** (EPC header 0x35), the General Identifier ‚Äî the EPC scheme used when no GS1 key (GTIN/SSCC/GLN/‚Ä¶) applies. Three fixed-width fields, no partition table / company prefix / check digit: general manager number (28 bits) + object class (24) + serial number (36), plus the EPC tag / pure-identity URIs. **Verified byte-for-byte against three worked vectors** ‚Äî `3500079FF00000B00000000C` ‚Üí `gid-96:31231.11.12`, `3500E82D900000F000000001` ‚Üí `gid-96:951001.15.1`, `350000A2600019003ADE56FA` ‚Üí `gid-96:2598.400.987649786`. Remaining GS1-keyed schemes (SGLN/GRAI/GIAI, which still need their own partition tables) stay identified-not-decoded. No new tool. Fuzz-clean. (`internal/epc`)
- `epc_decode` SSCC-96 ‚Äî ‚úÖ v0.469.0 extended `epc_decode` with **SSCC-96** (EPC header 0x31), the GS1 Serial Shipping Container Code ‚Äî the logistics-unit (case/pallet/container) scheme, the second-most-common EPC after SGTIN. Decodes filter / partition / company prefix / serial reference and reconstructs the **SSCC-18** (extension digit + company prefix + serial-reference remainder + recomputed GS1 mod-10 check digit) plus the EPC tag / pure-identity URIs. The SSCC partition table (distinct from SGTIN's ‚Äî no item reference, wider serial reference) and the SSCC-18 reconstruction are **verified byte-for-byte against the worked vector** `3134257BF4499602D2000000` ‚Üí `urn:epc:tag:sscc-96:1.0614141.1234567890` (company prefix 0614141, serial reference 1234567890, SSCC-18 106141412345678908). The 24 trailing reserved bits are checked (non-zero noted). Remaining 96-bit schemes (SGLN/GRAI/GIAI/GID) still identified-not-decoded. No new tool. Fuzz-clean. (`internal/epc`)
- `epc_decode` (GS1 EPC UHF RAIN RFID ‚Äî SGTIN-96) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.468.0 ‚Äî decodes the GS1 **Electronic Product Code** binary on UHF RAIN RFID (EPC Gen2 / ISO 18000-63) tags ‚Äî retail item-level tagging and supply-chain logistics ‚Äî a **whole RFID band the toolkit did not decode** (it covered HF ISO 14443/15693/NDEF and LF EM4100/HID/FDX-B/T5577, but not UHF EPC). Reading a UHF tag needs a RAIN reader (hardware, out of scope), but the captured 96-bit EPC decodes entirely offline. **SGTIN-96** (header 0x30, the dominant retail scheme) is fully decoded: filter, partition, company prefix, item reference, serial number, the canonical EPC tag URI (`urn:epc:tag:sgtin-96:‚Ä¶`) and pure-identity URI (`urn:epc:id:sgtin:‚Ä¶`), and the reconstructed **GTIN-14** (with a recomputed GS1 mod-10 check digit). The SGTIN-96 layout, the partition table, and the SGTIN‚ÜíGTIN reconstruction are taken from the **GS1 EPC Tag Data Standard** and **verified byte-for-byte against its canonical worked example** ‚Äî `3074257BF7194E4000001A85` ‚Üí `urn:epc:tag:sgtin-96:3.0614141.812345.6789` (company prefix 0614141, item ref 812345, serial 6789, GTIN-14 80614141123458) ‚Äî not recalled. No confidently-wrong output: the other 96-bit schemes (SSCC/SGLN/GRAI/GIAI/GID, 0x31-0x35) are identified by name but not field-decoded (raw + note) rather than guessed; unknown headers and 198-bit variants are reported unsupported. Verified against the canonical vector + a second GS1 check-digit cross-check + other-scheme/unknown/error cases; fuzz-clean (3.4M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî fixed bit-field extraction + GS1 mod-10, stdlib only (`internal/epc`).
- `nfc_t2t_tlv_decode` (NFC Type 2 Tag data-area TLV walker) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.467.0 ‚Äî walks the TLV blocks in a Type 2 Tag's **data area** (user memory from page 4 onward) and **decodes the NDEF message in place**, bridging a raw tag-memory dump to `ndef_decode`: a Type 2 Tag (NTAG / MIFARE Ultralight) stores its NDEF inside a TLV structure (NULL 0x00 / Lock Control 0x01 / Memory Control 0x02 / NDEF 0x03 / Proprietary 0xFD / Terminator 0xFE), and this locates and decodes it. The data-area complement to `nfc_t2t` (which decodes the page 0-3 header: UID/BCC/lock/CC) ‚Äî previously an operator had to manually extract the NDEF bytes from a dump to feed `ndef_decode`. Each block is reported with type/offset/length/raw value; the NDEF TLV value is handed to the shared NDEF walker (URI/Text/Smart Poster/handover/MIME). The 1-or-3-byte length form (0xFF big-endian escape) is handled and the Terminator ends the walk. The TLV type values + length encoding are from the **NFC Forum Type 2 Tag Operation Specification** (cross-checked vs the Nordic nrfxlib T2T docs). No confidently-wrong output: a TLV whose declared length overruns the buffer is reported as truncated, and the Lock/Memory Control reserved-area descriptors are surfaced raw rather than guessed. Verified against a full Lock+NDEF+Terminator data area (NDEF Text record decoded in place) + NULL-skip / 3-byte-length / unknown-type / truncated / no-terminator / error cases; fuzz-clean (3.8M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî TLV framing over the shared NDEF walker (`internal/t2t`).
- `ntag_config_decode` (NTAG213/215/216 configuration-page decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.466.0 ‚Äî decodes the NTAG21x **configuration pages**, the registers controlling an NFC Type-2 tag's password protection, lock state, NFC counter, and UID/counter ASCII-mirror ‚Äî answering an operator's first questions about a dumped tag: is it password-protected, **read+write or write-only (PROT)**, is the config **permanently locked (CFGLCK)**, how many failed password attempts are allowed (**AUTHLIM**), is the NFC read counter enabled. The protection-state complement to `ndef_decode` / `nfc_t2t` (which decode the tag's *data*, not its access registers). Decodes **AUTH0** (first protected page), the **ACCESS** byte (PROT/CFGLCK/NFC_CNT_EN/NFC_CNT_PWD_PROT/AUTHLIM), and the **MIRROR** byte (MIRROR_CONF UID/counter mirror, MIRROR_BYTE/PAGE, strong-modulation) from CFG0+CFG1 (8 bytes; 16 bytes adds PWD+PACK). The config pages live at different addresses per variant (29h/83h/E3h) but the layout is identical, so it decodes the page bytes regardless of origin. The page layout (Table 8), MIRROR byte (Table 9), ACCESS byte (Table 10), and every field value meaning (Table 11) were **extracted and verified byte-for-byte from the NXP NTAG213/215/216 data sheet rev 3.2 ¬ß8.5.7** (read directly from the PDF ‚Äî not recalled). No confidently-wrong output: an undocumented MIRROR_CONF value (0b11) is surfaced as reserved; AUTH0=0xFF (protection disabled) is noted rather than asserted against an unknown memory size. Verified against factory-default / read+write-protected / CFGLCK+mirror / NFC-counter / PWD+PACK / error cases; fuzz-clean (4.8M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî fixed bit-field extraction, stdlib only (`internal/ntag`).
- `t5577_config_encode` (T5577 / ATA5577 configuration-word build) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.623.0 ‚Äî the inverse of `t5577_config_decode` (v0.465): builds the 32-bit T5577 block-0 config word from its raw fields (modulation / data bit rate / max block + optional master key / PSK clock / AOR / PWD / ST). **Completes the offline clone-prep chain**: read a credential ‚Üí generate the clone data block (the LF `*_encode` tools) ‚Üí generate the config word that sets a T5577 blank up for the right protocol before the data blocks are written. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bit layout is the same Proxmark3-verified one `t5577_config_decode` uses, and the encoder **round-trips** with it (decoding the emitted word reproduces the fields) and reproduces the two reference configs (EM4100 ‚Üí `00148040`, HID Prox ‚Üí `00107060`); the PSK clock bits are only written for the PSK modulations (1-3), matching the decoder; out-of-range fields are rejected. Generation only ‚Äî transmits nothing and writes to no device, so it stays Low like the decoder. Verified by the two reference-config reproductions and a decode‚àòencode round-trip across modulation/flag combinations; native ‚Äî fixed bit-field placement, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/t55xx`). Registry 614‚Üí615.
- `t5577_config_decode` (T5577 / ATA5577 configuration-register decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.465.0 ‚Äî decodes the **T5577 block-0 configuration register**, the 32-bit word that controls how an LF 125 kHz tag modulates/clocks its data. The T5577 is the ubiquitous rewritable LF blank used to clone EM4100 / HID Prox / Indala / AWID; decoding its config block surfaces the **modulation** (Direct / FSK1/2/1a/2a / ASK-Manchester / PSK1/2/3 / Biphase / Biphase-a), **data bit rate** (RF/8‚Ä¶RF/128), PSK clock, AOR, **max block**, password-enabled and sequence-terminator flags ‚Äî the diagnostic complement to the project's T5577 clone/write tooling (`rfid_write` / `loader_t5577_multiwriter`, which set these configs but couldn't read them back). The bit layout, bit-rate table, and the modulation value‚Üíname table are taken from the **Proxmark3 reference** (`doc/T5577_Guide.md` + `client cmdlft55xx.c GetModulationStr`) and verified byte-for-byte against **two real config words**: `0x00148040` (EM4100 ‚Üí RF/64, Manchester, 2 blocks) and `0x00107060` (HID Prox ‚Üí RF/50, FSK2a, 3 blocks). (Verification caught a recalled error ‚Äî PSK1 is modulation value 1, not 0x0A.) No confidently-wrong output: a modulation value outside the documented set is surfaced as a numeric code, and extended mode (master key 0x6/0x9, which reinterprets the reserved bits) is flagged rather than mis-decoded. Verified against both vectors + constructed PSK/flags / extended-mode / error cases; fuzz-clean (4.2M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî fixed bit-field extraction, stdlib only (`internal/t55xx`).
- `presco_encode` (Presco block generator) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.620.0 ‚Äî the inverse of `presco_decode` (v0.612), **completing the LF clone-generation set** (`em4100_encode`, `rfid_pacs_encode`, `ioprox_encode`, `jablotron_encode`, `viking_encode`, `noralsy_encode`): builds the 128-bit Presco LF block from a 32-bit full code ‚Äî the 0x10D00000 preamble, two zero words, then the full code (site code = (full>>24)&0xFF, user code = full&0xFFFF). Presco carries no checksum, so the structural frame is the integrity gate. **No confidently-wrong output**: the layout is the same one `presco_decode` uses (from the Proxmark3 `cmdlfpresco.c` encoder/decoder, which are inverse), and this encoder **round-trips** with the decoder (decoding the emitted block reproduces the full code) and reproduces the reference vector (full code 0x07AABBCC ‚Üí `10D00000000000000000000007AABBCC`). Generation only ‚Äî transmits nothing and writes to no device, so it stays Low like the decoder. Verified by the vector match and a decode‚àòencode round-trip across several full codes; native ‚Äî fixed-frame placement, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/presco`). Registry 612‚Üí613.
- `presco_decode` (Presco 125 kHz LF access-control decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.612.0 ‚Äî decodes the **Presco** 128-bit LF data block, the credential format used by Presco readers (gate / garage / building access) ‚Äî continuing the LF reader-cloning recon set alongside `ioprox_decode` / `jablotron_decode` / `viking_decode` / `noralsy_decode`. Recovers the **32-bit full code** and the Proxmark-style **site code** / **user code** derived from it. Input is the *decoded* 128-bit block ‚Äî the bytes a Proxmark3 `lf presco demod` emits, MSB-first; the on-air ASK demodulation is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. Layout: 32-bit 0x10D00000 preamble, two zero words, then the 32-bit full code (bits 96-127); site = (full>>24)&0xFF, user = full&0xFFFF. **No confidently-wrong output**: the layout is taken from the **Proxmark3** client (`cmdlfpresco.c`) ‚Äî both its encoder (`getPrescoBits`) and decoder (`detectPresco`), which are inverse and so internally cross-check. Presco is a **single-reference** format here (the Flipper Zero mainline firmware does not implement it) and carries **no checksum**, so integrity rests on the 96-bit structural gate (preamble 0x10D00000 + two zero words, a ~1-in-2^96 marker) ‚Äî a block that fails the gate is **rejected** rather than mis-decoded; the 32-bit full code is the unambiguous primary value (literally the final word after the gate), with site/user surfaced as the Proxmark derivation. Verified against three vectors constructed from the (confirmed) encode layout and independently checked (full 0x07AABBCC ‚Üí site 7 / user 48076; plus 0x00000001 and 0x12345678), and bad-preamble / non-zero-filler structural rejections; fuzz-clean (~2.9M execs, 0 panics); race-clean. Native ‚Äî a structural gate + a 32-bit field read, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/presco`). Registry 605‚Üí606.
- `noralsy_encode` (Noralsy block generator) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.619.0 ‚Äî the inverse of `noralsy_decode` (v0.611): builds the 96-bit Noralsy LF block from a printed card number and year, completing the LF clone-generation set (`em4100_encode`, `rfid_pacs_encode`, `ioprox_encode`, `jablotron_encode`, `viking_encode`). BCD-encodes the card into the 28-bit packed field (placed non-contiguously per the layout), BCD-encodes the year, writes the 0xBB0214FF preamble, and computes the two 4-bit nibble checksums (chk1 over bits 32-71, chk2 over bits 0-75, the latter including chk1). **No confidently-wrong output**: the layout, the non-contiguous packing, the year field and the two checksums are the same Proxmark3-/Flipper-cross-verified ones `noralsy_decode` uses, and the encoder **round-trips** with it (decoding the emitted block reproduces the card number + year with both checksums valid) and reproduces the reference vector (card 1234567 / year 2021 ‚Üí `BB0214FF1232104567370000`) ‚Äî the strongest verification, no external vector needed. A card beyond 7 BCD digits, or a year outside the round-trippable 1961-2060 window (the decoder's >60 century-heuristic boundary), is rejected rather than emitting a block that re-decodes to a different year. Generation only ‚Äî transmits nothing and writes to no device, so it stays Low like the decoder. Verified by the vector match and a decode‚àòencode round-trip across several card/year pairs incl. the 1999/2060 boundaries; native ‚Äî BCD encode + non-contiguous placement + two nibble checksums, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/noralsy`). Registry 611‚Üí612.
- `noralsy_decode` (Noralsy 125 kHz LF access-control decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.611.0 ‚Äî decodes the **Noralsy** 96-bit LF data block, the credential format used by Noralsy readers/fobs (common in **French / wider-EU** residential access control and intercom systems) ‚Äî continuing the LF reader-cloning recon set alongside `ioprox_decode` / `jablotron_decode` / `viking_decode`, complementing the HID/Indala/AWID PACS coverage. Recovers the **card ID** and **manufacture year** and validates the two nibble **checksums**. Input is the *decoded* 96-bit block ‚Äî the bytes a Proxmark3 `lf noralsy demod` / Flipper Zero LF read emits, MSB-first; the on-air ASK demodulation is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. Layout: 32-bit 0xBB0214FF preamble, a 28-bit card ID packed across bits 32-43/56-63/64-71, an 8-bit BCD year (bits 44-51), and two 4-bit nibble-XOR checksums (chk1 over bits 32-71, chk2 over bits 0-75). **No confidently-wrong output**: the bit layout, the (non-contiguous) card-ID assembly masks, the year field and the two checksums are taken from ‚Äî and **agree byte-for-byte between two independent reference implementations**, the **Proxmark3** client (`cmdlfnoralsy.c` `noralsy_chksum` + the cardid/year assembly) and the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`protocol_noralsy.c`); the 32-bit 0xBB0214FF preamble is a hard structural gate (a ~1-in-4-billion marker) ‚Äî a block without it is **rejected** rather than mis-decoded; the two checksums are surfaced as `chk1_valid`/`chk2_valid` (a frame whose checksums fail is reported, never asserted as a real credential). The references **disagree only on card-ID presentation** (Proxmark BCD-decimal vs Flipper hex), so **both** are surfaced (`card_id_bcd` + `card_id_hex`, with a `card_id_is_bcd` flag) rather than asserting one; and the 19xx/20xx century split is a documented heuristic, noted as such. Verified against three vectors constructed from the spec and independently checked (card 1234567 / year 2021; a year-1999 case; and a non-BCD card flagging `card_id_is_bcd:false`), a checksum-mismatch case and a bad-preamble structural rejection; fuzz-clean (~3.3M execs, 0 panics); race-clean. Native ‚Äî fixed bit extraction + two nibble checksums, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/noralsy`). Registry 604‚Üí605.

- `jablotron_encode` (Jablotron block generator) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.617.0 ‚Äî the inverse of `jablotron_decode` (v0.609): builds the 64-bit Jablotron LF block from a printed card number, extending the LF clone-generation set (`em4100_encode`, `rfid_pacs_encode`, `ioprox_encode`). BCD-encodes the card number into the five card-data bytes (the inverse of the decoder's render), prepends the 0xFFFF preamble and appends the 8-bit checksum (sum of the card bytes XOR 0x3A). **No confidently-wrong output**: the layout + checksum are the same Proxmark3-/Flipper-cross-verified ones `jablotron_decode` uses, and the encoder **round-trips** with it (decoding the emitted block reproduces the card number) and reproduces the reference vector (card 1234567890 ‚Üí `FFFF12345678909E`) ‚Äî the strongest verification, no external vector needed. A card number beyond ten BCD digits is rejected. Generation only ‚Äî transmits nothing and writes to no device, so it stays Low like the decoder. Verified by the vector match and a decode‚àòencode round-trip across several card numbers; native ‚Äî BCD encode + a checksum, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/jablotron`). Registry 609‚Üí610.
- `jablotron_decode` (Jablotron 125 kHz LF access-control decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.609.0 ‚Äî decodes the **Jablotron** 64-bit LF data block, the credential format used by Jablotron readers/fobs (widely deployed across **Czech / Slovak / wider-EU** access control and intercom systems) ‚Äî continuing the LF reader-cloning recon set alongside `ioprox_decode`, complementing `em4100_decode` / `fdxb_decode` and the HID/Indala/AWID PACS coverage. Recovers the **40-bit card data**, renders the **printed card number** (BCD), and validates the **8-bit checksum** (`(sum of the five card bytes mod 256) XOR 0x3A`). Input is the *decoded* 64-bit block ‚Äî the bytes a Proxmark3 `lf jablotron demod` / Flipper Zero LF read emits, MSB-first; the on-air ASK demodulation is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. Layout: 16-bit 0xFFFF preamble, 40-bit card data (bits 16-55), 8-bit checksum (bits 56-63); the printed number reads each card byte as two BCD digits, the five concatenated base-100. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bit layout, the checksum and the BCD render are taken from ‚Äî and **agree byte-for-byte between two independent reference implementations**, the **Proxmark3** client (`cmdlfjablotron.c` `jablontron_chksum` / `getJablontronCardId`) and the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`protocol_jablotron.c`); the 0xFFFF preamble is a hard structural gate ‚Äî a block without it is **rejected** rather than mis-decoded; the checksum is surfaced as `crc_valid` (a structurally-valid block that fails it is reported, never asserted as a real credential); and when the card data is not valid BCD the printed-number field is flagged (`card_id_is_bcd:false`) and the raw 40-bit value is relied upon. Verified against two vectors constructed from the spec and independently checked (card bytes `12 34 56 78 90` ‚Üí printed 1234567890, checksum 0x9E; plus a non-BCD case `00 01 B6 69 01`), a checksum-mismatch case and a missing-preamble structural rejection; fuzz-clean (~3.5M execs, 0 panics); race-clean. Native ‚Äî fixed bit extraction + checksum + BCD render, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/jablotron`). Registry 602‚Üí603.
- `subghz_classify` Magellan protocol ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.631.0 ‚Äî added the **Magellan** 32-bit OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 30 protocols), broadening coverage into **security-system sensors/remotes** (door/motion/smoke/REM events) rather than only garage remotes. Frame: 24-bit data + 8-bit CRC8; the 24-bit data, **bit-reversed**, splits into an 8-bit event code and a 16-bit serial. PWM: bit 1 = te_short mark + te_long space, bit 0 = te_long mark + te_short space (te_short 200¬µs / te_long 400¬µs); a te_long√ó3 start mark anchors the frame after a ~12√óte_short preamble. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding, the CRC-8 (poly 0x31, init 0x00 over the three data bytes) and the reverse-then-split field formula are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/magellan.c` ‚Äî the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder, `magellan_crc8`/`check_crc` and `check_remote_controller`); a frame failing the **CRC-8 gate is rejected**, never surfaced. Verified against the **firmware's own documented example** (0x37AE4828 ‚Üí CRC 0x28, reversed 0x1275EC ‚Üí event 0x12, serial 0x75EC) ‚Äî the CRC port is pinned by that vector independently ‚Äî plus a decode round-trip across a spread of event/serial values and CRC-mismatch / truncated / no-start-bit rejections; race-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` MegaCode protocol ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.629.0 ‚Äî added the **Linear MegaCode** 24-bit fixed-code OOK protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 29 protocols). MegaCode is the Linear/Nortek garage/gate remote format (315 MHz AM). Decodes the 24-bit static code and the **4-bit facility code + 16-bit serial/key + 3-bit button** field split, with the **start bit (MSB) required to be 1** as a structural gate. The on-air encoding is pulse-position within a fixed 6√óTE frame, which collapses to a constant 1√óTE mark separated by an inter-mark space whose width encodes the (prev,cur) bit pair ‚Äî (1,1)=5√óTE, (1,0)=2√óTE, (0,1)=8√óTE, (0,0)=5√óTE; the decoder normalises this by subtracting 3√óTE from the space when the previous bit was 0, then classifies 5√óTE‚Üí1 / 2√óTE‚Üí0, exactly as the firmware does. A leading guard space of 11‚Äì14√óTE precedes the frame; a space ‚â•10√óTE ends it. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings (te=1000¬µs), the space-to-bit normalisation and the facility/serial/button split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/megacode.c` ‚Äî the `feed` decoder state machine, the `get_upload` encoder gap widths, and `check_remote_controller`); the gap table is **cross-checked between two independent firmware functions** (decoder + encoder agree), and a frame whose start bit is not 1 is **rejected**. Verified against the **worked example documented verbatim in the firmware** (remote key 17316 / facility 3 / button 1 ‚Üí 0x9A1D21) plus a decode round-trip across a deterministic spread of facility/serial/button values and structural-rejection cases; race-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` SMC5326 protocol ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.628.0 ‚Äî added the **SMC5326** (PT2262-family tri-state encoder) 25-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 28 protocols). SMC5326 is a standard PT2262-compatible encoder chip in countless cheap remotes / sensors. Decodes the 25-bit code and the **16-bit address** (`code>>9 & 0xFFFF`, eight tri-state DIP positions) per the Flipper reference. Mark-first PWM: bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space (te_short 300¬µs / te_long 900¬µs = 3√óTE); frame preceded by a ~24√óTE inter-frame gap space. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the mark-first PWM encoding and the address split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/smc5326.c` ‚Äî the `get_upload` encoder + the decoder feed loop + `get_string`); the decoder uses `estimateTEMin` (the short/long pulses appear ~equally per bit). Verified by a decode round-trip over four codes built per the firmware's encoder, address cross-checked (code 0x0123456 ‚Üí address 0x091A); race-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Gate TX protocol ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.627.0 ‚Äî added the **Gate TX** (GateTX) 24-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM Sub-GHz protocol to the `subghz_classify` decoder set (now 27 protocols). Gate TX is a common garage/gate remote format. Decodes the 24-bit code and derives the **20-bit serial + 4-bit button** from the bit-reversed key, per the Flipper reference. Frame: a long header space (~47√óTE) + a te_long start-bit mark, then 24 MSB-first PWM bits (bit 0 = short space + long mark, bit 1 = long space + short mark; te_short 350¬µs / te_long 700¬µs). **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM bit encoding and the serial/button reversed-key formula are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/gate_tx.c` ‚Äî the `get_upload` encoder + the `GateTXDecoderStep` state machine + `check_remote_controller`), and the decoder uses `estimateTEMin` (not the naive estimator, which would mis-pick te_long since the short/long pulses appear ~equally per bit). Verified by a decode round-trip over three codes built per the firmware's own encoder, with the serial/button cross-checked against the reversed-key formula (e.g. code 0x123456 ‚Üí serial 295622 / button 10); race-clean. No new tool ‚Äî extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `cyfral_decode` (Cyfral iButton frame) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.626.0 ‚Äî decodes the **Cyfral** iButton contact-key (former-CIS / Eastern-European intercom systems) ‚Äî the second of the two **non-Dallas iButton** formats `ibutton_decode` deferred, **completing the iButton family** (Dallas + Metakom + Cyfral). **Takes the on-wire frame, not the rendered 2-byte ID**: a Cyfral key decodes to 16 bits but that value carries no integrity information (every 16-bit value is structurally valid), so the genuine, gated decode is of the 40-bit on-wire frame ‚Äî a start nibble (0b0001), 8 data nibbles each ‚àà {1110,1101,1011,0111} (carrying 2 bits each: E‚Üí11/D‚Üí10/B‚Üí01/7‚Üí00), a stop nibble (0b0001) ‚Äî validating those constraints (a strong ~(4/16)‚Å∏ gate) and extracting the key. **No confidently-wrong output**: the frame structure + nibble mapping are taken from the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/ibutton/protocols/misc/protocol_cyfral.c`); a frame failing any nibble constraint is **rejected** as not-a-Cyfral-frame rather than mis-decoded; the mapping is hand-checkable (no external vector). Verified against a hand-traced vector (on-wire `1EDB7EDB71` ‚Üí key 0xE4E4), all-0x7/all-0xE extremes, and bad-start / bad-stop / bad-data-nibble / error rejections; fuzz-clean (~3.4M execs, 0 panics). Native ‚Äî a nibble walk + a 4-entry pattern map, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/cyfral`). Registry 616‚Üí617.
- `metakom_decode` (Metakom iButton key) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.625.0 ‚Äî decodes the **Metakom** 4-byte (32-bit) contact-key format used by Metakom intercom systems (common across the former-CIS / Eastern-European residential market) ‚Äî one of the two **non-Dallas iButton** formats `ibutton_decode` (Dallas 1-Wire) explicitly deferred (the other is Cyfral). Input is the decoded 4-byte key (the Flipper 'ID' value), MSB-first; the on-wire sync / 0b010 start-stop framing is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. **No confidently-wrong output**: the key width, byte order and validity rule ‚Äî every data byte must have an **even** number of 1 bits ‚Äî are taken from the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/ibutton/protocols/misc/protocol_metakom.c` `metakom_parity_check`), and the rule is hand-checkable by bit-counting (no external vector needed). Metakom carries no stronger structural marker, so the per-byte even parity is the **only** integrity gate (a comparatively weak ~1-in-16 gate) ‚Äî a key that fails it is reported as parity-invalid rather than asserted as genuine, and the raw bytes are always surfaced. Verified against even-parity-valid (`030F33C3`), odd-parity-invalid (`010F33C3`), all-zero, and error cases; fuzz-clean (~2.5M execs, 0 panics). - `ioprox_decode` (IO Prox / Kantech XSF 125 kHz LF access-control decode) ‚Äî ‚úÖ shipped v0.608.0 ‚Äî decodes the **IO Prox (Kantech XSF)** 64-bit LF data block, the credential format used by **Kantech ioProx** readers (widely deployed across North American commercial / institutional access control) ‚Äî closing the **LF reader-cloning recon gap** left by the HID Prox / Indala / AWID PACS coverage, and complementing `em4100_decode` / `fdxb_decode`. Input is the *decoded* 64-bit block ‚Äî the 'Raw' bytes a Proxmark3 `lf io demod` / Flipper Zero LF read emits, MSB-first; the on-air FSK demodulation is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bit layout (nine zero preamble bits ‚Üí 0xF0 marker ‚Üí FC ‚Üí version ‚Üí card-hi ‚Üí card-lo ‚Üí checksum, each separated by a framing `1` bit) and the checksum algorithm are taken from ‚Äî and **agree byte-for-byte between two independent reference implementations**, the **Proxmark3** client (`cmdlfio.c`) and the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/lfrfid/protocols/protocol_io_prox_xsf.c`); the structural frame (preamble + 0xF0 marker + the six separator bits) is a hard gate ‚Äî a block whose marker or separators don't match is **rejected** as not-an-ioProx-frame rather than mis-decoded, and the checksum is surfaced as `crc_valid` ‚Äî a structurally-valid block that fails the checksum is reported as such, never asserted as a real credential.
